2001 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gallagher


Docket No. 22006


Court of Appeals of Michigan


68 Mich. App. 63; 241 N.W.2d 759; 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 678


January 14, 1976, Submitted  
March 23, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Appeal granted by People v. Gallagher, 399 Mich. 827, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 253 (1977)
Modified by People v. Gallagher, 404 Mich. 429, 273 N.W.2d 440, 1979 Mich. LEXIS 419 (1979)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, George Wicklund, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of a Wayne County trial court (Michigan), which convicted him after a jury found him guilty of the offense of receiving and concealing stolen property, a violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.535.


OVERVIEW: Police officers stopped defendant while he was towing a late model Cadillac. The Cadillac attracted the officers' attention because, although it appeared to be in good condition, most of its exterior sheet metal had been removed. After stopping defendant, the officers observed that the vehicle identification number had been removed from the dash assembly. Defendant was arrested and charged with receiving and concealing stolen property after he was unable to produce proof of ownership or a bill of sale. At trial, the State presented evidence that showed that the car was stolen and that defendant was in the business of salvaging and rebuilding automobiles. He was convicted and appealed. The court affirmed the judgment. The presumption contained in Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.535 did not unconstitutionally force defendant to give up his right to remain silent. It did no more than to make possession of the car prima facie evidence of guilt. Defendant was free to testify or not as he chose. The constraint upon him to give testimony arose from the force of circumstances and not from any form of compulsion forbidden by the Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

2002 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Gerzeski v. State


Docket Nos. 22209, 22210


Court of Appeals of Michigan


68 Mich. App. 91; 241 N.W.2d 771; 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 681


December 10, 1975, Submitted  
March 23, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 397 Mich 832.
Appeal granted by Stanton v. Lloyd Hammond Produce Farms, 397 Mich. 820, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 681 (1976)
Appeal granted by Gerzeski v. Dep't of State Hwys, 397 Mich. 832, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 897 (1976)
Affirmed by Gerzeski v. State, 403 Mich. 149, 268 N.W.2d 525, 1978 Mich. LEXIS 332 (1978)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Court of Claims, Ross W. Campbell, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for entry of judgment for defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, state highway department and others, appealed the judgment of the Court of Claims (Michigan), in favor of plaintiffs, decedents' estates, for wrongful death damages caused by defendants' nuisance. Defendants argued that the trial court erred in denying their motion for summary judgment based on governmental immunity.


OVERVIEW: Defendants removed dirt from a tract of land in order to build a highway. The excavation resulted in a pit that filled with water and the water froze. Two boys fell through the ice and drowned, and the father of one of the boys drowned trying to save them. The decedents' estates filed actions against defendants. The trial court denied defendants' motion for summary judgment based on governmental immunity, and it awarded the decedents' estates damages after finding that the pit was a nuisance in fact. Defendants appealed, and the court reversed. The court held that the immunity authorized by Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1407 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 3.996(107)) was dispositive and required reversal. The condition of the pit was created by want of care and such negligence was not a public nuisance. A public nuisance was one that would be a nuisance at all times and under any circumstances. Accordingly, defendants' ordinary negligence was not an exception to governmental immunity because it did not amount to an unconstitutional taking of private property without just compensation under Mich. Const. art. 10, § 2 (1963).


OUTCOME: In the wrongful death action based on nuisance brought by the decedents' estates, the court reversed the trial court's denial of defendants' motion for summary judgment, holding that defendants were statutorily immune from ordinary negligence liability.

 

2003 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Imerman Screw Products Co. v. Hamtramck


Docket No. 24859


Court of Appeals of Michigan


67 Mich. App. 727; 242 N.W.2d 505; 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 1291


February 12, 1976, Submitted  
March 9, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Tax Tribunal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation appealed a judgment from the Michigan Tax Tribunal that granted defendant City of Hamtrack's motion to dismiss the corporation's action for a refund of taxes or to redetermine an assessment of the taxes, on the ground that § 35 of the Tax Tribunal Act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 205.735, required exhaustion of administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: The corporation disagreed with the assessment of personal property taxes on imported, unopened steel, and rather than seek review in the local board of review, filed this action. In affirming the dismissal of the corporation's claim, the court agreed that § 35 established review by the local board of review as a condition precedent to the acquisition of jurisdiction by the Michigan Tax Tribunal. The court held that it did not matter whether the corporation called its claim one for a refund of taxes or for a redetermination of the assessment, the corporation still was required to present its claim before the local board of review first before it could seek other review. The court further held that even assuming the tax was repugnant to U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, cl. 2, that constitutional provision was not self-executing, so the tax was not void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for the city in the corporation's action for a refund of taxes or redetermination of assessment.

 

2004 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Small


Docket No. 19891


Court of Appeals of Michigan


67 Mich. App. 580; 242 N.W.2d 442; 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 1272


April 10, 1975, Submitted  
March 8, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Washtenaw, Edward D. Deake, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the trial court (Michigan) that convicted him of possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 335.341(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: Following a police investigation that took place over a period of three and a half months, defendant was arrested and 33,600 tablets of LSD were seized from the trunk of his car. Defendant was convicted by a jury of possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance; he was sentenced to from two to seven years in prison. In affirming the conviction, the court held that the police had probable cause to arrest defendant; therefore the search of his trunk was a lawful search incident to the arrest. The court noted that as part of its ongoing investigation, the police had made numerous drug purchases from a woman who obtained her drug supply from defendant. The police made extensive efforts to identify the supplier and arrested defendant as he exited a grocery store with the woman at a time when the woman had arranged to purchase LSD from her supplier.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

2005 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Novi v. State, Dep't of Treasury, State Boundary Com.


Docket Nos. 20227, 20228, 20268, 20410


Court of Appeals of Michigan


67 Mich. App. 596; 242 N.W.2d 449; 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 1273


December 8, 1975, Submitted  
March 8, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 397 Mich   .
Appeal granted by Novi Twp. v. State Boundary Comm'n, 397 Mich. 810, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 715 (1976)
Leave to appeal granted by Novi Twp. v. State Boundary Comm'n, 397 Mich. 846, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 784 (1976)
Reversed by Midland v. Michigan State Boundary Com., 401 Mich. 641, 259 N.W.2d 326, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 123 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from Ingham, Jack W. Warren, J., and Donald L. Reisig, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Michigan State Boundary Commission (SBC) appealed from the judgments of trial courts (Michigan) that determined that its orders approving two annexation petitions were void.


OVERVIEW: Two cities filed petitions with the SBC for annexation of lands lying within plaintiff townships. The SBC approved the petitions and issued orders accordingly. The townships filed actions in the trial courts seeking to have the SBC orders declared void because the legislation conferring annexation jurisdiction upon the SBC was unconstitutional. The trial courts entered judgments in favor of the townships, and the court affirmed. It held that the annexation legislation violated Mich. Const. art. 4, §§ 24, 25 (1963) because its title did not advise anyone that the powers of the SBC were being dramatically enlarged by such legislation. However, in reversing in part the holdings of the trial courts, the court held that the legislation's classification of "100 or less" persons as determining referendum rights did not constitute a violation of equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments.

 

2006 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Serafin v. Serafin


Docket No. 23915


Court of Appeals of Michigan


67 Mich. App. 517; 241 N.W.2d 272; 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 1264


November 10, 1975, Submitted  
February 26, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Appeal granted by Serafin v. Serafin, 397 Mich. 889, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 1077 (1976)
Affirmed by Serafin v. Serafin, 401 Mich. 629, 258 N.W.2d 461, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 122 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, Charles Kaufman, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-husband sought review of the order of the Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan), which granted a divorce, but required the ex-husband to pay child support for a child born during the marriage, but which he did not father.


OVERVIEW: The trial court refused to recognize evidence that the parties did not have access to each other during the time in which the child must have been conceived, because of an evidentiary rule known as Lord Mansfield's rule which disallowed a spouse to bastardize the legitimacy of a child born during the marriage. The court reversed and held that in the application of the rule to these particular facts, the rule violated the due process clauses of the United States and Michigan Constitutions. The court held that while it did not question the strong presumption of legitimacy, the hindrance caused by the operation of the evidentiary rule to these particular facts, was fatal because it prevented the admission of conclusive evidence establishing the paternity of the child in question; and that preventing a party from introducing his own evidence ran contrary to basic tenets of fundamental fairness, as did excluding evidence crucial to a disposition of the issue that was in controversy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment.

 

2007 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People of Pontiac v. Klein


Docket No. 21889


Court of Appeals of Michigan


67 Mich. App. 556; 242 N.W.2d 436; 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 1269


January 7, 1976, Submitted  
February 23, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Oakland, Richard D. Kuhn, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a decision from the 50th District Court (Michigan), which convicted defendants of violating a municipal ordinance that banned the use of profane or obscene language.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with violating a municipal breach of peace ordinance that prohibited profane or obscene language. They requested a jury instruction that would have instructed the jury that they could not convict defendants without first finding that they had uttered fighting words. The request was denied, and the trial court instructed the jury that they had to find the language to be grossly vulgar or profane to convict. Defendants were convicted and sought review. The court reversed and found that the trial court erred when it denied defendants' requested instruction. It found that the language used by defendants was required to be characterized as fighting words in order to sustain a conviction for violation of the peace ordinance. Therefore, the trial court erred when it did not use the instruction requested by defendants.


OUTCOME: The corut found that the trial corut erred when it did not use the instructions provided by defendants and reversed defendants' convictions.

 

2008 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Serafin v. Peoples Community Hospital Authority


Docket No. 22836


Court of Appeals of Michigan


67 Mich. App. 560; 242 N.W.2d 438; 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 1270


January 15, 1976, Submitted  
February 23, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Leave to appeal denied by Serafin v. Peoples Cmty. Hosp. Auth., 397 Mich. 880, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 761 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, Charles S. Farmer, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review from a judgment of no cause of action of the patient's medical malpractice action against defendant health care providers entered in the Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan). The case was dismissed by the trial court's directed verdict granted at the close of proofs in a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: The patient argued that the cause of death was a blood transfusion reaction. However, the patient did not offer any medical experts of his own but instead relied on cross-examination of two of the health care providers. The court rejected this argument because there was no record evidence to support the patient's theories especially where all the witnesses testified as to the cause of death, which excluded the patient's theory of negligence. The patient also argued that the trial court abused its discretion by limiting the scope of his examination both in direct examination and cross-examination. The court rejected this argument because the trial court primarily disallowed further questioning related to theories of death, which were not plead by the patient. Further, the court noted that the trial court had the authority to control the order and admission of evidence. Finally, the court found that the constitutionality of Mich. Comp. Laws § 331.422 (Mich. Stat. Ann. 14.1179(22)) pertaining to certain interrogatories was not an issue as the patient received all the information requested in the interrogatories through the testimony of one of the health care providers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's directed verdict, dismissing the patient's medical malpractice action at the close of proofs.

 

2009 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brow


Docket No. 23886


Court of Appeals of Michigan


67 Mich. App. 407; 241 N.W.2d 227; 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 1252


December 8, 1975, Submitted  
February 11, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Livingston, Bert M. Hensick, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Livingston County Circuit Court (Michigan), which convicted him of larceny over $ 100, a violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.356. Defendant was subsequently sentenced to a term of three to five years in prison.


OVERVIEW: A complainant claimed that his toolbox was missing from his truck. The police traced the toolbox to defendant. Defendant was charged with stealing or unlawfully removing property from an automobile. At the close of the preliminary examination, the prosecutor moved to have defendant bound over for trial on a charge of larceny from a motor vehicle of property in excess of $ 5 in value. The magistrate, however, bound defendant over on a charge of larceny over $ 100. Defendant moved to suppress evidence and to quash the information. The trial court denied the motions. Defendant was convicted of the charged crime. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings. The court held that the magistrate's alteration of the charged offense deprived defendant of important cross-examination and, consequently, of his right to a preliminary examination. The court ruled that there was a legitimate question concerning whether the stolen property exceeded $ 100 in value. The court held that defendant conceded the value element and did not cross-examine the complainant concerning this element because the complaint charged a theft of property worth more than $ 5.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

2010 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Stanton v. Lloyd Hammond Produce Farms


Docket No. 22408


Court of Appeals of Michigan


67 Mich. App. 279; 240 N.W.2d 773; 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 1180


November 5, 1975, Submitted  
February 10, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 397 Mich   .


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board.



DISPOSITION: Award of medical expenses affirmed and denial of wage benefits reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee claimed wage benefits and medical expenses after he was injured while employed by defendant employer. A referee awarded both. The Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Michigan) affirmed the medical expenses award, but reversed the award of wage benefits under the agricultural workers' exclusion, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 418.115(d). The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee delivered produce for the employer. The employee was returning to the employer's farm from a delivery when his truck hit a patch of ice and rolled over. When the accident happened, the employee was on his way to his sister's home to tell his brother-in-law that he would need a ride home from the farm. He could not call them because their phone was out of order. The route taken by the employee would have added less than 10 miles to the total trip, but the employer claimed the deviation took the employee out of the course of employment. The employee argued that Gallegos v. Glaser Crandall Co., which found that § 418.115(d) violated equal protection, meant that the exclusion was void ab initio. Reversing the denial of wage benefits and affirming the award of medical benefits, the court held that the employee's expectable deviation from the routine of work did not render his injuries noncompensable. The court declined to apply the void ab initio theory and held that application of § 418.115(d) to the employee violated his right to equal protection because there was no basis for distinguishing between employees based solely on the contents of their trucks.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of medical expenses. The court reversed the denial of wage benefits and remanded the cause to the Commission for reinstatement of the referee's award.

 

2011 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People of Adrian v. Poucher


Docket No. 23294


Court of Appeals of Michigan


67 Mich. App. 133; 240 N.W.2d 298; 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 1163


December 9, 1975, Submitted  
January 27, 1976, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Lenawee, Rex B. Martin, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People appealed the decision from the Circuit Court for the County of Lenawee (Michigan), which affirmed the district court, which held that a motorcycle helmet law, City of Adrian, Mich., Ordinance § 6.23 of the Uniform Traffic Code, was unconstitutional. Defendant was charged with not wearing a crash helmet while operating a motorcycle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion to quash the summons, which was granted. The People argued that the ordinance was within the legitimate police power of a city. On appeal, the court agreed. A city had a legitimate interest in promoting the general welfare and health of its citizens, which the ordinance fostered. Further, issues of police power belonged to the legislature, not the courts. Moreover, the presumption that legislation was constitutional came into play, which defendant did not rebut. While not specifically overruling the case law that the lower courts relied upon, the court disapproved the decision that held that motorcycle helmet laws were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The decision of the circuit court was reversed.

 

2012 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. McDonald


Docket No. 23769


Court of Appeals of Michigan


67 Mich. App. 64; 240 N.W.2d 268; 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 1152


November 6, 1975, Submitted  
January 27, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Kent, John H. Vander Wal, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court (Michigan), which sustained his conviction for cutting the hair of a male person contrary to § 55 of the Barber Licensing and Regulation Act of 1968, as amended, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 338.1655.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a licensed cosmetologist. He was convicted after a bench trial for cutting the hair of a male person. On appeal, defendant alleged that the licensing restriction was unconstitutional. The court noted that § 2 of the Cosmetology Act, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 338.752(b) permitted a licensed cosmetologist to cut the hair of "any female." The court reversed. The court noted that it could not perceive any rational or reasonable relation between the legislative objectives to secure qualified practitioners and insure sanitary facilities and the restriction of the haircutting activity of cosmetologists to female persons. Accordingly, it held that the restriction in § 338.752 violated the due process and equal protection clauses of the United States and Michigan Constitutions, U.S. Const. amend XIV, Mich. Const. art. 1, §§ 2 and 17, respectively.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for cutting the hair of a male person.

 

2013 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Harter v. Swartz Creek


Docket No. 22643


Court of Appeals of Michigan


66 Mich. App. 552; 239 N.W.2d 422; 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 1218


December 3, 1975, Submitted  
January 7, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Genesee, John W. Baker, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of a judgment of a trial court (Michigan), which upheld the constitutionality of Mich. Comp. Laws § 46.175b in the taxpayer's action against defendant, the City of Swartz Creek, Michigan.


OVERVIEW: The City attempted to enter into sewage disposal and water supply contracts, which were to be financed by municipal bonds. Pursuant to § 46.175b, the city published notice of its resolution authorizing the contracts in the local newspaper. The taxpayer, who was also a landowner, did not reside in the City, and he did not receive a copy of the newspaper. The taxpayer challenged the proposed contracts, and the trial court granted summary judgment to the City. In reversing, the court held that § 46.175b was unconstitutional. The court concluded that § 46.175b violated the due process clauses of both the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution and Mich. Const. art. 2, § 16 because it failed to provide adequate methods of notice for known parties.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and held the statute in question unconstitutional.

 

2014 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Williams


Docket No. 22350


Court of Appeals of Michigan


66 Mich. App. 521; 239 N.W.2d 653; 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 1214


October 9, 1975, Submitted  
January 7, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Newaygo, Harold Van Domelen, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded for trial with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Newaygo County Circuit Court (Michigan), which denied his motion to dismiss a criminal charge of murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to murdering a seven-year-old girl in Allegan County and a 13-year-old girl in Newaygo County. He was adjudicated a criminal sexual psychopathic person and committed to a state hospital. Three months after his release, he was arrested for the murder occurring in Newaygo County. Defendant moved to dismiss the charge. The trial court denied the motion. Defendant contended that the maintenance of the charge violated the 180-day rule, his right to a speedy trial, and Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 780.508. The court held: (1) defendant was not, consistent with the purposes of the 180-day rule, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 780.131 et seq., an inmate of a penal institution during his confinement in a mental hospital; (2) defendant's right to a speedy trial was not denied where a complaint issued six years previously but there was no warrant served, no formal charges mad, and no arraignment; and (3) the immunity provided in Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 780.508 prohibited prosecution on the Allegan County charge only, which was the crime of which defendant stood charged when he was committed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision from the trial court, which denied defendant's motion to dismiss the criminal charge of murder. The court remanded the case to the trial court with the instruction that the court conduct a Walker hearing to determine the validity of defendant's 1967 confession to the Newaygo murder.

 

2015 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Warren v. State Constr. Code Com.


Docket No. 22033


Court of Appeals of Michigan


66 Mich. App. 493; 239 N.W.2d 640; 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 1211


October 15, 1975, Submitted  
January 7, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Macomb, Howard R. Carroll, J.
City of Warren v. State Constr. Code Comm'n, 393 Mich. 810, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 1096 (1975)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State Construction Code Commission (commission) filed a motion for immediate consideration and an application for emergency stay of proceedings after the circuit court had entered a second temporary restraining order exempting plaintiff city from the application of the State Construction Code Act of 1972 (Act), Mich. Comp. Laws § 125.1501 et seq. (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 5.2949(1) et seq.).


OVERVIEW: The commission promulgated rules governing the construction and occupancy of buildings contained in the basic building code. The circuit court issued a restraining order temporarily exempting the city from the application of the State Construction Code Act of 1972 (Act), Mich. Comp. Laws § 125.1501 et seq. (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 5.2949(1) et seq.). The city filed an amended complaint, adding another count based on § 64 of the Administrative Procedures Act of 1972, Mich. Comp. Laws § 24.264 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 3.560(164)), and again requested injunctive relief. The commission filed a motion for immediate consideration and an application for emergency stay of proceedings in the court. The circuit court entered a second temporary restraining order based on the city's amended complaint. On appeal, the court vacated the temporary restraining orders and dismissed the complaint. The court held that the law enacted by the legislature contained detailed standards, which were implemented by the commission. The court held that the delegation of legislative power to the commission to promulgate a state construction code was valid and not unconstitutional on its face.


OUTCOME: Pursuant to the commission's request on appeal, the court dismissed the city's complaint alleging that the Act was unconstitutional and reversed the order of the circuit court that had issued a second temporary restraining order exempting the city from the application of the Act.

 

2016 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gillman


Docket No. 21437


Court of Appeals of Michigan


66 Mich. App. 419; 239 N.W.2d 396; 1976 Mich. App. LEXIS 1203


December 2, 1975, Submitted  
January 6, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Lenawee, Rex B. Martin, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the district court (Michigan), which convicted him of breaking and entering in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.110.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of breaking and entering as a result of breaking into a sporting goods store. Defendant appealed, claiming that the trial court erred in allowing a detective to be recalled to the stand because the detective was a rebuttal witness to defendant's alibi witness and defendant received no notice from the State that the detective would be called. In addition, defendant claimed that he was entitled to a reversal of the conviction because there was insufficient evidence to support a finding of the element of "entering." The court ruled that the trial court did not err in allowing the detective to be recalled because the detective was called solely to impeach the credibility of defendant's alibi witness and not to offer testimony contradicting the actual alibi testimony that was given. Finally, where the plastic over the window had been removed, the window glass had been shattered, and a wooden bar, which was part of the burglary system had been removed, there was sufficient evidence to support a finding that defendant had "entered" the store because all that was necessary to find an "entering" was that any part of his body was introduced within the store.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

2017 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Atcher


Docket No. 15264


Court of Appeals of Michigan


65 Mich. App. 734; 238 N.W.2d 389; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1019


October 16, 1975, Submitted  
December 3, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Leave to appeal denied by People v. Atcher #1, 399 Mich. 866, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 364 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Berrien, Chester J. Burns, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought relief from an entry of judgment by the trial court (Michigan) on a jury verdict convicting and sentencing defendant of extortion for threatening a witness under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.213; Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.410.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his co-defendant approached the victim on several occasions when they saw her sitting outside of the courtroom and threatened her about testifying against another person accused of assault and battery. Defendant was charged and convicted for this conduct. On appeal, the court found that defendant failed to object to certain of the prosecution's remarks. That generally precluded consideration of the issue on appeal. The prosecution's remarks were not prejudicial or racially motivated and did not require reversal. Defendant's counsel was not incompetent. Sufficient evidence supported the jury's verdict on the charge. The argument that the statute was inapplicable to defendant's conduct or was unconstitutional was frivolous. Also, defendant did not object to the prosecution's calling an unendorsed res gestae witness on rebuttal, the trial court gave a limiting instruction about the testimony, and that testimony was not prejudicial to defendant to require reversal. Finally, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in determining that the victim was competent to testify. None of defendant's assertions of error required reversal of his conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting and sentencing defendant.

 

2018 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Stoudemire


Docket No. 18153


Court of Appeals of Michigan


65 Mich. App. 664; 238 N.W.2d 365; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1010


October 10, 1975, Submitted  
November 24, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Request granted People v. Stoudemire, 399 Mich. 1039, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 1452 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, Theodore R. Bohn, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, defendant was convicted in a trial court in Wayne (Michigan) of assault with intent to commit rape under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.85. He appealed as of right. The complainant was a co-owner of a store that defendant frequented. The complainant said that, after ascertaining that she was the only person in the store, he forced her into a back room, drew a pistol, stated that he intended to rape her, and set about to do so.


OVERVIEW: The complainant said that her husband returned and defendant fled before completing the rape. The arresting officers were not asked about any statement defendant made. The prosecutor asked defendant on cross-examination whether he had said anything to the arresting police officers. Defendant replied that he told them he had been assaulted by the complainant's husband and another man. The court explained that to allow such a question of defendant violated either his right to have the prosecution introduce during its case in chief all statements claimed to have been made by him before he was put to his proofs or permitted bringing to the jury's attention evidence that defendant did not make a statement, an impermissible reflection on his exercise of his right to remain silent. Under the circumstances of this case, the court believed that the violation did not compel a reversal. The court noted that defense counsel did not object and the prosecutor made no reference to defendant's testimony during his closing argument. The court rejected defendant's argument concerning identification testimony because his identity was not at issue. The court rejected defendant's other argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

2019 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sabo


Docket No. 22472


Court of Appeals of Michigan


65 Mich. App. 573; 237 N.W.2d 564; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 993


October 15, 1975, Submitted  
November 13, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 396 Mich 849.
Leave to appeal denied by People v. Sabo, 396 Mich. 849, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 1279 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Houghton, Stephen D. Condon, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, sought review of a judgment of the circuit court (Michigan), which convicted him of breaking and entering upon his plea of guilty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 17 years old when he was charged with dual counts of safe robbery at a high school and breaking and entering the school building with intent to commit larceny under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.110. Defense counsel filed a motion to dismiss the charges against defendant because of lack of jurisdiction or, in the alternative, to waive jurisdiction to the probate court. The trial court dismissed the motion, and defendant pled guilty to the breaking and entering charge. The court affirmed the judgment and held that even if there was concurrent jurisdiction under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 712A.2(d) and § 712A.2(d) was unconstitutional, original jurisdiction reposed in the circuit court. The court noted that Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 712A.2(a) granted exclusive original jurisdiction over juveniles under 17 years of age to the probate court, and that Mich. Const. art. VI, § 13 (1963), granted original jurisdiction to the circuit court of all matters not prohibited by law. The court found no statute prohibiting circuit court jurisdiction over a 17-year-old accused of a felony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment against defendant.

Anderson v. Brown Bros., Inc.


Docket No. 19023


Court of Appeals of Michigan


65 Mich. App. 409; 237 N.W.2d 528; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 975


March 14, 1975, Submitted  
November 12, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Leave to appeal denied by, Request denied by Anderson v. Brown Bros., Inc., 396 Mich. 872, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 556 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Ingham, Marvin J. Salmon, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured victim challenged the judgment of the trial court (Michigan), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, city and contractor, on the nuisance and simple negligence counts of the victim's complaint and also granted their motion for judgment of no cause of action on the gross negligence or wilful and wanton misconduct count.


OVERVIEW: The contractor was removing gravel from the city's property to create a man-made lake. As the victim began to dive into the lake of the gravel pit, the bank crumbled and he fell headfirst into the shallow water and sustained paralyzing injuries. The trial court granted summary judgment on the nuisance and simple negligence counts based on the authority of the recreational property owners immunity statute, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 300.201 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 13.1485). The court found that the victim's diving and swimming activities were within that statute. However, reading that statute together with the governmental immunity statute that was in effect at the time of the injury, it held that the statute did not cover the lands of municipality, or the tenants or lessees of that land, while the municipality was engaged in a governmental function. It reversed the summary judgment on the nuisance and simple negligence counts. The court did not find that the trial court's findings of fact and conclusions of law on the gross negligence count were clearly erroneous and it affirmed the judgment of no cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of no cause of action on the gross negligence or wilful and wanton misconduct count of the victim's complaint. It reversed the grant of summary judgment on the nuisance and simple negligence counts.

Shavers v. Ag

Court of Appeals of Michigan


65 Mich. App. 355; 237 N.W.2d 325; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 970

November 5, 1975, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, Horace W. Gilmore, J.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:

Comp. Laws Ann. § 500.3101 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought a declaratory judgment action to test the constitutionality of no fault legislation under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 500.3101 et seq., which abolished most common law tort liability for automobile related personal injuries in Michigan. Defendants were state officials and insurance companies, which filed cross-complaints challenging the legislation. OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the determination that the legislation's property protection provisions violated due process and equal protection principles, reversed in part the determination that the legislation was rendered unconstitutional by excluding motorcycles, and vacated in part the judgment where the parties lacked standing to raise certain issues.

Marshall v. Consumers Power Co.


Docket No. 21045


Court of Appeals of Michigan


65 Mich. App. 237; 237 N.W.2d 266; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 957; 82 A.L.R.3d 729


May 14, 1975, Submitted  
October 27, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Leave to appeal denied by Marshall v. Consumers Power Co., 397 Mich. 822, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 717 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Midland, James R. Rood, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county resident appealed from a judgment of the Midland County Circuit Court (Michigan) that granted summary judgment for defendant nuclear power plant company in plaintiff's action seeking damages and a declaratory judgment that defendant's proposed plant would violate the Michigan Environmental Protection Act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 691.1201 et seq. (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 14.528(201) et seq.), and constitute a public and private nuisance.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff county resident challenged the grant of summary judgment for defendant nuclear power plant company in plaintiff's action alleging that the operation of defendant's proposed power plant would violate the Michigan Environmental Protection Act (MEPA), Mich. Comp. Laws § 691.1201 et seq. (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 14.528(201) et seq.), and constitute a common law nuisance. The trial court held that federal law preempted state consideration of plaintiff's complaint. On appeal, the court held that under the Atomic Energy Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2021(k) the federal government preempted state action concerning radiological, but not nonradiological matters. The court found that licensing and regulation of more dangerous activities, such as nuclear reactors, remained the exclusive responsibility of the Atomic Energy Commission, but that the fact that, under the National Environmental Policy Act of 1969, 42 U.S.C.S. § 4321 et seq., a nuclear plant's environmental impact was a matter of concern to both federal and state governments did not limit state action under MEPA. Although state action was not limited, the court affirmed because plaintiff failed to allege a present injury or nuisance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment in favor of defendant nuclear power plant company in plaintiff county resident's action seeking to stop construction of defendant's proposed plant on the grounds that it violated the Michigan Environmental Protection Act (MEPA) and constituted a nuisance. The court held that federal preemption did not completely limit state action under MEPA, but that plaintiff failed to allege present injury.

 

2024 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


White Pine Hunting Club v. Schalkofski


Docket No. 21624


Court of Appeals of Michigan


65 Mich. App. 147; 237 N.W.2d 223; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 944


June 4, 1975, Submitted  
October 14, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Alpena, Joseph P. Swallow, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hunting club sought review an order of the trial court (Michigan), which dismissed its declaratory judgment action brought to challenge the constitutionality of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 229.1. The trial court held that the eminent domain statute was constitutional in favor of defendant individuals.


OVERVIEW: The hunting club brought the action, alleging that Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 229.1 was an unconstitutional taking of property. The statute allowed the individuals to apply to the township supervisor when they sought to establish a private road. A meeting then would have been held for the purpose of empanelling a jury to determine the necessity for the road. The trial court held that the statute was constitutional. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the statute was unconstitutional because it was repugnant to Mich. Const. art. 10, § 2. The constitution expressly used the words "public use" when it authorized a taking of land, and even when a state paid a landowner for property, it did not have power to take the property without his consent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

 

2025 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


CITIZENS v. STATE SUPERINTENDENT OF PUB. INSTRUCTION


Docket Nos. 22482, 22483, 22484, 22485


Court of Appeals of Michigan


65 Mich. App. 168; 237 N.W.2d 232; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 947


June 12, 1975, Submitted  
October 14, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Leave to appeal denied by Citizens to Advance Pub. Educ. v. State Superintendent of Pub. Instruction, 397 Mich. 854, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 860 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Ingham, James T. Kallman, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state superintendent of public instruction appealed the decision of the Gingham County Circuit Court (Michigan), which granted defendants, citizens group to advance public education and others motion for a summary judgment and entered an order that enjoined the operation of three programs from operating shared time secular educational programs that had leased premises from a parochial school.


OVERVIEW: On the parochial school grounds the three school districts operated a shared time educational program. Secular subjects were taught my teachers employed by the public school systems. The classes were open to all children in grades three to eight. Children enrolled in the parochial school attend the public school instruction during part of the day and private classes for the remainder of the day. The court reversed the judgment, noting that shared time in and of itself did not violate Mich. Const. art. 8, § 2, which prohibited school districts from discriminating as to religion, creed, race, color, or national origin. The court also noted that the three programs had a secular legislative purpose of educating young people in secular subjects. The court found that the content of the activity on the premises leased was controlled solely by the public school district and the lessor had no authority over these activities. The programs were open to all children eligible to attend public schools. There was a clear time segregation of supervision between the school district and the parochial school.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment in favor of the citizens group in their action to enjoin the operation of three programs from operating shared time secular educational programs that had leased premises from a parochial school.

Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion denied by In re Cooper, 1998 U.S. App. LEXIS 14729 (6th Cir. Mich., June 24, 1998)

DISPOSITION: On remand, affirmed.

OVERVIEW: One defendant, a juvenile, had contended that a probate court's waiver of jurisdiction under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 712A.4 was erroneous because the statute was unconstitutional. The court concluded that the waiver was proper because defendant had been afforded the benefit of the standards set forth in Mich. Juv. Ct. Thus, the question did not deprive defendants of a fair trial. The trial court did not err in denying defendants' motion to sever the case for trial. The acquittal of three others accused of conspiracy did not diminish the capability of defendants to conspire to commit murder.


OUTCOME: On remand, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Butler v. Raupp


Docket No. 19960


Court of Appeals of Michigan


65 Mich. App. 20; 236 N.W.2d 748; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 929


June 20, 1975, Submitted  
October 13, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Oakland, Farrell E. Roberts, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as to defendant Raupp, reversed and remanded as to the liability of defendants Scollin, Jr., and Scollin, Sr.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of the decision from the Oakland County Circuit Court (Michigan), which entered a jury's unanimous verdict of no cause of action against defendants, and denied plaintiff's motions for judgment notwithstanding the verdict and a new trial in plaintiff's personal injury action against defendants.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff suffered injuries when the car he was a passenger in collided with another automobile. Plaintiff filed a personal injury action. The trial court entered the jury's verdict in favor of defendants and denied plaintiff's motions for judgment notwithstanding the verdict and for a new trial. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment in favor of the defendant driver that plaintiff was with and reversed and remanded the claim against defendant driver of the other vehicle and the owner of that vehicle. The court held the trial court improperly held that plaintiff's negligent entrustment claim was not properly pled because it was not contained in a separate count in the plaintiff's complaint, holding that failure to include the claim in a separate count was not a fatal error. The court also held that plaintiff's negligent entrustment claim was not barred because plaintiff did not raise the claim at the pretrial conference. The court also held that since the trial court's judgment, the guest passenger statute, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 257.401, had been ruled unconstitutional. Thus, liability of defendant driver that struck the car plaintiff was riding with had to be redetermined.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of defendant that plaintiff was riding with, however, the court reversed and remanded for a new trial the judgment in favor of defendants, driver who struck the car plaintiff was riding in and the owner of that automobile.

Midland v. Michigan State Boundary Com.


Docket Nos. 19154, 19155, 19156, 20255


Court of Appeals of Michigan


64 Mich. App. 700; 236 N.W.2d 551; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1309


April 11, 1975, Submitted  
October 13, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Appeal granted by Midland Twp. v. State Boundary Comm'n, 397 Mich. 810, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 661 (1976)
Reversed by Midland v. Michigan State Boundary Com., 401 Mich. 641, 259 N.W.2d 326, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 123 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from Ingham and Midland, Donald L. Reisig and John X. Theiler, JJ.



DISPOSITION: Midland Township v. State Boundary Commission; Affirmed.

Midland Township v. Midland County Board of Commissioners; Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, State Boundary Commission (SBC) and county boards of commissioners, challenged the orders of the Circuit Courts for Ingham and Midland Counties (Michigan), which awarded summary judgment in favor of plaintiff townships, permanently enjoined orders entered by the SBC under 1970 Mich. Pub. Acts 219 (Act), and declared that the Act was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the provisions of 1970 Mich. Pub. Acts 219, the SBC approved two petitions for annexation that were filed with and transferred from the county boards of commissioners. The townships filed an action to permanently enjoin the SBC from enforcing the orders entered and from conducting further proceedings under the Act, which they claimed was violative of Mich. Const. of 1963, art. IV, § 24-25. The SBC sought review, and the court affirmed the orders of the circuit courts. The court held that the procedure followed by the Michigan legislature in enacting the Act was violative of the constitution because: (1) the Act did not include within its title as an object of the law the subject of "annexation"; the title of the Act did not mention conferring additional powers on the SBC; and (3) in adopting the Act, the legislature attempted to amend 1968 Mich. Pub. Acts 191 without re-enacting or republishing the latter act. The court rejected defendant's arguments that there were insufficient criteria to support the delegation of legislative authority to the SBC, that the classification in the Act was constitutionally suspect, and that the annexations constituted gerrymandering.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the circuit courts that declared the Act unconstitutional and permanently enjoined the enforcement of the SBC's orders entered under and proceedings taken pursuant to the Act.

Hanger v. State


Docket No. 22342


Court of Appeals of Michigan


64 Mich. App. 572; 236 N.W.2d 148; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1296


June 9, 1975, Submitted  
September 24, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Leave to appeal denied by Hanger v. Dep't of State Highways, 399 Mich. 812, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 904 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Court of Claims, James T. Kallman, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from the decision of the Court of Claims (Michigan), which granted defendant State Highway Department's (department) motion for accelerated judgment on the grounds that plaintiffs had not complied with the six-month notice provision of the Court of Claims Act, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 600.6431(3) (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 27A.6431(3)) (the act), in filing their claim for personal injuries for the department's alleged negligence.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought an action against the department and sought damages for injuries sustained in an automobile accident allegedly occasioned by defective road maintenance. The lower court granted the department's motion for accelerated judgment based on the untimely filing under the act and the court reversed. The court found that the six-month notice provision in the act applied to plaintiffs and was not constitutionally infirm in that it was rationally related to the legitimate government interest of having notice of claims while investigation was still easily achieved. The court held that the action could only be dismissed for failure to comply with the notice provisions if the department could show that it was prejudiced by plaintiffs filing of the claim seven months after the accident. The court remanded the matter for a determination of whether the department suffered any prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's grant of the department's motion for accelerated judgment and remanded the matter with the order that for the notice provisions to bar the action, the department had to show that it suffered prejudice as a result of plaintiffs' late filing.

Horner's Trucking Serv. v. State Highway Dep't


Docket No. 21022


Court of Appeals of Michigan


64 Mich. App. 513; 236 N.W.2d 122; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1289


June 10, 1975, Submitted  
September 23, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Leave to appeal denied by Horner's Trucking Serv. v. Dep't of State Hwys, 399 Mich. 812, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 908 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Court of Claims, Kenneth G. Prettie, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant appealed a decision of a Court of Claims (Michigan), which granted a motion for an accelerated judgment, pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.6431(1) of the Michigan Court of Claims Act, brought by defendant, the Michigan State Highway Department. The claimant had sought property damages and contribution for potential liability for an accident allegedly caused by a highway defect.


OVERVIEW: The claimant's truck was involved in an accident with another vehicle on a state highway. The claimant sent the Department a notice of the accident. Two weeks later, the claimant filed its action against the Department. The claims court granted the accelerated judgment because of the claimant's failure to prove notice within one year of the accident. On appeal, the claimant alleged that the 120-day notice of the sovereign immunity statute, Mich. Comp. Laws § 691.1404, was applicable but void; that the notice provision of Mich. Comp. A determination that § 600.6431 was jurisdictional had to be made by the State Supreme Court.

Civil Rights Comm'n v. Chrysler Corp.


Docket No. 18597


Court of Appeals of Michigan


64 Mich. App. 393; 235 N.W.2d 791; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1277; 16 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1578; 10 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P10,571


June 4, 1975, Submitted  
September 22, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Michigan Civil Rights Com. ex rel. Boyd v. Chrysler Corp., Mack Ave. Stamping Plant, 80 Mich. App. 368, 263 N.W.2d 376, 1977 Mich. App. LEXIS 1297 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Ingham, Jack W. Warren, J.
Mich. Civ. Rights Comm'n v. Chrysler Corp., 391 Mich. 843, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 796 (1974)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Civil Rights Commission (CRC) challenged the summary judgment for defendant employer granted by the Ingham County Circuit Court on the employer's petition for review of the CRC's finding that race was a factor in the suspension and discharge of an employee.


OVERVIEW: Following the employee's suspension from his job, he filed a complaint with the CRC alleging racial discrimination in employment. The employee was later discharged, and he filed a union grievance for unjust discharge. The arbitrator in the union grievance concluded that the employee was properly discharged. The CRC then issued a final order concluding that race was a factor in the employee's discharge. The employer petitioned for review. The circuit court granted the employer summary judgment. The appeal followed. The court reversed the judgment. Pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 423.307 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 17.458) a written complaint was mandatory. Here, the employee's complaint filed with the CRC immediately subsequent to his suspension, and less than one month prior to his discharge substantially complied with the mandatory requirements of that statute. The employee's union grievance claimed only unjust discharge and made no reference to the racial discrimination alleged before the CRC. Moreover, there was no indication that the arbitrator gave any consideration to the possibility of racial discrimination. Thus, the arbitrator's decision did not bar the CRC proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment for the employer and remanded the case to the circuit court for a decision on the merits.

 

2033 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Livingston


Docket No. 21682


Court of Appeals of Michigan


64 Mich. App. 247; 236 N.W.2d 63; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1259


June 17, 1975, Submitted  
September 11, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Recorder's Court of Detroit, Samuel C. Gardner, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from a decision of the Recorder's Court of Detroit (Michigan), which suppressed the evidentiary use of tape recordings. Defendants argued that the recordings were unconstitutionally obtained, that they violated the Michigan wiretapping act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.539a et seq. (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.807(1) et seq.), and that a participant had not voluntary consented to the warrantless search of her telephone conversations.


OVERVIEW: A man tape-recorded phone conversations of his wife discussing the possibility of having the man murdered by a hit man. The police confronted the wife and suggested that she help trap the hit man in return for immunity. The plan did not work, but the hit man later threatened the wife and firebombed her house. In concert with the police, the wife feigned renewed interest in the murder plot, and several phone conversations were recorded. Defendants were charged with conspiring to commit first-degree murder. The trial court granted defendants' motion to suppress the tape recordings. The court reversed the order, holding that: (1) a recent decision was read to hold that search warrants were required for taped phone conversations, but the decision was not retroactive because police reasonably relied on the prior law; (2) evidence obtained by the man in violation of wiretapping laws did not require suppression because suppression was not among enumerated remedies; and (3) the trial court erred in ruling that the wife's consent to the tape recordings in conjunction with an immunity offer was not voluntary, as the wife contacted the police in response to threats and firebombing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order suppressing the admission of the tape recordings into evidence, and remanded the case for trial.

 

2034 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Xerox Corp. v. Detroit


Docket Nos. 20039, 20040, 20041, 20042, 20043, 20044, 20045, 20046, 20047, 20048, 20049, 20050, 20051, 20052, 20053, 20054, 20055, 20056


Court of Appeals of Michigan


64 Mich. App. 159; 235 N.W.2d 173; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1249


May 6, 1975, Submitted  
September 10, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 395 Mich 800.
Leave to appeal denied by Xerox Corp. v. City of Detroit, 395 Mich. 800, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 1014 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, Harry J. Dingeman, Jr., J.
Xerox Corp. v. City of Detroit, 383 Mich. 779, 1970 Mich. LEXIS 659 (1970)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation filed suit against defendants, a county and city, alleging that property taxes were unlawfully assessed on leased equipment. The Circuit Court for Wayne County (Michigan) denied defendants' motions for summary judgment and a directed verdict, and they appealed.


OVERVIEW: Property taxes were assessed against the corporation as the owner of leased copying equipment. The corporation paid the taxes under protest and filed suit claiming that the assessments were illegal where the assessors used the published selling prices for the equipment to determine value. Defendants claimed that they were entitled to summary judgment because the State Tax Commission had already made a binding decision in the matter. The court affirmed the denial of summary judgment because the Commission's determination was not final where the corporation had followed the proper procedural steps by first seeking relief from the Commission and then bringing suit for a refund. A hearing before the Commission pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 211.152 and a suit under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 211.53 to recover taxes paid under protest were not mutually exclusive remedies where the legislature provided taxpayers with alternate remedies for contesting taxes. Further, the remedy under § 211.53 was available only if a taxpayer established that the tax was unconstitutional and that was a matter of judicial review rather than administrative action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

2035 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Morgan v. Win Schuler's Restaurant


Docket No. 21610


Court of Appeals of Michigan


64 Mich. App. 37; 234 N.W.2d 885; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1230


June 6, 1975, Submitted  
August 28, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board.



DISPOSITION: Modified and affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the employer and its insurer, sought review of a decision of the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Michigan), which found that plaintiff employee was totally disabled on the basis of a psychiatric condition, which was precipitated by an accident at work.


OVERVIEW: The employee received third-degree burns when she was lighting floating brandy on top of coffee in her capacity as a waitress with the employer. The insurer voluntarily paid her compensation benefits for 44 weeks, and the employee filed a petition claiming a disabling injury continuing beyond that period of time and claiming a disabling neurosis resulting from the accident. A referee and the Board found that the employee was totally disabled on the basis of a psychiatric condition that was precipitated by the accident and awarded her compensation. The court affirmed that decision after lowering the award of interest. The court held that the employee's difficulties arose from a single-event injury and not from an occupational disease. The court found that the apportionment provision of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 418.431 could not be interpreted to cover single-event injuries. The court concluded that there was a reasonable basis for the distinction allowing for apportionment for occupational diseases but not for single-event injuries and that the employer was not denied equal protection. The court found evidence that the employee's total tip income exceeded her reported tip income.


OUTCOME: The court modified the Board's award of interest from six percent to five percent and affirmed the decision as modified.

 

2036 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Wayne v. Gladstone


Docket No. 21662


Court of Appeals of Michigan


64 Mich. App. 55; 235 N.W.2d 60; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1232


June 16, 1975, Submitted  
August 28, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, James N. Canham, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant land contract vendee sought review of an order of a trial court (Michigan), which ordered a building on her land to be padlocked for one year and the furniture and fixtures in the building sold in plaintiff state's suit under the nuisance abatement statute, Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.3801 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 27A. 3801).


OVERVIEW: The state brought suit against the land contract vendee under the nuisance abatement statute, Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.3801 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 27A. 3801), and the trial court ordered a building on her land to be padlocked for one year and the furniture and fixtures in the building sold. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the land contract vendee was not properly served with process. The court held that the state failed to avail itself of all the different methods it had to effect service upon the land contract vendee. The court held that the state could not, consistent with due process, proceed to lock up the property without first diligently trying to give her actual notice of the proceedings and an opportunity to be heard.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a trial court's orders to padlock a building on the land contract vendee's land for one year, and to sell the building's furniture and fixtures under the nuisance abatement statute.

Baker v. State Bd. of Dentistry


Docket No. 21073


Court of Appeals of Michigan


63 Mich. App. 729; 235 N.W.2d 157; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1222


June 12, 1975, Submitted  
August 27, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the State Board of Dentistry.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff dentist appealed an order of defendant State Board of Dentistry (Michigan), which suspended the dentist's license for six months for practicing in two locations in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 338.216.


OVERVIEW: The State Board of Dentistry suspended the dentist's license for practicing in two locations in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 338.216, and the dentist appealed. The court held that: (1) grants of legislative authority to boards were not to be left to the undefined caprice or choice of the boards; and (2) the Board had not complied with the requirements of the Administrative Procedures Act of 1969, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 24.201 et seq., as it had not followed the notice and public hearing requirements of the Act and had not formulated, much less promulgated and made available for public inspection, guidelines concerning its granting or withholding of approval of bi-location practices. The Board's order was vacated.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the Board's order suspending the dentist's license.

 

2038 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Cameron v. Secretary of State


Docket No. 21378


Court of Appeals of Michigan


63 Mich. App. 753; 235 N.W.2d 38; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1226


June 3, 1975, Submitted  
August 27, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 395 Mich 774.
Leave to appeal denied by Cameron v. Sec'y of State, 395 Mich. 774, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 939 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Ingham, Jack W. Warren, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver sought review of an order of the Ingham County Circuit Court (Michigan), which declined to address the constitutional issue that he raised in a petition, pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 257.323, for review of the Secretary of State's suspension of his driving privileges. The suspension was based on the Secretary's receipt of a record of his conviction for negligent homicide by the operation of a motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Following the driver's conviction, he was placed on probation for two years and his driver's license was suspended for a one year period. Pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 257.319, the Secretary then ordered an administrative suspension of his license for the same one-year period. He petitioned the circuit court for restoration of his driving privileges, contending that the Secretary's action was arbitrary and confiscatory as it deprived him of his license peremptorily and without benefit of a prior hearing. On appeal, the court held that the suspension was constitutional. It was similar to a suspension pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 257.303a, which had previously been held constitutional. Both statutes provided for a summary suspension of driving privileges for the protection of the motoring public. The Secretary's authority was sufficiently limited so that it did not provide unconstitutionally broad discretion as a conviction of one of six specified crimes was a condition precedent to a suspension. The Secretary's discretion as to the suspension's length was not unbridled, as it was limited to 21 months. Further, state law provided for effective post-revocation review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment, which modified the Secretary's administrative suspension of the driver's driving privileges by allowing him to drive back and forth to work only, but it extended the suspension so that it totalled two years.

 

2039 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mowrey


Docket No. 20630


Court of Appeals of Michigan


63 Mich. App. 676; 235 N.W.2d 23; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1215


June 11, 1975, Submitted  
August 26, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from St. Joseph, Robert E. A. Boyle, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the trial court (Michigan), which convicted him of taking indecent liberties with a child under the age of 16 years after defendant pled guilty. Defendant was examined at a state hospital to determine whether he needed psychiatric treatment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the trial court erred in failing to sua sponte order a hearing to determine defendant's competency to waive his constitutional rights and enter a plea of guilty. On appeal, the court held that there was no showing that defendant could not effectively communicate with his counsel or that he was unable to assist in his own defense as required for the trial court to raise the issue of defendant's competency. The court noted that on three occasions defendant stated to the trial court that his reason for pleading guilty was to obtain psychological help in dealing with his deviant behavior. The court indicated that defendant's statements did not suggest any lack of understanding of the nature of the charge against him. The court stated that the trial court could not have ordered private psychiatric treatment at the public's expense, and therefore the trial court insulated the defendant from free movement in society. The court determined that the trial court had done the best that it could within the limitations of the system.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

2040 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Peterson


Docket No. 19187


Court of Appeals of Michigan


63 Mich. App. 538; 234 N.W.2d 692; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1199


March 3, 1975, Submitted  
August 25, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Delta, Bernard H. Davidson, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the trial court (Michigan), which convicted defendant of possession of marijuana with intent to deliver under Mich. Comp. Laws § 335.341(1)(c) (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 18.1070(41)(1)(c). Defendant maintained that the search and seizure was illegal, that the application of the "two-ounce presumption" was improper, and that there was insufficient evidence to support the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The house in which defendant resided was searched by police and was conducted pursuant to a search warrant. The police found marijuana at the residence and defendant was arrested, charged, and convicted of possession with intent to deliver. Defendant appealed and the court reversed the conviction. Initially, the court held that the affidavit was sufficient to support the search warrant and that no error was committed in introducing the marijuana into evidence. The court reversed on the basis that the prosecutor relied on, and the trial court instructed on, the "two-ounce presumption," embodied in § 335.341(2), because case law previously ruled the presumption unconstitutional. The court also ruled that the presumption was inapplicable in the case, as there was no evidence that defendant possessed more than two ounces. Finally, the court concluded that the trial court did not err in denying a directed verdict of acquittal on the issue of simple possession but that the evidence was insufficient with regard to the possession with intent to deliver charge. Thus, the trial court should have granted a directed verdict for defendant on the possession with intent to deliver offense.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded defendant's conviction for possession of marijuana with intent to deliver.

 

2041 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Ford Motor Co. v. State Tax Comm'n


Docket No. 19600


Court of Appeals of Michigan


63 Mich. App. 577; 234 N.W.2d 711; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1202


March 3, 1975, Submitted  
August 25, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Appeal granted by Ford Motor Co. v. State Tax Comm'n, 396 Mich. 843, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 1190 (1976)
Affirmed by Ford Motor Co. v. Michigan State Tax Com., 400 Mich. 499, 255 N.W.2d 608, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 147 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from State Tax Commission.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporate taxpayer appealed from a decision of the Michigan State Tax Commission, challenging the method used to assess the taxpayer's inventories for a personal property assessment.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer timely filed a sworn personal property statement with the city in which its property was located, using the true cash value of its inventories in the city on tax day to determine the amount of its personal property. The city's board of review rejected the taxpayer's election to use the tax day method and determined that the true cash value of the taxpayer's taxable property in the city was the true cash value on tax day plus the average monthly value of the taxpayer's inventories in the city. On the taxpayer's appeal, the commission agreed with the city's board of review. The appellate court reversed the commission's decision, holding (1) that under the applicable statute, the taxpayer could elect to have its inventory in one assessing district assessed by the tax day method while having its inventory in another assessing district taxed on the basis of the average monthly inventory present in that assessing district, and (2) that the average level of assessment should have been computed after excluding the taxpayer's personal property because the value of the taxpayer's property comprised approximately 23 percent of the value of all property located in the city.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the commission's decision and remanded the cause for the entry of an order consistent with the court's opinion.
