Lockaby v. Wayne County


Docket No. 20075


Court of Appeals of Michigan


63 Mich. App. 185; 234 N.W.2d 444; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1150


February 11, 1975, Submitted  
August 12, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Reversed by, Remanded by Lockaby v. Wayne County, 399 Mich. 860, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 389 (1977)
Reversed by Lockaby v. Wayne County, 406 Mich. 65, 276 N.W.2d 1, 1979 Mich. LEXIS 349 (1979)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, George E. Bowles, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient sought review of the orders of the Wayne County Court (Michigan), which granted summary judgment and/or accelerated judgment in favor of defendants, county, county board of commissioners, individual county officials, city, and city hospital in the patient's action to recover for injuries purportedly suffered while in custody and during transportation to and treatment at the city hospital.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought an action to recover for injuries purportedly suffered while in the custody of the county sheriff's department and during transportation to and treatment at the city hospital. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the county, county board of commissioners, and individual county officials and granted a motion for summary and/or accelerated judgment in favor of the city and city hospital, based on the affirmative defense of governmental immunity. On appeal the court affirmed, holding that: (1) the patient's claim did not come within the dangerous or defective public building exception to governmental immunity, Mich. Comp. Laws § 691.1406 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 3.996(106)) because the alleged deficiencies had to do with providing human services, and not with the physical structure of any building; (2) the motor vehicle exception to the governmental immunity provision did not apply because the ambulance was not in a "state of being at work" within the meaning of the statute at the time and place the injury was allegedly inflicted; and (3) the governmental immunity statute, Mich. Comp. Laws § 691.1407 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 3.996(107)) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment and/or accelerated judgment in favor of defendants in the patient's action to recover for injuries purportedly suffered while in the county's custody and during transportation to and treatment at the city hospital.

 

2043 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Bedford v. Bates


Docket No. 21944


Court of Appeals of Michigan


62 Mich. App. 715; 233 N.W.2d 706; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1114


June 4, 1975, Submitted  
July 23, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Monroe, William J. Weipert, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged the judgment of the trial court (Michigan), which granted an injunction mandating that the property owner tie into the public sewer system of appellee township. The township had filed the action against the property owner to compel connection when she refused to forego using her septic tank system and refused to tie into the sewer system in compliance with an amended township ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The township had amended an ordinance to conform to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 123.281 et seq., which mandated that structures in which sanitary sewage originated had to be tied into public sewer systems. The property owner claimed that absent a showing that her septic tank system was inadequate she could not be forced into connecting with the public sewer system absent adequate compensation. On appeal, the court held that the township's police power allowed that type of sewer regulation with no compensation to the property owner. The court found that the ordinance was constitutional. The court stated that the community was to be considered as a whole in the matter of preservation of the health of all inhabitants because a failure by a few to conform to sanitary measures could inflict ill health and death upon many. Further, the court indicated that although the ordinance could work a hardship on one or more individuals whose facilities were sanitary, the action could not be regarded as unconstitutionally arbitrary or the taking of property without due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of the injunction.

 

2044 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Sutliff Agency, Inc. v. H. W. Kaufman Financial Group, Inc.


Docket No. 19912


Court of Appeals of Michigan


62 Mich. App. 418; 233 N.W.2d 607; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1075


January 16, 1975, Submitted  
July 15, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Oakland, Robert L. Templin, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant garnishees appealed an order by the Oakland County Circuit Court (Michigan) denying their motion to quash writs of garnishment previously issued by the circuit court clerk. Defendants claimed that Mich. Gen. Ct. R. 738 (1963) was unconstitutional in that it deprived them of their property without due process of law in violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Mich. Const. art. I, 17 (1963).


OVERVIEW: Mich. Gen. Ct. R. 738 (1963) and Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. 600.4011 permitted prejudgment garnishment writs. On appeal by defendants, the court held that the trial court erred in refusing to quash the writs of garnishment. The court discussed a decision issued by the Supreme Court of Michigan in the same year as the instant case, which held that the Michigan prejudgment garnishment procedure was unconstitutional insofar as the statute and the rule permitted the garnishment of funds in which the claimant had no interest without a bond requirement to protect the owner of the funds and without an opportunity for a prompt hearing. Two days after this decision, the United States Supreme Court rendered a decision in which it held that the Georgia prejudgment garnishment procedure violated due process. Because the Georgia procedure was similar to Michigan procedure, the United States Supreme Court decision was dispositive of the issue in the instant action. The court found that it was unnecessary to consider defendants' other argument relative to the propriety of the issuance of the writs because the issue of the constitutionality of the procedure was resolved in defendants' favor.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that had denied defendants' motion to quash writs of garnishment. The court granted defendants' motion to quash the writ of garnishment.

 

2045 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Samuels


Docket No. 19079


Court of Appeals of Michigan


62 Mich. App. 214; 233 N.W.2d 520; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1049


April 9, 1975, Submitted Division Three  
June 23, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Leave to appeal denied by People v. Samuels, 397 Mich. 861, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 818 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Kent, Stuart Hoffius, J.



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, appealed as of right from his jury convictions in a trial court (Michigan) for assault with intent to do great bodily harm less than murder, a violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.84, and armed robbery, a violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.529. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment and to 6 to 10 years on the respective convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant surrendered and was held on charges stemming from an armed robbery of a store during which the store's proprietor was shot and seriously wounded. A hearing was held and the juvenile court waived jurisdiction to the circuit court. During trial it was disclosed that the victim of the robbery saw the three men who robbed him talking to a postman just prior to the time they entered his store. The postman was subsequently contacted by detectives but he was not indorsed as a witness on the information nor was he ever called as a witness. Defendant was found competent to stand trial and was convicted. On appeal, defendant argued that reversible error occurred at his jury trial because the prosecutor did not indorse on the information the name of an alleged res gestae witness and did not produce the witness at trial. The court remanded for an evidentiary hearing to determine if the witness was a res gestae witness and if his testimony was cumulative. There was no showing whether the mailman witnessed the commission of the crime. Because there was a rebuttable presumption that he was a res gestae witness, the prosecution was required to prove otherwise.


OUTCOME: The court remanded for an evidentiary hearing to determine if a witness was a res gestae witness and if his testimony was cumulative. The court held that if the trial court determined that the witness was not a res gestae witness or determined that his testimony would have been merely cumulative, the convictions were affirmed. The court held that if both were found to be the case, defendant was entitled to a new trial.

 

2046 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People of Ferndale v. Palazzolo


Docket No. 21302


Court of Appeals of Michigan


62 Mich. App. 140; 233 N.W.2d 216; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1039


April 17, 1975, Submitted Division Two  
June 11, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 395 Mich   .
Leave to appeal denied by City of Ferndale v. Palazzolo, 395 Mich. 807, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 738 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Oakland, James S. Thorburn, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Oakland County Circuit Court (Michigan), which convicted him of maintaining a pinball machine contrary to Ferndale, Mich., Ordinance 200, § 2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of maintaining a pinball machine in violation of § 2. The circuit court affirmed his conviction. Defendant argued that § 2 was vague and ambiguous and that the classifications created by § 2 were arbitrary and unreasonable and violated the equal protection clauses of the United States and Michigan Constitutions. The court concluded that the prosecution failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that any opportunity to win a free replay even existed and therefore there could not be any gambling involved. The court further concluded that § 2 was vague and ambiguous because, in light of the changes which had taken place in the field of coin-operated amusement machines in the 30 years since § 2 was enacted, it did not inform the citizen with reasonable precision which acts it intended to prohibit. Section 2 also violated equal protection of the laws. The court reasoned that pinball and bowling, which was exempted under § 2, was very similar to the game of pinball as played on defendant's machine because both games allowed players with sufficiently high scores a free throw of the ball.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for maintaining a pinball machine contrary to a city ordinance.

 

2047 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Chippewa Valley Schools v. Hill


Docket No. 20494


Court of Appeals of Michigan


62 Mich. App. 116; 233 N.W.2d 208; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1036; 90 L.R.R.M. 2976


April 9, 1975, Submitted Division Two  
June 11, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 395 Mich   .
Leave to appeal denied by Chippewa Valley Schs v. Hill, 395 Mich. 806, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 698 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Macomb, Howard R. Carroll, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school district filed a motion pursuant to Mich. Gen. Ct. R. 769.9(1)(c) (1963) for vacation of an arbitrator's award that sustained the grievance of defendants, a female teacher and the teachers' association. The teacher and the association filed for a confirmation of the award pursuant to Mich. Gen. Ct. R. 769.8 (1963). The circuit court (Michigan) entered an order confirming the award, and the district appealed.


OVERVIEW: The collective bargaining agreement between the district and the association contained a procedure to follow for grievances filed by teachers, the final step of which was arbitration. The teacher requested maternity leave at the beginning of the next school year, which was granted. The teacher delivered her baby a week before the end of current school year. The district advised her that her leave began as of the date of delivery and that she could not use accumulated sick leave to cover the last week of school. The arbitrator found for the teacher, and the circuit court affirmed. The district alleged that the circuit court erred in refusing to vacate the award because the arbitrator exceeded his power. The court affirmed, holding that the issue of sick leave was part of the subject matter of the agreement and that the arbitrator did not exceed his powers by rendering a decision on the issue of sick leave. Even if the court were constrained to believe that the agreement excluded sick benefits for normal pregnancy, by implication, the court would not substitute its judgment for that of the arbitrator because the parties agreed to be bound by the decision of the arbitrator.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's decision, which entered an order confirming the arbitrator's award in favor of the teacher and the association.

 

2048 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Gargagliano v. Secretary of State


Docket No. 19759


Court of Appeals of Michigan


62 Mich. App. 1; 233 N.W.2d 159; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1024


January 14, 1975, Submitted Division Three  
June 10, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Kent, John T. Letts, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant secretary of state (state) appealed a judgment of the Kent County Circuit Court (Michigan), which entered a declaratory judgment and permanent injunction against the state in plaintiff patient's action challenging the constitutionality of a statute under which the patient's driver's license was suspended.


OVERVIEW: When a patient was released from a state hospital and placed on convalescent status, the hospital superintendent notified the state of the patient's status pursuant to § 303a of the Michigan Vehicle Code, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 257.303a (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 9.2003(1)). Shortly thereafter, the patient received notice from the department that her operator's license would be suspended indefinitely and would remain suspended until she met the requirements of the licensing authority. The patient brought her action against the state claiming that § 303a violated the Fourteenth Amendment. The patient claimed that, at the time the notice was sent, she was still hospitalized under the terms of § 303a. The trial court found in favor of the patient. On appeal, the court affirmed. When the patient was released, she was on convalescent status. Under state law, a person on convalescent status remained in the legal custody of the hospital. The court found that § 303a was unconstitutional because it failed to accord a hearing prior to the suspension of a driver's license, and that the patient's license was wrongly suspended. The post-suspension appeal that the state made available was meaningless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for the patient.

 

2049 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Ed Zaagman, Inc. v. Kentwood


Docket No. 19381


Court of Appeals of Michigan


61 Mich. App. 693; 233 N.W.2d 146; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1585


April 10, 1975, Submitted Division Three  
June 10, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by, in part Ed Zaagman v. City of Kentwood, 395 Mich. 814, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 720 (1975)
Affirmed by Ed Zaagman, Inc. v. Kentwood, 406 Mich. 137, 277 N.W.2d 475, 1979 Mich. LEXIS 353 (1979)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Kent, George V. Boucher, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of the judgment of a trial court (Michigan), which enjoined the city from enforcing a zoning ordinance as applied to appellee developer's mobile home park.


OVERVIEW: The issue on appeal concerned whether the land in question was suited for the uses specified by the zoning ordinance. The trial court ruled in the developer's favor and held that no reasonable and substantial relationship existed between the city's classification placed on the developer's property and the general public health, safety, welfare, and morals. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the trial court erred in enjoining the enforcement of the zoning ordinance, as applied to plaintiff's proposed mobile home park. The court held that to invalidate a zoning ordinance, the developer had to prove that the ordinance in question denied him a specific constitutional right and thus was unreasonable. The court held that when the burden of proof was placed upon the developer, where it belonged, then it was clear that the developer failed to establish that no reasonable relationship existed between the factors such as density, traffic conditions, fire hazards, etc., and the zoning ordinance and that the developer did not show that the ordinance did not bear a direct and substantial relationship to the preservation of public health, morals, safety, and general welfare.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the case to the trial court.

 

2050 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Rogers v. Board of Education


Docket No. 19378


Court of Appeals of Michigan


61 Mich. App. 682; 233 N.W.2d 141; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1584


February 14, 1975, Submitted Division One  
June 10, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Leave to appeal denied by Rogers v. Trentox Bd. of Educ., 395 Mich. 818, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 701 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, Nathan J. Kaufman, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tenured teacher sought review of a judgment from the circuit court (Michigan), which affirmed the Teacher Tenure Commission's decision to enforce an involuntary leave of absence imposed by defendant school board but also allowed additional days of income protection benefits pursuant to a collective bargaining agreement. The school board cross-appealed the allowance of additional days of income.


OVERVIEW: The school board placed the teacher on an involuntary leave of absence in October for the remainder of the school year due to her excessive absences related to health problems. After the teacher exercised her statutory right to a hearing, the school board affirmed its original decision, and the Commission and the trial court subsequently affirmed the school board's decision. On appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 38.112 did not require a pretermination hearing and that imposition of the involuntary leave could precede a hearing. At the subsequent hearing, the teacher had failed to demonstrate her ability to return to work as of the date of the involuntary leave. There was no constitutional requirement for a prior hearing because the teacher's property interests were created by statute and, thus, her substantive rights were inextricably intertwined with the limitations on the procedures employed in determining that right. The school board acted in a manner to provide the students with a stable educational program after they endured six weeks of substitute teachers and educational disruption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, in part, upholding the imposition of the involuntary leave of absence but reversed the allowance of additional income protection to the teacher.

National Used Cars, Inc. v. Kalamazoo


Docket No. 21175


Court of Appeals of Michigan


61 Mich. App. 520; 233 N.W.2d 64; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1558


April 10, 1975, Submitted Division Three  
May 30, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Kalamazoo, Lucien F. Sweet, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff junkyard appealed an order from the Kalamazoo County Circuit Court (Michigan), which denied the junkyard's motion to amend its complaint and granted defendant city's motion for summary judgment. The junkyard had brought an action against the city and alleged that Kalamazoo, Mich., Ordinance 509 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted ordinance 509, which regulated the operation of junkyards within the city limits, under the authority of the Home Rule Cities Act, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 117.1 et seq. (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 5.2071 et seq.)). The junkyard challenged the constitutionality of the ordinance. The trial court denied the junkyard's motion to amend its complaint, and it granted the city's motion for summary judgment. The junkyard appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part the decision of the trial court. The court remanded the case. The court held that the ordinance was valid, and that it could be upheld on aesthetic grounds alone. The court ruled that a community's desire to enhance the scenic beauty of its neighborhoods by keeping junkyards concealed from view was clearly a legitimate feature of the public welfare. However, the court held that the trial court erred when it denied the junkyard's motion to amend its complaint. The court found that the city would not have been prejudiced by the amendment. The court ruled that in the absence of a showing of either bad faith or actual prejudice, mere delay did not warrant denial of the junkyard's motion to amend.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part the decision of the trial court, which found that an ordinance was constitutional, but reversed the in part the decision of the trial court, which had denied the junkyard's motion to amended its complaint. The court remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

2053 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Farris


Docket No. 20329


Court of Appeals of Michigan


61 Mich. App. 417; 232 N.W.2d 723; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1545


January 16, 1975, Submitted Division Two  
May 29, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Monroe, James J. Kelly, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the trial court (Michigan), which convicted defendant of possessing a controlled substance, marijuana, with intent to deliver pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 335.341(1)(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial judge erroneously failed to determine the factual basis for the plea since there was nothing other than the two ounce presumption to indicate that he intended to deliver the marijuana. The State claimed that, because of the amount involved, the intent to deliver was readily inferable. The trial judge did not infer the intent to deliver from the large quantity possessed, but instead, the statutory presumption was on the trial judge's mind at the plea taking and at sentencing. The record revealed that the attention of the trial judge focused on the amount involved and not on defendant's intent. The trial judge impermissibly considered the quantity as a substitute for the element of intent. It was improper for the plea taking judge to presume intent solely from the fact that more than two ounces were possessed. The record did not reveal the factual basis for a finding of specific intent to deliver.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the decision of the trial court.

People v. Spencer


Docket No. 20159


Court of Appeals of Michigan


61 Mich. App. 392; 232 N.W.2d 413; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1542


April 9, 1975, Submitted Division Three  
May 29, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Kent, George V. Boucher, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the decision of the trial court (Michigan), which entered a jury verdict convicting defendants of concealing stolen property under Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.535.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were tried before a jury on charges of concealing stolen property in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.535. The jury found defendants guilty, and the trial court sentenced defendants to prison. Defendant argued that Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.535 was unconstitutionally vague because the maximum sentence for the commission of the crime was dependent upon the manner in which the goods were stolen. Defendant also claimed that the trial court committed reversible error by not informing defendants of the consequences of testifying. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court found that defendants failed to raise the constitutional issue before the trial court. The court found that the trial court instructed defendants of the consequences of testifying. The court held that the appointment of one attorney to represent both defendants was not inherent error and only became improper if the interests of defendants conflicted. The court concluded that the record did not prove the existence of any conflict and the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which convicted defendants of concealing stolen property.

Hart v. Wayne County


Docket No. 19285


Court of Appeals of Michigan


61 Mich. App. 188; 232 N.W.2d 678; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1517


December 9, 1974, Submitted Division One  
May 28, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 394 Mich 780.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, Blair Moody, Jr., J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought review of the decision of the trial court, Wayne County (Michigan), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant county on the taxpayer's complaint challenging a statute providing funding for a portion of the salaries of the city court judges.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer filed suit against the county, challenging the practice of the county funding portions of the salaries of the city court judges. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the county and the taxpayer appealed. The taxpayer was a resident of the county but not a resident of the city. He was required to pay, through taxes, for a portion of the judges' salaries. The county funded the judges' salaries pursuant to a local act. The court found that the county voters living outside of the city did not vote in the referendum which resulted in the apparent adoption of the local act because the election was restricted to the qualified electors of the city. The court held that the local action affected the voters of the county in a way that required their participation in a referendum election. Because only the city residents voted in the election purporting to adopt the local act, the local act was unconstitutionally adopted, and, therefore void. The trial court should have granted summary judgment in favor of the taxpayer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and entered summary judgment in favor of the taxpayer.

People v. Rodriguez


Docket No. 17610


Court of Appeals of Michigan


61 Mich. App. 42; 232 N.W.2d 293; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1502


February 10, 1975, Submitted Division Two  
May 27, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Oakland, William P. Hampton, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of a trial court of Oakland County (Michigan), which denied his motion to withdraw his guilty plea. Defendant was convicted of possession of marijuana with intent to distribute contrary to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 335.341 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 18.1070(41)).


OVERVIEW: When defendant was arrested he was in possession of 600 pounds of marijuana and he admitted delivery to co-defendants. Immediately after accepting his plea, the trial court entered an order of nolle prosequi against one co-defendant. Defendant sought to withdraw his plea on the ground that the state had promised him leniency and probation. The trial court denied his motion. On appeal, the state denied any promises and asserted that defendant's post-conviction claim was totally inconsistent with his statement at plea-taking. The court affirmed the constitutionality of the Controlled Substances Act (act), Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 335.301 et seq. (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 18.1070(1) et seq.) and found that defendant's plea was not motivated by a subsequently invalidated presumption of delivery under § 41(2) of the act, but was motivated by the endorsement of the res gestae witness. However, the court remanded for a determination of whether the state had promised leniency and whether defendant had reason to believe the promise. The trial court's hearing on his motion had been held and decided on the same day, with no evidence other than the affidavits of defendant and the prosecutor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the constitutionality of the Controlled Substances Act and the validity of defendant's guilty plea insofar as it had not relied on the subsequently invalidated presumption of delivery. The court remanded to the trial court for the purpose of an evidentiary hearing on the issue of promises of leniency.

Palmer v. Superior


Docket No. 20033


Court of Appeals of Michigan


60 Mich. App. 664; 233 N.W.2d 14; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1483


March 5, 1975, Submitted Division Two  
April 25, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Washtenaw, Patrick J. Conlin, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner sought review of the decision of the Washtenaw County Circuit Court (Michigan), which denied the property owner's request for a declaratory judgment that defendant town's zoning ordinance was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The property owner sold the property to a buyer that wanted to put mobile homes on the property. The town's planning commission denied the required zoning approval for the development. The trial court denied the property owner's request for a declaratory judgment that the zoning ordinance was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court explained that a municipality was not required to sanction the best and highest use of the property. The court held that the decision of the town's planning commission was an administrative decision that had a presumption of constitutionality. The court determined that the evidence concerning the inadequacy of the sewage and school systems supported the town's decision to deny the mobile home development. The court held that the town's ordinance was not preempted nor conflicting with any state act. The court held that Mich. Comp. Laws § 125.271 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 5.29639(1)) authorized localities to regulate mobile home developments.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that denied the property owner's request for a declaratory judgment that the town's zoning ordinance was unconstitutional.

Suits v. Charter Township of Meridian


Docket No. 20973


Court of Appeals of Michigan


60 Mich. App. 347; 230 N.W.2d 426; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1447


March 5, 1975, Submitted Division Two  
April 9, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Ingham, Donald L. Reisig, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff complainants appealed the decision of the Ingham County Circuit Court (Michigan), which entered summary judgment in favor of defendant township and upheld the constitutionality of a obscenity ordinance.


OVERVIEW: The complainants brought a declaratory judgment action against the township to declare an obscenity ordinance unconstitutional. The ordinance made it unlawful for any business to knowingly place offensive sexually explicit material on public display for the purpose of sale, entertainment, or redistribution. The trial court upheld the ordinance and entered summary judgment in favor of the township. On appeal, the court affirmed. The term "public display" in the ordinance was not vague. The court found that any person of common intelligence would interpret the ordinance as prohibiting the display of offensive sexually explicit material that was easily seen by the public. The State obscenity statute did not regulate "public display" of obscene material. Thus there was no preemption by state law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

2059 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ferguson


Docket No. 20078


Court of Appeals of Michigan


60 Mich. App. 302; 230 N.W.2d 406; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1441


March 4, 1975, Submitted Division Two  
April 8, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Leave to appeal denied by People v. Ferguson, 396 Mich. 857, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 512 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Livingston, James Teahen, J.
People v. Ferguson, 46 Mich. App. 331, 208 N.W.2d 647, 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1207 (1973)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the trial court (Michigan), which convicted and sentenced defendant for breaking and entering, possession of burglary tools, and safe robbery. Defendant argued that the bank, safe, and vault robbery statute, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.531, violated equal protection because it penalized assaultive and nonassaultive larcenies in the same manner.


OVERVIEW: Defendant also argued that § 750.531 violated the object-title clause of Mich. Const. art 4, § 24 (1963). On appeal, the court disagreed. The court noted that § 750.531 was enacted to protect structures constructed to protect valuables and that an assault in connection with an attempt to break open a safe was not an essential element of the offense. Thus, there was no basis for finding that § 750.531 was unreasonable or arbitrary in classifying assaultive and nonassaultive violations in the same category. Likewise, there was no merit to defendant's object-title claim because the words objected to were part of the catch line heading rather than part of the title. Finally, defendant's claim that the penalty for violating § 750.531 constituted cruel and unusual punishment was rejected. The penalty provision of § 750.531 provided for imprisonment for life or for any term of years, and trial judges had wide discretion to consider the facts of the particular case upon sentencing. As such, the court concluded that the possible penalties were not excessive even in the case of a nonassaultive violation and held that the sentencing provision did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Knapp v. Dearborn


Docket No. 19543


Court of Appeals of Michigan


60 Mich. App. 18; 230 N.W.2d 293; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1412


February 11, 1975, Submitted Division One  
March 25, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, Thomas Roumell, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured minor sought review of the grant of an accelerated judgment pursuant to Mich. Gen. Ct. Rule 116.1(2) (1963) to defendant city and a finding of lack of subject matter jurisdiction by the trial court (Michigan). The trial court found that the city was immune from suit by the minor because of governmental immunity, consistent with Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1407 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 3.996(107)).


OVERVIEW: The injured minor was hurt by a defective pump at a park operated by the city. The trial court awarded judgment to the park pursuant to the governmental immunity statute, Mich. Laws Ann. § 691.1413 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 3.996(113)). The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case back to the trial court. The court found that although the governmental immunity statute was constitutional, it might be inapplicable because the operation of the park might be considered a proprietary function of the city under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1413 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 3.996(113)), and thus, no immunity to the city would be granted. The court also found that neither Mich. Gen. Ct. R. 116.1(2) for judgment as a matter of law nor Mich. Gen. Ct. R. 117.2(1) for an accelerated judgment were tenable motions in this case. The court noted that the trial court did not order an immediate trial of the disputed facts, as required under Mich. Gen. Ct. R. 116.1, nor could it because the minor had requested a jury. The court rejected the minor's challenge to the judgment under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1406 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 3.996(106)).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which granted the city's motion for accelerated judgment and that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. The court remanded the injured minor's claim for damages resulting from her injures at a park operated by the city, finding that the city may not be able to use to governmental immunity statute to deny liability.

Rossi v. Richfield


Docket No. 19621


Court of Appeals of Michigan


60 Mich. App. 34; 230 N.W.2d 553; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1414


February 5, 1975, Submitted Division Two  
March 25, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Genesee, Donald R. Freeman, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners challenged a judgment of the trial court (Michigan), which denied the landowners' request for a ruling declaring defendant town's zoning ordinance prohibiting the construction of mobile home parks unconstitutional as applied to the landowners' property. The landowners argued that the ordinance was invalid because it was published without the required zoning map.


OVERVIEW: The landowners also argued that the ordinance was unrelated to the public health, safety, and general welfare. On appeal, the court disagreed and affirmed. Contrary to the landowners' first claim, the record established that the town complied with the procedural requirements of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 125.279 by publishing a notice that informed the public of the proposed ordinance prohibiting mobile home parks and that specified the location where the proposed ordinance and map were displayed for viewing. As to the second claim, the trial judge found that the ordinance was related to the public protection and welfare because the town lacked police or fire protection to adequately service a mobile home park of the scope envisioned by the landowners. That finding was supported by record evidence. Given that evidence, the court held that it could not have reached a different conclusion and that as a result, the finding that the ordinance was related to the public health, safety, and welfare could not be disturbed. Finally, the landowners failed to establish that the effect of the ordinance precluded the use of their property for any purposes to which it was reasonably adapted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

2062 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Wahl v. Brothers


Docket Nos. 20185, 20186


Court of Appeals of Michigan


60 Mich. App. 66; 230 N.W.2d 311; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1418


January 14, 1975, Submitted Division Two  
March 25, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 394 Mich 797.
Leave to appeal denied by, Reversed by, Remanded by Wahl v. Leonard, 394 Mich. 797, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 481 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Oakland, James S. Thorburn, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff passengers appealed from a judgment of the trial court (Michigan) that granted defendant tavern's motion for an accelerated judgment in an action for injuries the passengers sustained when they were struck by one of the tavern's patrons.


OVERVIEW: The passengers sustained serious injuries when the vehicle in which they were travelling was struck by a vehicle leaving the tavern's parking lot. The passengers filed an action against the tavern under the Dramshop Act (Act), but failed to do so within the act's two year statute of limitations period. The trial court granted the tavern's motion for an accelerated judgment, and the passengers appealed. The court affirmed. On appeal, the passengers contended that the Act's statute of limitations period violated the Equal Protection Clause and the Due Process Clause. The passengers had a heavy burden of showing that the application of such a limitations period had no reasonable basis. The procedural requirement of the limitations period applied to each and every person who sought to bring an action under the Act, and as such, it did not discriminate against any particular class or group of people. Further, because dramshop liability was an entirely statutory creation, it was reasonable for the legislature to confine liability by defining a time limit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that granted the tavern's motion for an accelerated judgment.

McNitt v. Citco Drilling Co.


Docket No. 20272


Court of Appeals of Michigan


60 Mich. App. 81; 230 N.W.2d 318; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1420


January 14, 1975, Submitted Division Three  
March 25, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 394 Mich 818.
Appeal granted by McNitt v. Citco Drilling Co., 394 Mich. 818, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 631 (1975)
Affirmed by McNitt v. Citco Drilling Co., 397 Mich. 384, 245 N.W.2d 18, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 306 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wexford, William R. Peterson, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administrator appealed an interlocutory order of the Wexford Circuit Court (Michigan), which held inadmissible the results of a blood test for the alcoholic content of the decedent's blood. The administrator filed a civil action against defendant, the owner and driver of the other vehicle involved in the fatal accident. The blood sample was taken from the decedent while he was unconscious.


OVERVIEW: The blood sample was taken at the request of the state police. There was no claim that it was taken either by consent or in connection with treatment. On appeal, the court first held that the blood sample was taken in violation of the decedent's right of security in his person. The court affirmed the order, finding that the owner's reliance on the "implied consent law" was misplaced, as the statute did not give implied consent to a waiver of all of a citizen's constitutional protections. As to the owner's argument that the administrator was without standing to object, the court determined that it was a question of first impression in Michigan. It read Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. §§ 600.2921 and 600.2922 to mean that an administrator who asserted a cause on behalf of a deceased stood in the deceased's place for all purposes incident to the enforcement of the claim, including rights personal to the deceased in his lifetime. The court concluded that the decedent was denied the protection against the admission of the illegally obtained blood sample because he died before his claim could be litigated. Thus, the administrator had standing to object to the admission of the test results.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the interlocutory order and remanded the case to the circuit court for any further proceedings.

State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Shelly


Docket No. 19577


Court of Appeals of Michigan


59 Mich. App. 491; 229 N.W.2d 820; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1370


February 11, 1975, Submitted Division Two  
March 12, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Oakland, John N. O'Brien, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants insured and his son, appealed from that portion of a declaratory judgment of the trial court (Michigan), which held that plaintiff insurer was bound to provide coverage to the insured and his son with respect to an accident in which the son was driving the insured's automobile, but only in the statutory amounts per individual and accident, instead of in the higher amounts provided for in the policy issued by the insurer to the insured.


OVERVIEW: A number of individuals were killed or injured in an accident involving the insured's car. At the time, his son was driving the insured's car. The insurance policy issued by the insurer to the insured provided coverage in the amount of $ 25,000 per individual and $ 50,000 per accident, and contained a clause excluding coverage of the insured's vehicle when his son was driving. In the insurer's action for a declaratory judgment as to the coverage for which it was obligated, the trial court ruled that the Motor Vehicle Accident Claims Act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.1101, did not violate the title-object rule of Mich. Const. art 4, § 24 (1963), that the policy clause excluding coverage of the insured's son was invalid under that statute, and that the insurer was obligated to provide coverage in the statutory amount of $ 10,000 per individual and $ 20,000 per accident. The court affirmed the declaration that the statute's provisions were consistent with the object stated in its title and it was constitutional. Aligning itself with the trend of decisions in other states, the court reversed insofar as the judgment limited coverage to the statutory amounts instead of the policy amounts.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed insofar as it held that the insurer was required to provide coverage to the insured and his son, and was reversed insofar as it held that the required coverage was limited to the statutory amounts per individual and accident, instead of being for the higher amounts provided for in the policy issued by the insurer to the insured.

Kohn v. Wayne County


Docket No. 20349


Court of Appeals of Michigan


59 Mich. App. 566; 229 N.W.2d 850; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1380


February 12, 1975, Submitted Division One  
March 12, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 394 Mich 783.
Leave to appeal denied by Kohn v. Wayne Cnty., 394 Mich. 783, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 436 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, James L. Ryan, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff district judge sought review of a decision of the Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan), which dismissed his complaint for mandamus seeking more pay for 17 days that he was assigned to serve as a judge in the circuit court.


OVERVIEW: The district judge was assigned by the Court Administrator of the Supreme Court pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 600.8212 to serve as a judge in the circuit court for 17 days. For his service, the judge was paid at a rate of $ 20 per day. The district judge refused tender of payment and brought an action for mandamus against defendant county and claimed that he should have been paid the same salary for that period as an elected circuit judge. The trial court dismissed the district judge's complaint and held that he was entitled to his regular pay as a judge of a district court plus $ 20 per day as additional compensation for his service in the circuit court. The court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that only those judges elected in the county were "regularly holding court there" under § 600.8212. The court noted that the paragraph added in 1963 to Mich. Const. art. 6, § 18, did not refer to circuit courts alone and that it was enacted to correct a disparity in salaries of circuit judges within the same circuits caused by staggered judicial terms. The court concluded that assigned judges were never included among the class of those to be protected by § 18.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision against the district judge.

 

2066 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


La Forest v. Vincent Steel Processing, Div. of Letts Industries


Docket Nos. 19084, 19094


Court of Appeals of Michigan


59 Mich. App. 386; 229 N.W.2d 466; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1359


December 10, 1974, Submitted Division One  
March 11, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed regarding the apportionment of liability among the insurance carriers of the prior employer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, certain workmen's compensation insurance carriers and employers, sought review of a decision in favor of appellee, the widow of an employee, from the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Michigan), which apportioned liability among the various carriers, and held that the employers and the carriers were not entitled to reimbursement from appellee Silicosis and Dust Disease Fund.


OVERVIEW: In the proceedings below, the Board had determined that the employers and carriers were not entitled to reimbursement from the Fund because they had failed to sustain their burden of proving that the disease process which caused the disablement and death of the widow's decedent was so common and widespread as to present a threat to the industry comparable to silicosis, phthisis, or pneumoconiosis. In reversing only the apportionment of damages among the carriers, the court noted that while Michigan's Workmen's Compensation Act provided for apportionment of liability between employers, it made no provision for apportionment of liability between insurers. It was for the legislature, not a court, to provide for apportionment in cases such as the instant one. The court held that where liability was apportioned between employers in the case of a disease, the insurer of the prior employer on the risk on the last day of work in which the claimant was last subjected to the conditions resulting in disability was liable for the entire compensation apportioned to the prior employer. The court affirmed the remainder of the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the judgment allowing for apportionment of liability among the carriers, affirmed the remainder of the judgment, and remanded for entry of an order consistent with the court's opinion.

Cooper v. Currigan


Docket No. 18886


Court of Appeals of Michigan


59 Mich. App. 354; 229 N.W.2d 451; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1356


December 2, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
March 11, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 394 Mich 786.
Leave to appeal denied by Cooper v. Currigan, 394 Mich. 786, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 405 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Ingham, James T. Kallman, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant accident claims fund challenged a judgment of the trial court, Ingram (Michigan), which found the fund liable for the full amount of a judgment against appellee driver and in favor of the individual.


OVERVIEW: The individual was injured in a collision with the driver, who was uninsured. The individual then recovered a personal injury judgment against the driver. However, the individual also received benefits from his employer. The fund argued that the benefits the individual received from the employer should be deducted from its liability for the judgment against the driver. On review, the court agreed and reversed the trial court's judgment. In reaching its conclusion, the court held that Mich. Comp. Laws § 257.1122(2) required the deduction from fund liability for amounts paid by corporate employers under the employer's sickness and accident benefits plan.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment finding the fund fully liable for an award against the driver in a vehicular collision with the individual.

 

2068 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Wiles v. Liquor Control Comm'n


Docket No. 18487


Court of Appeals of Michigan


59 Mich. App. 321; 229 N.W.2d 434; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1351


February 4, 1975, Submitted Division Two  
March 10, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 394 Mich 819.
Leave to appeal denied by Wiles v. Liquor Control Comm'n, 394 Mich. 819, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 638 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Ingham, Ray C. Hotchkiss, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant liquor control commission appealed from an order of the Ingham County Circuit Court (Michigan) holding Mich. Comp. Laws. Ann. § 436.17a unconstitutional and directing the commission to approve plaintiff tavern owners' application to reclassify their tavern license to a class C license.


OVERVIEW: The owners applied to upgrade their tavern license. Pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 436.17a, a church within 500 feet filed an objection and the commission thus denied the application. It affirmed the denial upon a rehearing. Neither hotel licenses nor specially designated merchant licenses were subject to denial because of a church objection. The trial court held the statute unconstitutional and ordered the commission to approve the application. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the trial court's findings were insufficient to support the legal conclusion that the statute was unconstitutional. Although the statute, as applied, distinguished between hotels, taverns, and specially designated merchants, there were reasons to rationally distinguish the operation of a hotel from a tavern and the same was true for specially designated merchants. The court assumed that the legislature considered the distinctions and concluded that the restrictions of the statutes were not necessary as far as hotels and specially designated merchants were concerned. The court also held that the statute was not an unconstitutional legislative attempt to advance religion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order that reversed the commission's denial of the owners' application.

 

2069 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Gallagher v. Michigan Secretary of State


Docket No. 16823


Court of Appeals of Michigan


59 Mich. App. 269; 229 N.W.2d 410; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1343


January 9, 1974, Submitted Division One  
March 10, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 394 Mich 818.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Macomb, William J. Beer, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed. On rehearing, affirmed in part and modified in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver filed an application for rehearing, which challenged the court's previous decision requiring him to exhaust his administrative remedies before he sought a declaratory judgment in an action against defendant Michigan Secretary of State that involved his driver's license revocation.


OVERVIEW: The police officer executed a warrantless arrest of the driver for the misdemeanor of drunken driving, an offense that was not committed in the officer's presence. The driver brought an action against the secretary. The trial court issued an injunction that restrained the administrative agency from subjecting the driver to the statutorily prescribed procedure for the revocation of his driver's license for his refusal to take a Breathalyzer test. The trial court also declared that the driver's arrest was illegal. The court held that the driver had to exhaust administrative remedies before seeking a declaratory judgment. The driver filed a petition for rehearing, which the court granted. On rehearing, the court held that the driver's arrest was illegal. A police officer could not execute a warrantless arrest for a misdemeanor unless the offense was committed in the officer's presence, regardless of whether the officer had probable cause. The court also upheld the trial court's injunction, finding that a valid arrest was a condition precedent to the implied consent statute set forth in Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 257.625c; Mich. Stat. Ann. § 9.2325(3).


OUTCOME: The court modified its decision to affirm the trial court's judgment declaring the driver's arrest illegal. The court affirmed the trial court's issuance of the injunction restraining the administrative agency from subjecting the driver to the statutorily prescribed license revocation procedures. The court vacated the portion of the injunction restraining the administrative agency from conducting any proceedings.

 

2070 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Cahalan v. Diversified Theatrical Corp.


Docket No. 20165


Court of Appeals of Michigan


59 Mich. App. 223; 229 N.W.2d 389; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1341


September 23, 1974, Submitted Division One  
March 4, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 394 Mich 803.
Appeal granted by, in part State ex rel. Wayne County v. Diversified Theatrical Corp., 394 Mich. 803, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 491 (1975)
Appeal granted by, in part State ex rel. Wayne Cnty Prosecutor v. Diversified Theatrical Corp., 394 Mich. 803, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 515 (1975)
Reversed by State ex rel. Cahalan v. Diversified Theatrical Corp., 396 Mich. 244, 240 N.W.2d 460, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 254 (1976)
Costs and fees proceeding at, Motion granted by State ex rel. Wayne County Prosecutor v. Diversified Theatrical Corp., 397 Mich. 963, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 1104 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, Thomas J. Foley, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed with modification.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant theatre owners appealed a judgment and order of the Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan) after an advisory jury verdict, which found the owners in violation of the public nuisance act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.3081 et seq.; Mich. Stat. Ann. tit. 27A, § 3801 et seq. The circuit court ordered the theaters closed for one year and the contents sold, and permanently enjoined the owners from using the theaters for the purpose of lewdness.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court found that the owners were exhibiting "lewd" films in violation of the public nuisance act (act). The owners asserted that the act, on its face and as construed and applied violated state and federal constitutional guarantees. On appeal, the court modified and affirmed. The court held that the act applied to activity alleged to be obscene. The court found that the act was not rendered vague for lack of a precise definition of "lewd", construing that term as synonymous with the definition of obscenity espoused by the United States Supreme Court. Under that standard, the court found that the average person, applying contemporary community standards, would find that the films appealed to the prurient interest, thus, were obscene. The court ruled that the films portrayed sexual conduct in a patently offensive way and had no serious literary, artistic, political or scientific value. The court found that the closing of the theaters did not constitute an impermissible prior restraint. The court held that the injunction against the owners was too broad and should have been limited to enjoining the showing of the offending films.


OUTCOME: The court modified the circuit court order, which found the owners in violation of the public nuisance act. The court held that the order permanently enjoining the owners from using the theaters for lewd purposes was overly broad, and limited the order to exhibition of the offending films. The court otherwise affirmed.

Zimmer v. State


Docket No. 19741


Court of Appeals of Michigan


60 Mich. App. 769; 231 N.W.2d 519; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1498


January 14, 1975, Submitted Division Two  
February 28, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Court of Claims, Willard L. Mikesell, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a representative of a decedent's estate, appealed from an order of the Michigan Court of Claims, which entered an order for accelerated judgment in favor of defendant, the State of Michigan, and dismissed the negligence action. The fatal accident had occurred on July 20, 1969. On September 21, 1970, a notice of intention to claim was filed by plaintiff in the Court of Claims. On June 2, 1971, plaintiff filed a verified complaint.


OVERVIEW: The decedent was killed when his vehicle struck a guard rail leading off a highway entrance ramp. Seven months thereafter a letter was sent to the State notifying it that a claim was going to be presented in the future. The Assistant Attorney General responded to the letter, saying that plaintiff no longer had any claim against the State because of failure to give notice of intention to file claim in the Court of Claims within 60 days after the accident. In the interim, the Michigan Supreme Court held the 60-day notice requirement unconstitutional. The trial court found that because plaintiff had not complied with the six-month notice provision of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 600.6431(3), the motion for accelerated judgment should be granted. The court reversed and remanded, finding that the claim was filed within the applicable two-year statute of limitations, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1411(2). Plaintiff's complaint alleged that the guard rail was improperly designed, constructed, installed, and maintained. There was no assertion of nuisance. Therefore, plaintiff's action fell within the scope of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1402.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for further proceedings. The court awarded costs to plaintiff.

In re Kidder

December 4, 1974, Submitted Division Three  
February 26, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, reversed and remanded, 393 Mich 819.

2073 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Stremler v. Dep't of State Hwys


Docket No. 19861


Court of Appeals of Michigan


58 Mich. App. 620; 228 N.W.2d 492; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1740


December 3, 1974, Submitted Division Three  
February 13, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Reserved by Stremler v. Dep't of State Hwys, 399 Mich. 840, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 272 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Court of Claims, Kenneth G. Prettie, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administratrix sought review of a judgment of the Court of Claims (Michigan), which granted judgment in favor of defendant Department of State Highways in an action initiated by the administratrix to recover for the alleged tort liability of the department.


OVERVIEW: The administratrix initiated an action to recover for the alleged tort liability of the department after the decedent was killed in an accident. The trial court granted judgment in favor of the department, and the administratrix sought review. Pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 691.1407 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 3.996(107)), all governmental agencies were immune from tort liability in all cases wherein the agency was engaged in the exercise and discharge of a governmental function. The court held, however, that acts in the discharge of governmental functions, which created a nuisance per se, did not come within such immunity. The court determined that the construction and maintenance of public highways was the exercise of a governmental function for the public discharge of which no liability existed except as created by statute. The court found that the department was not liable for negligent injuries arising from defective plans of construction of public works as long as the injury was not the result of a direct act or trespass of the department. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court, which granted judgment in favor of the department in an action initiated by the administratrix to recover for the alleged tort liability of the department after the decedent was killed in an accident.

Johnson v. Valley Grey Iron Foundry


Docket No. 19612


Court of Appeals of Michigan


58 Mich. App. 574; 228 N.W.2d 469; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1734


December 10, 1974, Submitted Division Three  
February 12, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 394 Mich 769.
Leave to appeal denied by Johnson v. Valley Grey Iron Foundry, 394 Mich. 769, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 393 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant previous employer sought review from a judgment of the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Michigan), which reversed a decision of a referee and allowed appellee former employee to seek and obtain full recovery from appellee last employer despite a redemption agreement entered between the employee and the previous employer. The employee had filed a petition for compensation benefits against the previous employer and the last employer.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked for the previous employer for 18 years. The last employer employed the employee for five months. He testified that while employed with the previous employer the atmosphere within its plant was contaminated with dust and smoke. On his last day of work for the previous employer, the employee suffered a groin injury when a grinding wheel, which he was operating, exploded. He was off one day and then became employed with the last employer. He encountered the same atmospheric conditions as at the previous employer. He began to cough yellow phlegm at night and was forced to quit. At the redemption hearing, all parties were fully aware of the position taken by the other parties. At the time of the filing of the claim, the previous employer was faced with two possible liabilities. First a possible direct liability to the employee arising from the groin injury and second, a possible derivative liability of contribution to the last employer in the event of an award against the last employer. In considering Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 418.435; Mich. Stat. Ann. § 17.235, the court held that only the previous employer's direct liability for the groin injury was redeemed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the board.

Hill v. Michigan Nat'l Bank


Docket No. 18474


Court of Appeals of Michigan


58 Mich. App. 430; 228 N.W.2d 407; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1714; 17 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 310


October 15, 1974, Submitted Division One  
February 11, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 394 Mich 769.
Leave to appeal denied by Hill v. Mich. Nat'l Bank of Detroit, 394 Mich. 769, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 366 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, Michael L. Stacey, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff car purchaser sought review from an order of the Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan) that dismissed his complaint against defendant contract holder. The car purchaser alleged damages resulting from the contract holder's self-help repossession of the car purchaser's vehicle and, additionally, sought injunctive relief preventing the contract holder from proceeding with a repossession sale.


OVERVIEW: The car purchaser argued that the contract holder's self help repossession of the vehicle from the car purchaser pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws. § 440.9503 violated the car purchaser's right to due process of law. The car purchaser argued that his due process was denied because there was no notice or opportunity for the car purchaser to be heard before the vehicle was seized by the contract holder. The court rejected this argument and affirmed the trial court. The court noted that the case law from other jurisdictions and from the federal courts stood for the proposition that private self help repossession did not amount to a finding of state action because the statute was a permissive statute and the contract holder's decision to repossess the was not compelled by the statutory language. The court further noted that the decision to repossess was made in reliance upon the terms of its security agreement made pursuant to a private contract. Thus, the contract holder had the right to peacefully repossess the property and, as the car purchaser had not requested state aid through the judicial process, the trial court's conclusion that the repossession was peaceful was not disturbed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that dismissed the car purchaser's complaint.

Estate of Thomas v. Consumers Power Co.


Docket Nos. 18925, 18926


Court of Appeals of Michigan


58 Mich. App. 486; 228 N.W.2d 786; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1721


June 14, 1974, Submitted Division Three  
February 11, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Saginaw, Joseph R. McDonald, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff decedents' estate (estate) sought review of the order of the trial court (Michigan) granting summary judgment in favor of defendants, landowner and power company, in the estate's wrongful death suit alleging gross negligence or wilful and wanton misconduct pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 300.201 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 13.1485 ).


OVERVIEW: The decedents were killed when they drove a snowmobile between a utility pole and a guy wire installed by the power company on a fairground owned by the landowner. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, holding that they had not engaged in gross negligence or wilful and wanton misconduct pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 300.201 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 13.1485 ). The court held that the power company, as an easement holder, was an "owner of property" under § 300.201, and could therefore invoke its protection, reasoning that because the statute was a codification of the common law of landowner liability, rather than a statute in derogation of common law, it had to be construed liberally. The court held that there was no gross negligence where there was no allegation of prior negligence by the defendants or subsequent negligence by the decedents. The court held there was no wilful or wanton misconduct where defendants lawfully erected the utility pole in the course of their business, and that the statute's disparate treatment of owners versus licensees was rationally related to the legitimate purpose of promoting tourism in the area.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment to defendants in a wrongful death action arising out of a snowmobile accident on the landowner's property. Costs were awarded to defendants.

Tally v. Detroit


Docket No. 16490


Court of Appeals of Michigan


58 Mich. App. 261; 227 N.W.2d 214; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1699


May 7, 1974, Submitted Division One  
February 10, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, James N. Canham, J. Affirmed, 54 Mich App 328 (1974).



DISPOSITION: On rehearing, affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted a petition for rehearing of the case as to whether a city ordinance provided sufficient standards to uphold the revocation of a license, pursuant to petitions for rehearing filed by all parties in the controversy.


OVERVIEW: On its own motion, the court has requested that the parties file supplemental briefs on two issues. After extensive review of is prior decision, the court determined that it was necessary only to address the first issue, whether § 5-4-5 of the Detroit City Code provided sufficient standards to uphold the revocation of a license. The court observed that in its original opinion, it had affirmed the trial court's ruling that the ordinance was not a reasonable exercise of the police power. The court found, however, that upon subsequent reflection, it concluded that the ordinance was a reasonable exercise of the police power, and the standards provided for determining whether or not a license should be issued or revoked did not violate the constitutional requirements of due process contained in either the United States Constitution or the Michigan Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, and reversed the judgment of the trial court, holding that the ordinance provided sufficient standards to uphold the revocation of a license. The court found that the trial court had erred by ruling that a more definite standard was required in order to uphold the ordinance.

Hobbs v. Michigan State Highway Dep't

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Court of Claims, Kenneth G. Prettie, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff executrix of the estate of deceased brought suit against defendant Michigan State Highway Department for damages arising out of an automobile accident. The Court of Claims (Michigan) granted summary judgment in favor of the highway department and the executrix appealed.


OVERVIEW: The motorist was killed when the automobile he was driving plunged off an overpass bridge. The executrix claimed that the highway department was negligent in designing, constructing and maintaining the bridge and that such negligence was the proximate cause of the accident. More important, the executrix has clearly pled sufficient facts to bring her claim under § 2 of the general highway statute, Mich. Comp. Laws § 691.1402. Furthermore, the 120-day notice requirement violated equal protection; therefore, the executrix's failure to comply with it did not bar the claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

Hudak v. Ex-Cell-O Corp.

Court of Appeals of Michigan

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of a decision of a trial court (Michigan), which granted defendant employer's motion for accelerated judgment in its favor in an action for age discrimination based upon violations of Mich. Comp. Laws. Ann. § 423.303a.


OVERVIEW: Following plaintiffs' claim of age discrimination, the employer filed a motion for summary and accelerated judgment pursuant to Mich. Gen. Ct. R. 116, 117 (1963), alleging that Mich. Comp. Kalita v. Detroit


Docket No. 17790


Court of Appeals of Michigan


57 Mich. App. 696; 226 N.W.2d 699; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1651


November 14, 1974, Submitted Division One  
January 27, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, Theodore R. Bohn, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff adult bookstore owners and operators appealed the judgment of a trial court (Michigan), which upheld the constitutionality of a municipal ordinance enforced against plaintiffs by defendant city.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were cited for violating Detroit, Mich., Code § 39-1-50, which regulated the distribution of "sex inciting devices or contrivances," and other related products. They brought an action seeking a declaratory judgment that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The trial court upheld the ordinance as constitutional, and plaintiffs appealed, arguing that the language of the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to accurately describe the conduct that was forbidden by the ordinance. Plaintiffs also argued that the ordinance was overbroad. The court concluded that the use of the phrase "sex inciting device or contrivance" adequately informed persons of ordinary intelligence as to what behavior was prohibited, observing that, in addition to the listed and described items, any "sex inciting device or contrivance" was logically included as a manufactured item, usually made of rubber, which was used by some in connection with sexual activity and which was likely to have a tendency to encourage such activity. The court also noted that plaintiffs were undoubtedly intimately familiar with the products referred to in the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

2081 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


In re Vacation of Plat of Britton Estate


Docket No. 18476


Court of Appeals of Michigan


57 Mich. App. 468; 226 N.W.2d 526; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1615


June 7, 1974, Submitted Division Three  
January 8, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Van Buren, David Anderson, Jr., J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant opponents appealed a judgment from a Van Buren County Circuit Court (Michigan), which found in favor of plaintiff subdivision proprietors in the proprietors' action to vacate a plat.


OVERVIEW: In an action by the proprietors to vacate a plat, the circuit found in their favor. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the proprietors lacked standing to maintain the action because they did not represent 2/3 of the proprietors collectively of the platted land who also owned 2/3 by area of that land, as stated in Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 560.222(2). In so ruling, the court stated that its decision was based on judicial precedent, which held that the provisions of § 560.222(2) required such interpretation because the provisions were conflicting. As a result, precedent held that the language "2/3 of the proprietors collectively, of lands in the subdivision, and who also own 2/3 by area of the lands" required 2/3 ownership of the platted land in order to maintain an action to vacate the plat. This was required even though a prior portion of § 560.222(2) provided that any proprietor of a subdivision or any lot in a subdivision could maintain such an action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause.

 

2082 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Smith


Docket No. 19220


Court of Appeals of Michigan


57 Mich. App. 556; 226 N.W.2d 673; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1628


November 12, 1974, Submitted Division Three  
January 8, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Appeal granted by People v. Smith, 394 Mich. 824, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 682 (1975)
Remanded by People v. Smith, 396 Mich. 955, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 634 (1976)
Reversed by, Remanded by People v. Smith, 405 Mich. 418, 275 N.W.2d 466, 1979 Mich. LEXIS 332 (1979)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Kalamazoo, Raymond W. Fox, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Kalamazoo County Circuit Court (Michigan), which refused to dismiss murder charges against him for a killing that had taken place more than 19 years earlier.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder, but his prosecution never occurred because he was committed to a maximum-security mental hospital as a criminal sexual psychopath. After serving 18 years, defendant was released because a trial court found that the Criminal Sexual Psychopath Act (Act), which provided for classification as a criminal sexual psychopath and that such criminals could not be prosecuted, was unconstitutional. The state then reinstituted the murder charge. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss, which the trial court denied. On appeal, the court affirmed. When a court declared a statute to be unconstitutional, it was illegal from its inception. Therefore, defendant was not immune from prosecution under the Act because the Act was invalid. Defendant's right to a speedy trial was not violated because the delay in prosecution was not the prosecution's fault, even though nearly 20 years had passed. Defendant did not assert his right to a speedy trial, and the court found that the ability of defendant to present his defense was not significantly prejudiced by the delay.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision not to dismiss the murder charge against defendant.
