Phillips v. Flint


Docket No. 17960


Court of Appeals of Michigan


57 Mich. App. 394; 225 N.W.2d 780; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1605


June 14, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
January 7, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Genesee, Donald R. Freeman, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer sought review of a judgment from the Genesee County Circuit Court (Michigan), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff employee in his declaratory judgment action seeking a declaration of the political activities that were not proscribed by Flint, Mich., City Charter § 254 and Flint, Mich., City Charter § 255.


OVERVIEW: The employee filed a declaratory judgment against his employer, a city, to declare Flint, Mich., City Charter § 254 and Flint, Mich., City Charter § 255 unconstitutional, or in the alternative, seeking a declaration of the political activities that were not proscribed by the city charter sections. The trial court declared that the employee could engage in non-partisan activities. Upon review, the court modified the judgment by declaring that the employee could engage in political activity on issues rather than support for candidates, and as modified, affirmed. The court held that the city charter sections in issue were substantially overbroad because they prevented city employees from exercising their free speech rights. The court held that the partisan/non-partisan distinction made by the trial court was not appropriate at the municipal level because most municipal elections were non-partisan. The court held that the employees, like other citizens, were entitled to free speech on issues that affected them.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment by declaring that the employee could engage in political activity on issues rather than support for candidates, and as modified, affirmed.

 

2084 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Salas v. Clements


Docket No. 17779


Court of Appeals of Michigan


57 Mich. App. 367; 226 N.W.2d 101; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1601


November 12, 1974, Submitted Division One  
January 7, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Appeal granted by Salas v. Clements, 394 Mich. 813, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 538 (1975)
Reversed by Salas v. Clements, 399 Mich. 103, 247 N.W.2d 889, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 209 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, Thomas J. Foley, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed from a judgment of a trial court, Wayne County (Michigan), which granted summary judgment to defendant tavern owner in plaintiff's action to recover under the dramshop act, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 436.22. Plaintiffs had also filed an action against the owner for violation of the common-law duty to maintain safe premises for business invitees.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed an action against the tavern owner after they were allegedly injured by an intoxicated person who attacked them. The trial court granted summary judgment for the owner on the dramshop act claim because plaintiffs did not know the identity of the attacker and, thus, did not name him as a defendant in the action, contrary to a "name and retain" provision added to the dramshop act by 1972 Mich. Pub. Acts 196. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment. The "name and retain" amendment was not a violation of the equal protection and due process provisions of the Michigan and federal constitutions. The legislature had a rational basis for the enactment of the "name and retain" provision. The distinction that arose as a practical consequence of the implementation of the "name and retain" provision was reasonably related to legitimate state interests. Therefore, there was no arbitrary classification in violation of the equal protection guarantees. Moreover, the provision did not deprive plaintiffs of "a vested right of action" contrary to due process. Plaintiffs' right of action did not accrue until after the amendment took effect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

2085 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wilborn


Docket No. 15004


Court of Appeals of Michigan


57 Mich. App. 277; 225 N.W.2d 727; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1588


June 24, 1974, Submitted Division One  
January 6, 1975, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Recorder's Court of Detroit, George T. Ryan, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Recorder's Court of Detroit (Michigan), which convicted him after a jury found him guilty of four counts of felony murder.


OVERVIEW: Four occupants of a residence were tied up and shot in the head. All of them died. The premises were ransacked. Several thousand dollars and some jewelry were missing. One victim who was shot in both sides of the head lived long enough to identify defendant as the person who shot him. The prosecution offered evidence that defendant had a suitcase and money from the crime scene in his possession. He claimed alibi. The jury convicted him and he appealed. The court reversed the judgment. The trial court improperly instructed the jury on the aiding and abetting statute without evidence of any other participants in the crime, to which defendant objected. The judge, during the jury's deliberations, and without any questions or requests from the jury, then repeated the charge along with the comment that receipt of stolen property could be evidence of guilt. There was no mention of the defendant's alibi evidence. The trial court impermissibly indicated its belief that the jury should return a guilty verdict. From the evidence it could be presumed that the dying declarant saw his killer, and his statements were properly admitted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded for a new trial.

People v. Phelps


Docket No. 15413


Court of Appeals of Michigan


57 Mich. App. 300; 225 N.W.2d 738; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1590


October 9, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
January 6, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Leave to appeal denied by People v. Phelps, 395 Mich. 773, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 836 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Washtenaw, William F. Ager, Jr., J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for armed robbery, a violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.529, from a trial court (Michigan).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery after an informant tipped off police. Police showed the alleged victim a three-photo display that contained two photos of defendant, and the victim identified defendant in court. On appeal, the court held that the evidence showed that the victim had a sufficient independent recollection of defendant apart from the two-man photo display. The court rejected defendant's argument that he was entitled to counsel for the pre-custody photo display. The trial court did not err in failing to sua sponte order the prosecution to produce the informant because the prosecution had no duty to disclose an informant's identity unless that informant was a material witness. Defendant's right against self-incrimination was not violated by the prosecutor's waiving of the notice requirement that defendant intended to present an alibi defense; the court found that the waiver benefited defendant. Further, the alleged unconstitutionality of the alibi notice statute was not argued before the trial court, so the alleged error was waived. Defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

People v. Guerrero


Docket No. 16412


Court of Appeals of Michigan


57 Mich. App. 316; 225 N.W.2d 746; 1975 Mich. App. LEXIS 1592


November 13, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
January 6, 1975, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Leave to appeal denied by People v. Guerrero, 401 Mich. 814, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 1423 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Ingham, Marvin J. Salmon, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of a trial court (Michigan), which convicted defendant, after accepting his guilty plea, of breaking and entering an occupied dwelling with intent to commit larceny, a violation of Mich. Comp. Laws. Ann. § 750.110.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a guilty plea to breaking and entering an occupied dwelling. Defendant's plea was accepted, and he did not file a motion to withdraw his guilty plea. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that there was no evidence to show that defendant's plea had been involuntary in light of the record of the plea proceedings, which showed that defendant stated expressly that he was pleading guilty freely, voluntarily, and knowingly. The court further held that defendant's allegation that he had been promised leniency was unfounded because there was no evidence on which to consider his allegation. The court concluded that the imposition of sentence on defendant regardless of whether the dwelling was occupied at the time was not a violation of defendant's equal protection rights because the dwelling need not have been actually occupied at the time in order to have been considered a habitually occupied dwelling.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Sears v. Department of Treasury


Docket No. 18790


Court of Appeals of Michigan


57 Mich. App. 218; 226 N.W.2d 63; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 687


November 11, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
December 5, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action in the Court of Appeals.



DISPOSITION: Hearing ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff driver brought an action for a writ of mandamus to compel defendant, the Michigan Department of Treasury, either to return to the driver money seized pursuant to a jeopardy sales tax assessment or to compel the State Board of Tax Appeals to hold the hearing required by Mich. Comp. Laws § 205.7 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 7.657(7)).


OVERVIEW: The driver was stopped by a trooper for speeding. The trooper searched the driver's car, found a pistol, and arrested the driver. At the jail, the driver was searched and money was removed from his person. The driver was served with a notice that the money had been seized by the Department and that the driver had been assessed a jeopardy sales tax in that amount. The driver brought an action for a writ of mandamus to compel the Department either to return to the driver the money or to compel the Board to hold the hearing. The court ordered the Board to conduct the hearing and make the assessment, decision, or order. The court determined that the clear legislative intent of the statute was to allow persons in the same position as the driver to have a speedy disposition of their tax disputes. The court explained that the driver was entitled to a hearing within 60 days from the filing of the department's answer, but after almost a year and a half wait, the hearing clearly required by the statute had not been held. The court concluded that mandamus was the appropriate remedy because the Board neglected to perform its clear legal duty.


OUTCOME: The court ordered the Board to conduct a hearing concerning the jeopardy sales tax assessment within 60 days from the filing date of the court's opinion. The court ordered that within 20 days after such hearing, the Board shall make such assessment, decision, or order as it shall find the Department should have made in the first instance concerning the driver's request for the return of his money.

Foreman v. Oakland County Treasurer


Docket No. 19143


Court of Appeals of Michigan


57 Mich. App. 231; 226 N.W.2d 67; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 689; 76 A.L.R.3d 1108


October 15, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
December 5, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Leave to appeal denied by Foreman v. Oakland County Treasurer, 394 Mich. 815, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 591 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Oakland, William John Beer, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a county treasurer and others, sought review of a decision in favor of plaintiffs from the Oakland County Circuit Court (Michigan), which determined that Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 707.17(1) and Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 707.17(3) were unconstitutional, enjoined the further collection of fees pursuant to those statutes, and ordered a return of all fees previously collected.


OVERVIEW: In challenging the constitutionality of the statutes, plaintiffs contended that the statutory fee schedule, as contained in Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 707.17(1) and payable under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 707.17(3), was in fact a tax or revenue-raising scheme devised by the legislature rather than a fee schedule to be collected as an expense of administration of probating decedents' estates. In reversing the judgment for plaintiffs, the court agreed with defendants that the sum exacted by statute was not a tax, but merely a payment for services rendered to decedents' estates by the probate court. Not only had defendants established that a sufficiently reasonable relationship existed between the statutory fees in question and the expenses of administering the decedents' estates, but plaintiffs also had failed to rebut the presumption that the fees were reasonable. In finding no constitutional infirmity in the statutes, the court noted that the fees at issue represented a reimbursement by a decedent's estate for specific services rendered by the probate court in the administration of that estate, which was germane to the general object of the Probate Code.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter with instructions to enter an order dismissing the complaint for no cause of action.

State ex rel. Cahalan v. Bernstein


Docket No. 18603


Court of Appeals of Michigan


57 Mich. App. 204; 226 N.W.2d 56; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 685


October 8, 1974, Submitted Division One  
December 5, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 393 Mich 793.
Appeal granted by, Stay granted by State ex rel. Wayne County Prosecutor v. Bernstein, 393 Mich. 793, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 1150 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, Thomas J. Foley, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of the trial court (Michigan), which permanently enjoined him from maintaining his bar or any other building for the purpose of lewdness, assignation or prostitution and closed defendant's bar for a period of one year, subject to a petition to reopen upon the satisfaction of certain stated conditions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant owned and operated a bar with his wife. The police alleged that the bar was being used as a meeting place for prostitutes who solicited therein. The trial court found that the activities constituted a nuisance and permanently enjoined defendant from maintaining his bar or any other building for the purpose of lewdness, assignation or prostitution and closed the bar for a period of one year. Defendant argued that the padlock law, Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.3801 et seq.; Mich. Stat. Ann. § 600.3801 et seq. under which his bar was closed unconstitutionally denied him due process because it provided that his knowledge of the existence of the nuisance was not required. The court affirmed finding that defendant's actual knowledge was proven and that he could not attack the statute on the ground that it denied others due process. The police officers testified concerning the prostitutes' activities within the bar. The court also found unavailing, defendant's argument that the cost of stamping out the prostitution was too high, namely the closing of his bar. The court reasoned that this was an argument more properly addressed to the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that permanently enjoined defendant from maintaining his bar or any other building for the purpose of lewdness, assignation or prostitution and that closed defendant's bar for a period of one year.

People v. Balog

Court of Appeals of Michigan

November 26, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Roscommon, Carl L. Horn, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a decision from the trial court (Michigan), which convicted them of carrying concealed weapons in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.227. Defendants asserted that the concealed weapons statute was unconstitutionally overbroad, that the trial court erred in its jury instructions, that the search of their vehicle was illegal, and that the prosecutor impermissibly commented upon their right to refuse to testify.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were stopped by state police for a defective light on the rear registration plate of their vehicle. Two pistols were found in the car and defendants were convicted of carrying concealed weapons in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.227. On appeal, defendants asserted that the concealed weapons statute was unconstitutionally overbroad, that the trial court erred in its jury instructions, that the search of their vehicle was illegal, and that the prosecutor impermissibly commented upon their refusal to testify. The court held that police had authority to stop the car because of the rear license plate light and probable cause to search the vehicle after an ammunition clip was found on one defendant's person. The court concluded that appropriate curative instructions were given following the prosecutor's comments.

Sims v. Firestone Tire & Rubber Co.


Docket No. 18556


Court of Appeals of Michigan


56 Mich. App. 440; 224 N.W.2d 103; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 743


October 17, 1974, Submitted Division One  
November 7, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Appeal granted by Sims v. Firestone Tire & Rubber Co., 394 Mich. 807, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 497 (1975)
Affirmed by Sims v. Firestone Tire & Rubber Co., 397 Mich. 469, 245 N.W.2d 13, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 310 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, James Montante, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant consumers sought review of an order from the Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan), which entered judgment in favor of appellee auto-supply retailers and dismissed an action by the consumers to recover allegedly illegal sales tax charged in connection with services provided by the retailers.


OVERVIEW: The consumers alleged that the retailers collected from them tax based in part upon the sale of intangibles such as the cost of labor and services. The court, in affirming the trial court's judgment, found that the consumers were not entitled to equitable or legal relief. The court noted that the retailers lawfully collected the tax but, because they failed to keep separate books to account for such collection as required by Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 205.52, they were liable for the tax based on their gross sales proceeds. Noting that the retailers lawfully reimbursed themselves by adding such cost to the prices charged to all consumers, the court concluded that the retailers did not unjustly enrich themselves at the expense of the consumers. In addition, the court fund that the consumers were not charged an illegal tax because the tax under § 205.52 was charged to retailers for the privilege of engaging in their business. Accordingly, the court held that, even if the consumers were taxpayers under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. 205.51(1)(1), which they were not, the action should have been brought against the State of Michigan, the political subdivision to which the tax was paid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the retailers.

OVERVIEW: In defendant's trial for unlawful delivery of marijuana, defendant stipulated to the qualifications of the State's expert witness to identify marijuana and did not object to the expert's use of the Duquenois-Lavine test. Additionally, the court rejected defendant's argument that the laws prohibiting the possession use, and sale of marijuana violated his right to privacy, equal protection, and due process. Finally, the court rejected defendant's contention that his sentence was cruel and unusual punishment and found that the sentence was within the statutory guidelines.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for unlawful delivery of marijuana.

People v. Peters


Docket No. 16327


Court of Appeals of Michigan


56 Mich. App. 305; 224 N.W.2d 65; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 730


October 14, 1974, Submitted Division One  
November 6, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Appeal granted by People v. Peters, 394 Mich. 808, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 429 (1975)
Reversed by People v. Peters, 397 Mich. 360, 244 N.W.2d 898, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 305 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Recorder's Court of Detroit, John R. Murphy, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, appealed from his conviction in the Recorder's Court of Detroit (Michigan) for second-degree murder, a violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.317. Defendant's motion to quash the information on the grounds that the waiver statute, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 712A.4, was unconstitutional had been denied. Defendant was sentenced to life imprisonment and appealed as a matter of right. The People filed a motion to affirm.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested as a murder suspect, was taken to a youth home, and was questioned by the police. The probate court judge gave police permission to take defendant to police headquarters to take blood and hair samples and administer a polygraph test, with the consent of his guardian. The polygraph was completed and defendant was advised that he had failed the test. Defendant admitted that he stabbed the victim. A formal waiver hearing was held and the probate judge waived the jurisdiction of the juvenile division over defendant under the provisions of § 712A.4. On appeal, the court reversed. The Michigan Supreme Court had determined that the absence of standards to guide a probate judge in deciding waiver requests fatally flawed § 712A.4 and thus declared it to be unconstitutional. The court held that the retroactive effect of that decision was limited to those cases pending prior to October 3, 1972. Because defendant's case was pending prior to October 3, 1972, and since the issue was properly raised before the trial court and preserved on appeal, the court held that the recorder's court never constitutionally acquired jurisdiction over the person of defendant.


OUTCOME: The court denied the People's motion to affirm. The court reversed the conviction and discharged defendant without prejudice to the taking of proper and timely procedures whereby defendant could be tried as an adult.

Peterson v. Schuitema


Docket No. 18254


Court of Appeals of Michigan


56 Mich. App. 255; 224 N.W.2d 55; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 723


October 9, 1974, Submitted Division Three  
October 22, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Muskegon, Charles A. Larnard, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff passenger appealed an order from a Muskegon trial court (Michigan), which denied the passenger's motion for a new trial after directing a verdict in favor of defendant driver on the issue of gross negligence.


OVERVIEW: The passenger was injured in an car that was involved in an accident when the driver was distracted as he reached under the dashboard to turn off the car's air-conditioning at the passenger's request. The car entered an intersection without stopping at a stop sign, striking another car. The passenger brought suit, alleging ordinary and gross negligence. At the commencement of trial, the trial court ruled the Michigan guest passenger statute was constitutional; therefore, the trial proceeded solely on the issue of gross negligence. At the close of the parties' proofs, the driver made a motion for a directed verdict, which was granted. The passenger filed a motion for new trial, which was denied. The passenger appealed, contending that the guest passenger statute was unconstitutional as violative of constitutional equal protection and that the trial court's direction of a verdict was clear error. The court agreed in part, holding that the guess passenger statute had been validated by the Michigan Supreme Court against an equal protection attack. There was a sufficient possibility of a finding of gross negligence so the question should have been presented to the jury.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which had directed a verdict in favor of the driver, and remanded the case for a new trial.

Ryan v. Ore Lake


Docket No. 18626


Court of Appeals of Michigan


56 Mich. App. 162; 223 N.W.2d 637; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 709


June 11, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
October 9, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Livingston, Paul R. Mahinske, J.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a summer resort owners corporation, sought review of a decision of the Livingston County Circuit Court (Michigan), which declared the summer resort owners corporation act, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 455.21 et seq., unconstitutional by reason of its extreme vagueness.


OVERVIEW: The corporation was started pursuant to § 455.21 et seq., and an election was held pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 455.206 to determine whether plaintiff property owners' lands should be incorporated. The full incorporation measure was passed, and the property owners were deemed to be members of the corporation and liable for payment of dues and assessments. The property owners brought an action against the corporation to void all assessments and liens against their properties and to request an injunction restraining the corporation from enforcing the same. The trial court granted the property owners summary judgment and later declared the act unconstitutionally vague when the property owners sought to enjoin a new election. The court vacated that decision because, although the act contained vague terms, no hearing was held to determine whether the property owners' lands fell within those types of land permitted by § 455.206. The court held that because a disposition of the claim that the lands did not fall within § 455.206 could have rendered unnecessary any decision regarding constitutionality of the act, the trial court acted prematurely in reaching the constitutional issue.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's decision and remanded the case for a full hearing regarding whether the property owners' lands could, by election, be brought under the jurisdiction of the corporation.

Jones v. Shirley


Docket Nos. 18075, 18114


Court of Appeals of Michigan


56 Mich. App. 65; 223 N.W.2d 367; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 703


June 11, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
October 8, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 393 Mich 772.
Leave to appeal denied by Jones v. Racing Comm'r, 393 Mich. 772, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 621 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Ingham, Ray C. Hotchkiss, J.
City of Livonia v. Ingham Circuit Judge, 391 Mich. 775, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 479 (1974)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a racing commissioner and others, appealed an order of a trial court (Michigan), which denied their motion for accelerated judgment against plaintiff taxpayers and declared Mich. Comp. Laws § 431.43 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 18.966(13)) unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers filed an action against the racing commissioner and others, seeking a declaration that § 431.43 was unconstitutional. The racing commissioner and others filed a motion for accelerated judgment based on the taxpayers' alleged lack of capacity to sue. The lower court denied that motion and declared § 431.43 unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the lower court's judgment, concluding that the racing commissioner and others were entitled to accelerated judgment because the taxpayers had no standing to challenge § 431.43. First, there were three taxpayers instead of the five that were required to maintain such an action. Moreover, none of the three taxpayers demonstrated that he was going to suffer substantial injury or suffer loss or damage as a taxpayer from the application of the statute in question. As such, the taxpayers did not have standing to prosecute their claim. Although the constitutionality of § 431.43 was questionable, the court declined to address that issue given that the proper parties did not raise it.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment, which denied the motion by the racing commissioner and others for accelerated judgment against the taxpayers.

Michigan Baptist Homes & Development Co. v. Ann Arbor


Docket No. 17211


Court of Appeals of Michigan


55 Mich. App. 725; 223 N.W.2d 324; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 874


May 14, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
October 7, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Appeal granted by, in part Mich. Baptist Homes & Dev. Co. v. City of Ann Arbor, 394 Mich. 756, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 326 (1975)
Affirmed by Michigan Baptist Homes & Development Co. v. Ann Arbor, 396 Mich. 660, 242 N.W.2d 749, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 278 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from State Tax Commission.
Mich. Baptist Homes & Dev. Co. v. City of Ann Arbor, 390 Mich. 790, 1973 Mich. LEXIS 403 (1973)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff nonprofit corporation sought review of an order of the State Tax Commission (Michigan), which affirmed a decision of defendant city denying the nonprofit corporation exemptions from real and personal property taxes under the General Property Tax Act, Mich. Comp. Laws §§ 211.7, 211.9 (Mich. Stat. Ann. §§ 7.7, 7.9). The nonprofit corporation claimed that its retirement facility was exempt, since it was operated for charitable purposes.


OVERVIEW: The nonprofit corporation operated a retirement facility, which required applicants to disclose their assets and income to determine whether they had the financial means to pay the initial life-lease fee and monthly fees for accommodations. Only ambulatory elderly persons were allowed to reside in the facility. The fees the residents paid financed the facility's operations. The Michigan Tax Commission determined that the nonprofit corporation was not entitled to an exemption from real and personal property taxes under Mich. Comp. Laws §§ 211.7, 211.9 (Mich. Stat. Ann. §§ 7.7, 7.9) because the facility was not operated for charitable purposes. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the exemption in Mich. Comp. Laws § 211.7d (Mich. Stat. Ann. 7.7(4a)), did not apply because the facility was not qualified, built, or financed under the National Housing Act, 12 U.S.C.S. § 1701q. Because of the fees, health requirements for admission, quality of services and accommodations, and lack of access to low income elderly persons, the court held that the facility was not operated for charitable purposes and not entitled to exemptions under Mich. Comp. Laws § 2.119 (Mich. Stat. Ann. 7.9).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order which affirmed the city's decision denying the nonprofit corporation real and personal property tax exemptions for its retirement facility.

People v. Potts


Docket No. 17275


Court of Appeals of Michigan


55 Mich. App. 622; 223 N.W.2d 96; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 861


June 6, 1974, Submitted Division Three  
September 25, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Leave to appeal denied by People v. Potts, 396 Mich. 826, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 397 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Van Buren, David Anderson, Jr., J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Van Buren County (Michigan), following a jury trial, in which he was found guilty of aiding an escape from prison. Defendant raised several allegations of procedural and evidentiary error on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with aiding a prisoner to escape from a county jail. He was charged as a second offender and pled guilty to both charges. The case was appealed and remanded. Upon remand, at arraignment, defendant stood mute, and a plea of not guilty was entered. The People filed a motion to strike a witness because he was an accomplice that was outside of the State of Michigan. The motion was granted. A jury found defendant guilty of aiding an escape. Approximately two weeks later, defendant pleaded guilty to a second offender charge in a supplemental information. The court affirmed because the prosecutor was under no duty to call the witness, notwithstanding having indorsed him on the information. In addition, the trial court's comments on the evidence were fair, impartial, and accurate. Furthermore, the instructions as to the required intent, general intent, were sufficient in light of Mich. Comp. Laws. Ann. § 750.183. Finally, the amendment of the supplemental information was proper, the supplemental information statutes were constitutional and did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment, and the trial court used the proper criteria when it sentenced defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction.

 

2100 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


McKinstrie v. Henry Ford Hospital


Docket No. 17974


Court of Appeals of Michigan


55 Mich. App. 659; 223 N.W.2d 114; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 865; 15 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 1011


June 12, 1974, Submitted Division One  
September 25, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 393 Mich   .
Leave to appeal denied by McKinstrie v. Henry Ford Hosp., 393 Mich. 771, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 635 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, James Montante, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff hospital patient was granted leave to appeal from an order of a trial court (Michigan), which denied the patient's motion to have the Blood Banking and Transfusion Act, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1511, declared unconstitutional. The patient had filed a negligence action against defendants, a hospital and its blood supplier.


OVERVIEW: The patient received units of blood that were supplied to the hospital by the blood supplier. The patient claimed that the blood transfusion was the proximate cause of her serum hepatitis. Defendants contended that because of the Act, they were not liable absent a showing of negligence. The trial court denied the patient's motion to declare the Act unconstitutional. On appeal, the patient contended that Act was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power because the language delegated to unknown persons the power to determine whether or not there existed a medical test to determine the fitness of blood. Next, she argued that the Act was unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed. There was no delegation of power in the Act; it simply provided that if there was no medical test to determine the fitness of blood, the transfusion of that blood would be considered a service, not a sale, and not subject to implied warranties. While the trial court could have to interpret what the legislature meant by "fitness," that was simply a matter of statutory construction, not of delegation of power. The patient cited no authority in support of the position that the Act was vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

2101 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wheat


Docket No. 16357


Court of Appeals of Michigan


55 Mich. App. 559; 223 N.W.2d 73; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 854


June 24, 1974, Submitted Division One  
September 24, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Recorder's Court of Detroit, Robert E. DeMascio, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment entered in the Recorder's Court of Detroit (Michigan) that convicted him of attempting to take indecent liberties with a child in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.336 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 28.568).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the statute on which his conviction was based was unconstitutionally vague. He also argued the trial court's instruction to the jury did not sufficiently define the crime. Also, defendant argued that the trial court erroneously refused to instruct the jury as to a lesser-included offense and that the prosecutor was guilty of misconduct as a result of certain statements in his opening and closing arguments. The court rejected defendant's arguments and affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court noted that the prevailing case law held that the statute was constitutional and not unduly vague. The court also found that the trial court's instruction to the jury, that included a reading of the statute, sufficiently defined the crime. Further, defendant's attorney had approved the instruction and thus had failed to preserve the issue for appeal. The court also found that the lesser-included offense instruction requested by defendant was properly refused because the instruction was not a lesser-included offense. Finally the prosecutor's statements did not cause material prejudice to defendant especially in light of the trial court's curative instruction..


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of attempting to take indecent liberties with a child.

Koehler v. DRT Sportservice, Inc.


Docket Nos. 16601, 16881, 16882, 16883, 18600


Court of Appeals of Michigan


55 Mich. App. 567; 223 N.W.2d 461; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 855


June 13, 1974, Submitted Division One  
September 24, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 393 Mich   .
Leave to appeal denied by Koehler v. DRT Sportservice, Inc, 393 Mich. 776, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 1117 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, George T. Martin, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the decision of the trial court (Michigan), which granted defendants' motions for summary judgment in plaintiffs' claims arising under the dramshop act, Mich. Comp. Laws § 436.22 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 18.993) for plaintiffs' failure to join the estate of the driver as a defendant.


OVERVIEW: After consuming alcohol and becoming intoxicated at defendants' establishments, the driver hit another car in which plaintiffs' children were passengers. Four out of five young people were killed, the only survivor was left a paraplegic. The driver was also killed. Plaintiffs filed an action against defendants under the dramshop act. The dramshop act was amended to require plaintiffs to name and retain the intoxicated party as a defendant in an action against a tavern. One plaintiff entered into a settlement agreement with the driver's estate before the amendment, three plaintiffs entered into a settlement agreement with the driver's estate after the amendment, one plaintiff did not enter into any agreement. Defendants filed motions for summary judgment which were granted by the trial court. Plaintiffs appealed. The court interpreted the amendment to apply to the wrongful furnishing of intoxicants after the effective date of the amendment. The court found that the trial court erred in holding that the amendment was procedural and did not divest plaintiffs of a vested right. Thus, the court reversed the order of the trial court granting summary judgment in favor of defendants.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court granting defendants' motions for summary judgment in plaintiffs' actions under the dramshop act and remanded the cases for trial.

 

2103 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Serra


Docket Nos. 17390, 17391


Court of Appeals of Michigan


55 Mich. App. 514; 223 N.W.2d 28; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 850


April 3, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
September 17, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Macomb, Howard R. Carroll, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Macomb County (Michigan), striking down as unconstitutional the two-ounce presumption provision of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 335.341(2) and finding defendants not guilty of the possession of a controlled substance with the intent to deliver. The issue was whether the presumption violated the right against self-incrimination and due process of law.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a valid warrant, a search was conducted of defendants' residence. Marijuana plants in the yard and various containers of marijuana in the house were seized. The police officers who conducted the search were of the opinion that the quantity of marijuana seized was in excess of two ounces. Defendants were charged with the possession of a controlled substance with the intent to deliver. Probable cause for the charge was based solely upon § 335.341(2), the two-ounce presumption provision. The trial court held that the presumption was unconstitutional because it violated defendants' privilege against self-incrimination. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the two-ounce presumption impermissibly compelled defendants to take the stand in violation of their right against self-incrimination guaranteed by both the Fifth Amendment and Mich. Const. art. 1, § 17, and violated the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. Moreover, there was no rational connection between the proven fact (possession of two ounces of marijuana) and the presumed fact (intent to deliver) in light of common experience.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

2105 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Roberson


Docket No. 17775


Court of Appeals of Michigan


55 Mich. App. 413; 222 N.W.2d 761; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 836


June 12, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
September 11, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at People v. Roberson, 399 Mich. 1048, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 1483 (1977)
Later proceeding at People v. Roberson, 400 Mich. 985, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 697 (1977)
Leave to appeal denied by People v. Roberson, 400 Mich. 847, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 596 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Genesee, Thomas C. Yeotis, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the trial court (Michigan), following a jury trial, in which he was found guilty of armed robbery and assault with the intent to murder. Defendant challenged his armed robbery conviction on the ground that he was not represented by counsel at three photographic identification proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a ladies' apparel store and put a woman's coat on layaway. As defendant started to leave the store, he stopped, pulled a gun, took money from the cash register, and fled. Defendant was later apprehended by the police. All three persons in the store at the time of the robbery identified defendant as the robber at trial. Each eyewitness had previously identified defendant at a post-custodial, pretrial, photographic display. Defendant was found guilty of armed robbery and assault with the intent to murder. Defendant argued for reversal of his armed robbery conviction because he was not represented by counsel at the photographic displays. The court affirmed defendant's convictions. The court assumed that it was error to conduct the three photographic identification proceedings in the absence of defendant's counsel; however, the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The evidence was so overwhelming that even if there had been no identification testimony from the three robbery eyewitnesses, all reasonable jurors would have found that defendant was guilty beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for armed robbery and assault with the intent to murder.

Arlee v. Lucas


Docket No. 15572


Court of Appeals of Michigan


55 Mich. App. 340; 222 N.W.2d 233; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 827


June 7, 1974, Submitted Division One  
September 10, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, George E. Bowles, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff class of pre-trial detainees sought review of a judgment of the circuit court (Michigan), which denied their petition for a writ of mandamus alleging that defendant sheriff of Wayne County, Michigan, denied them the opportunity to exercise their right of franchise in an election.


OVERVIEW: The detainees filed a petition for a writ of mandamus alleging that they were denied the opportunity to exercise their right of franchise in an election. The circuit court denied their petition. On appeal, the court reversed and held that since the detainees were presumed to be innocent of the crimes of which they were charged until convicted, due process demanded an adjudication of guilt before disenfranchisement could have been imposed. The court held that pre-trial detainees who were otherwise qualified and registered were entitled to vote by absentee ballot. The court held that there was no reason to deny the basic right of voting by an absentee ballot to detainees who claimed the right because they were absent from their city or township, but afford the same right to detainees who, though confined, sought ballots due to a physical disability, religious tenet, or age. The statutory scheme was so unequal in its application that it could not stand on equal protection grounds. The court held that denying a detainee the right to vote because of their inability to make bail gave rise to a situation whereby wealth was a substantial factor in determining who had the right to vote.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Oakland, William P. Hampton, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction for breaking and entering an occupied dwelling with intent to commit larceny in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.110 entered by a trial court (Michigan) upon a jury's verdict.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered an occupied dwelling house and took some items of property from the house. Defendant later abandoned the items. The owner of the home saw defendant, but initially described the perpetrator of the crime as having a beard. At trial, defendant presented certain witnesses who claimed that they saw defendant in a bar at the time of the alleged breaking and entering. The court determined that the prosecution did not elicit false testimony from the victim regarding whether the perpetrator of the crime had a beard.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Ypsilanti v. Civil Rights Com.


Docket No. 18991


Court of Appeals of Michigan


55 Mich. App. 103; 221 N.W.2d 923; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 792; 8 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P9731


June 7, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
August 15, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Ypsilanti v. Civil Rights Com., 393 Mich. 254, 224 N.W.2d 281, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 232 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Washtenaw, Edward D. Deake, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed from the decision of the Washtenaw trial court (Michigan), which approved the extension of jurisdiction of the Civil Rights Commission and authorized the Commission to proceed with the charge of unlawful discrimination on the grounds of age and sex, following plaintiff's discrimination action against the city.


OVERVIEW: The Commission originally was created by the state constitution to deal with certain types of discrimination, and the legislature, through several statutes, increased the jurisdiction to include claims of age and sex discrimination. Plaintiff applied for a position as a police officer with the city and was denied a position. She then brought a complaint with the Commission and it conducted an investigation; it found probable cause to support the complaint as to age and sex discrimination only. The city challenged the constitutionality of the extension of the Commission's jurisdiction by the legislature, and the lower court and the court approved of the extension. The court found that the city was a home-rule city; its legislature was permitted to make policy that was not inconsistent with state statutes or constitutionally infirm. The court stated that the city had the right to establish bona fide occupational qualifications, such as the one involved here where only applicants between 21 and 31 years of age were considered. Plaintiff was inapplicable as a matter of law for the position, and the Commission could not proceed with the discrimination charge.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the part of the opinion and order of the trial judge authorizing the Commission to proceed with the charge of unlawful discrimination on the grounds of age and sex, and it remanded the matter to the trial court for entry of a judgment granting superintending control over the Commission.

People v. Fry


Docket Nos. 18034, 18035


Court of Appeals of Michigan


55 Mich. App. 18; 222 N.W.2d 14; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 780

August 14, 1974, Decided

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the trial court (Michigan), which convicted him, based on a jury verdict, of unarmed robbery in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.530. Defendant was also charged as a habitual criminal pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 769.12. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in its jury instruction, in allowing use of his prior convictions, and in imposing sentence.


OVERVIEW: The complainant and a friend were drinking wine at the complainant's residence when defendant and another man arrived. The next morning defendant went with the complainant to a nearby bank as complainant cashed his compensation check. When the men returned to the apartment, complainant was brutally beaten and robbed. The complainant identified defendant as his assailant from a photographic display and made an in-court identification of him at trial. Defendant was convicted of unarmed robbery and sentenced as a habitual criminal. 2111 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Snow v. Freeman


Docket No. 18557


Court of Appeals of Michigan


55 Mich. App. 84; 222 N.W.2d 43; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 788


May 13, 1974, Submitted Division One  
August 14, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Snow v. Freeman, 405 Mich. 837, 289 N.W.2d 925, 1979 Mich. LEXIS 1739 (1979)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, Thomas J. Brennan, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administratrix of the estate of decedent appealed an accelerated judgment of dismissal in favor of defendant hospital granted by the Circuit Court for the County of Wayne (Michigan). The complaint alleged malpractice against defendants, hospital and two physicians. The trial court granted the hospital an accelerated judgment based on governmental immunity.


OVERVIEW: The issue presented was whether a municipally-owned hospital was immune from suits against it for acts constituting malpractice. Withholding a legal remedy from persons injured by the state, while granting one to persons injured by nongovernmental tortfeasors, did not offend the Equal Protection Clause. The administratrix contended that the governmental immunity statute was unconstitutional and violative of due process as a deprivation of a property right without just compensation. The court declined to hold that governmental immunity was unconstitutional. The administratrix never had a cause of action, which was an accrued right, which subsequently could be denied, resulting in a deprivation of property. The hospital was immune as long as it was not doing something for its corporate benefit or for its pecuniary profit. Affidavits, which the hospital attached to its brief, stated that the hospital had always been supported by taxes and fees and had not realized a profit since its inception. The administratrix's complaint showed no allegation that the hospital was operating as a proprietary function. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's accelerated judgment of dismissal in favor of the hospital in the administratrix's action for malpractice.

 

2112 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. McDowell


Docket No. 16863


Court of Appeals of Michigan


54 Mich. App. 657; 221 N.W.2d 446; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1288


April 4, 1974, Submitted Division One  
August 13, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, Thomas Roumell, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimants sought review of a decision from the Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan), which granted defendant claimants a greater than pro rata share of the amount from the Motor Vehicle Accident Claims Fund available through interpleader on the basis of the judgments defendants had obtained prior to the invocation of interpleader by the secretary of state.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had granted defendant claimants a greater than pro rata share of the moneys deposited in the court for distribution from the Motor Vehicle Accident Claims Fund (Fund). On appeal, plaintiff claimants contended that, where all interested parties had been interpleaded, all claims filed against the Fund were to be paid pro rata, regardless of the fact that defendant claimants had already obtained judgments. The appellate court found that there was no showing of a lack of diligence by any plaintiff that would have justified the exhaustion of the Fund by defendants' judgments. The court further found that once interpleader had been properly invoked, the equitable principles of interpleader mandated a pro rata distribution of funds deposited in the court despite the status of defendants as judgment creditors. The court reversed the judgment which granted to defendants a more than pro rata share of the sum deposited in court and remanded with direction that the sum be distributed pro rata among all claimants.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that had allowed defendant claimants a greater than pro rata share of the funds available for distribution, finding that the equitable principles of interpleader mandated that where interpleader had been properly invoked, all claimants were entitled to a pro rata share of the funds deposited in the court.

People v. Johnson


Docket No. 16969


Court of Appeals of Michigan


54 Mich. App. 678; 221 N.W.2d 452; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1290


June 3, 1974, Submitted Division Three  
August 13, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Kent, Stuart Hoffius, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Kent County trial court (Michigan), which convicted him of obtaining by false pretenses personal property valued at more than $ 100, a violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.218.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of obtaining property by false pretenses, and the court reversed his conviction. The court found that the lower court erred when it allowed the prosecutor, over defense counsel's objection, to inquire into the facts comprising defendant's prior conviction of uttering and publishing. Defendant admitted this prior conviction on direct examination, and the prosecutor was not entitled to interrogate defendant on cross-examination as to the collateral facts comprising that prior conviction. It was prejudicial to defendant, especially in light of the fact that the prosecution made a point of including the prior conviction in its closing argument. The court determined that it was reversible error for the lower court to permit the introduction of defendant's prior misdemeanor conviction for possessing a starter's pistol because that conviction was entirely dissimilar to the false pretenses charge. The court concluded that the lower court's instruction as to the defense of alibi was improper in that it did not instruct that if any reasonable doubt existed as to defendant's presence at the scene of the crime, then defendant was entitled to a verdict of acquittal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded the matter for a new trial.

 

2114 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Watkins


Docket No. 14270


Court of Appeals of Michigan


54 Mich. App. 576; 221 N.W.2d 437; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1279


April 3, 1974, Submitted Division Three  
August 12, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Kent, John T. Letts, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the trial court for Kent County (Michigan), which convicted him by a jury of breaking and entering an occupied dwelling in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.110.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of breaking and entering an occupied dwelling. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the prosecution did not waive its objection to testimony concerning defendant's alibi by permitting defendant himself to testify as to his alibi because defendant did not properly plead the defense. The court held that when defendant took the stand to generally deny the charges against him, testimony with respect to his whereabouts was not considered alibi testimony per se and did not open the door to corroborating alibi witnesses. The court held that testimony offered for the sole purpose of placing defendant elsewhere than at the crime scene was alibi testimony. The court found no illegal police conduct and that the shirt and button were properly ruled admissible where the investigation was not accusatory. The court found that defense counsel made a serious mistake in not properly filing notice of an alibi defense, but that defendant's conviction could not be attributed to his trial counsel's mistake in failing to file a timely and proper notice of alibi. The court held that new trial would serve no useful purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for breaking and entering an occupied dwelling.

Detroit & Northern Sav. & Loan Asso. v. Woodworth


Docket No. 18890


Court of Appeals of Michigan


54 Mich. App. 517; 221 N.W.2d 190; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1269; 15 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. (Callaghan) 403


April 5, 1974, Submitted Division Three  
July 25, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from St. Joseph, Robert E. A. Boyle, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants purchasers sought review of the trial court (Michigan), which granted plaintiff bank relief in its repossession action of a mobile home purchased through an installment plan from the bank and which refused to permit the purchasers to introduce evidence of breach of contract as a defense at the show cause hearing to explain their arrears.


OVERVIEW: The purchasers of a mobile home fell behind in the monthly payments to the bank, and the bank sought to recover possession of the collateral. At the hearing on the repossession action, the court refused to permit the purchasers to explain the arrearage by claiming a breach of warranty and that the bank was not a holder in due course. The trial court only considered whether there was a contract, whether there was a default, and whether there was impairment of the collateral. On appeal, the court held that the purchasers were attempting to exercise rights to notify the bank of his intention to deduct the damages resulting from the breach of contract from the purchase price due under Michigan Uniform Commercial Code § 2-717, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 440.2717 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 19.2717). The court found that the clear wording of Mich. Admin. Order 1973-3 permitted the buyer to introduce evidence of his meritorious defense of breach of warranty, and it reversed and remanded the trial court's decision for a show cause hearing permitting the purchasers to present their defense.


OUTCOME: The court set aside the trial court order in favor of the bank and remanded the case for a show cause hearing at which the buyers would be able to introduce testimony of the meritorious defense of breach of contract.

Anderson v. Detroit


Docket No. 18558


Court of Appeals of Michigan


54 Mich. App. 496; 221 N.W.2d 168; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1265


June 12, 1974, Submitted Division One  
July 25, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Leave to appeal denied by Anderson v. City of Detroit, 400 Mich. 826, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 1073 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, Charles S. Farmer, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of a decision of the trial court (Michigan), which granted summary judgment to defendant city in plaintiffs' wrongful death action, which alleged that defendant police officers intentionally shot the decedent without provocation.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought an action against the city and the officers and alleged that the officers, while in the course of duty and without provocation, intentionally shot the decedent. The city filed a motion for summary judgment on the grounds of sovereign immunity provided in Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1407. The trial court granted the motion and dismissed the city as a defendant. The court affirmed that decision. The court held that § 691.1407 did not deny plaintiffs equal protection of the laws even though it allowed lawsuits for wrongful death resulting from the negligent operation of city vehicles or the maintenance of city buildings but denied the right to sue for negligent homicide committed by police officers. The court concluded that the "rational basis" test applied and that the statute had a rational basis for the disparity. The court noted that motor vehicles were inherently dangerous instrumentalities, whereas police officers were not inherently a menace to society. The court held that plaintiffs were not denied substantive due process because the right to sue for a future tortious injury was not property and could be abrogated by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

2118 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Tally v. Detroit


Docket No. 16490


Court of Appeals of Michigan


54 Mich. App. 328; 220 N.W.2d 778; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1241; 8 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P9617


May 7, 1974, Submitted Division One  
July 22, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, James N. Canham, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a dancer and the club where she worked, sought review of an order of the trial court (Michigan), which held that defendant city's ordinance pertaining to the regulation of topless dancing was, with one modification, constitutional. The trial court modified a provision of the ordinance to allow the mayor to deny a license to an applicant only upon proof that the applicant had been arrested and convicted.


OVERVIEW: After the court, in an earlier action, found that the city's code did not prohibit topless dancing, the city amended the code. Plaintiffs' action alleged that the amendments were unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that as a home rule city, pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 117.4j, the city had authority from the state to regulate liquor within its borders. The club was a cabaret within the definition of Detroit, Mich., City Ordinance § 5-4-1 and, thus, was subject to the city's licensing ordinance. The regulation of topless dancing was a valid exercise of the city's police power and the ordinance did not violate plaintiffs' First Amendment rights because the ordinance fell within the purview of the Twenty-first amendment, which allowed the proscription of sexually oriented performances in establishments licensed to sell liquor. After modification by the trial court, the ordinance was not so vague or overbroad that it allowed the exercise of unlimited discretion. Plaintiffs' evidence of an equal rights violation was insufficient to establish that the ordinance was unconstitutional because the classification was not patently unreasonable or arbitrary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that the city's regulation of topless dancing was constitutional. The court ordered that no costs were payable because a public question was involved.

Crampton v. Dep't of State


Docket No. 17878


Court of Appeals of Michigan


54 Mich. App. 211; 220 N.W.2d 765; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1221


June 10, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
June 26, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 392 Mich 791.
Appeal granted by Crampton v. Mich. Dep't of State, 392 Mich. 791, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 424 (1974)
Reversed by Crampton v. Michigan Dep't of State, 395 Mich. 347, 235 N.W.2d 352, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 166 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Ingham, Donald L. Reisig, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Department of State appealed and plaintiff driver cross-appealed from a judgment of the Ingham trial court (Michigan), which held unconstitutional Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 257.322, requiring a police officer to sit in judgment of another officer in the same community in hearing license suspension appeals under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 257.625f. The License Appeal Board proceedings were held void and the driver's license was restored.


OVERVIEW: The driver was arrested for driving under the influence of liquor contrary to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 257.625. He refused a chemical test pursuant to § 257.625c, the implied consent law, and requested a hearing before the License Appeal Board pursuant to § 257.625f. The hearing was conducted by representatives of the Secretary of State and the local police department as prescribed by Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 257.322. On judicial review of the Board's refusal to restore his license, the driver argued that the Board proceedings were void because its makeup violated his constitutional right to due process. He reasoned that a fair hearing was impossible because one of the Board members was a police officer in the same department as the arresting officer whose credibility might have determined the outcome of the hearing. No specific acts of bias by the police department Board member were shown. The court reversed the trial court's holding that § 257.322 deprived the driver of a fair and impartial tribunal, as the evidence below failed to overcome the presumed constitutionality of the challenged statute. As the issues raised by cross-appeal were not briefed, they were deemed abandoned.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court holding that the challenged statute was unconstitutional.

 

2120 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Barry


Docket Nos. 14578, 15930, 15931


Court of Appeals of Michigan


53 Mich. App. 670; 220 N.W.2d 39; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1191


January 11, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
June 24, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 392 Mich   .
Leave to appeal denied by People v. Barry, 392 Mich. 799, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 1054 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Oakland, William R. Beasley, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county drain commissioner and the people both appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court for Oakland County, which affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of violating § 601 of the Drain Code of 1956, Mich. Comp. Laws § 280.601 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 11.1601) (amended 1965), for accepting the fill from an excavation project for his private property. The appellate court also ruled that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted in the trial court of violating § 601 of the Drain Code of 1956 for sharing in the profits of a construction contract. The appellate court affirmed the conviction but ruled that the fill which defendant received from the project and that was transported to his private property constituted the profits in which he shared. The appellate court also ruled that § 601 was unconstitutional, and both sides appealed. The court reversed the appellate court judgment and set the conviction aside, concluding that his property was substantially improved by the addition of the fill. The conduct, however, while clearly unethical and a violation of the state employees' code of ethics, was not a violation of § 601. The legislature intended to make it an offense to receive a money grant or kickback, to share in the profits of the contractor, or to otherwise have an interest in the business doing the excavation. It was not at all certain if defendant's conduct was supposed to be covered by § 601. Even if it were, the evidence, when read as a whole, did not prove the offense beyond a reasonable doubt. The court also ruled that § 601 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's determination of the unconstitutionality of a section of the Drain Code of 1956. The court also set aside defendant's conviction for violating the statute and ordered defendant released.

 

2121 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Reed v. Reed


Docket No. 17889


Court of Appeals of Michigan


53 Mich. App. 625; 220 N.W.2d 199; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1181


February 8, 1974, Submitted Division Three  
May 31, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wexford, William R. Peterson, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant husband appealed as of right from a judgment of the Wexford Circuit Court (Michigan), which denied his motion for a new trial after granting plaintiff wife a judgment of divorce. He alleged that a local court rule precluding him from testifying until the attorneys were paid was an unconstitutional violation of his due process rights.


OVERVIEW: A local court rule precluded testimony from being taken in a divorce proceeding until the attorneys certified that they had been paid. In this case, the trial judge enforced the rule against the husband, who apparently had not paid the wife's attorney fees as ordered by the trial court. On appeal, the court held that the local rule, as phrased, violated the husband's due process rights protected by U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Mich. Const. art. I, § 17. The constitutional infirmity was not removed because the trial judge in his discretion could waive the bar. The court reasoned that access to the courts could not be conditioned on financial ability to pay attorney fees. In this case, there was a proper petition and a proper order requiring the husband to show cause why he should not be held in contempt for failing to pay the wife's attorney fees, which would have provided an ample remedy to enforce the trial court's order. There was no showing in the record whether that order was ever served, and if so, whether he responded. The court vacated the decree and the order denying the motion for new trial, confident that the able and experienced trial judge would set the record straight.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of divorce, vacated the order denying the motion for a new trial, and remanded to the trial judge for further proceedings consonant with the court's holding.

Hays v. Regents of University of Mich.


Docket No. 17702


Court of Appeals of Michigan


53 Mich. App. 605; 220 N.W.2d 91; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1178


February 13, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
May 31, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Reversed by, Remanded by, Judgment entered by Hays v. Regents of the Univ. of Mich., 393 Mich. 756, 223 N.W.2d 276, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 579 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Washtenaw, William F. Ager, Jr., J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant university sought review of an order from the Washtenaw Circuit Court (Michigan), which prohibited it from enforcing a portion of its residency regulations in determining the tuitional residency of students in a class action brought by plaintiff students.


OVERVIEW: The case involved the validity of the university's regulations classifying students as residents or nonresidents for differential tuition purposes. The trial court required hearings for determining residency and the establishment of a refund account. On appeal, the court affirmed as modified. The university maintained that since the university promulgated its now-unconstitutional regulation in good faith, the university should not be required to refund overpayments to students wrongfully classified in good faith as nonresidents. The court held that the funds at issue had already been budgeted and disbursed. The individual contribution by each student was "de minimis" when considered as a percentage of the total tuition collected in the academic year. In light of the balancing of the competing equities in the instant case, the court concluded that the university should not be required to refund the excess tuition collected.


OUTCOME: The order of the lower court was affirmed as modified regarding reimbursement of tuition to the students.

Dukesherer Farms, Inc. v. Ball

2124 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Freissler v. State


Docket No. 17156


Court of Appeals of Michigan


53 Mich. App. 530; 220 N.W.2d 141; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1167


March 13, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
May 30, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Leave to appeal denied by Freissler v. State Highway Comm'n, 393 Mich. 757, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 556 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Court of Claims, William R. Peterson, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured motorist challenged an order of the Court of Claims (Michigan), which denied her motion for a jury trial and her motion to consolidate her case against defendants, the Michigan Department of State Highways and the State of Michigan, with her suit currently pending in circuit court against the county and the county road commission.


OVERVIEW: The motorist was injured when her car was struck at an intersection. She alleged that the department and the state, by means of a defective design and layout, maintained a nuisance at the intersection. The court held that, because the right to a jury trial in a civil case was not an element of due process applicable to state courts, the case did not involve a denial of a federal constitutional right. Because a judgment against the state based on a claim such as the motorist's would be payable from state funds, but a similar judgment against a county road commission would be payable from county road funds, the court held that the legislature made a legitimate determination that local jurors might not be as fiscally responsible in awarding state funds to successful plaintiffs as they would be in awarding local tax dollars. By positing a legitimate purpose for the nonjury trial requirement, the court, therefore, found that the motorist was not denied the equal protection of the laws by that requirement. Because the same facts were present in both actions, and contributory negligence would undoubtedly be an issue in both actions, the court found that joinder of both actions was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in part, reversed in part, and remanded for proceedings wherein a circuit judge, sitting as trial judge in the Court of Claims, might, without jury, hear the case against the state and the state highway commission and simultaneously, sitting as circuit judge, with jury, hear the case against the county road commission.

Cruz v. Chevrolet Grey Iron, Div. of General Motors Corp.


Docket No. 16679


Court of Appeals of Michigan


53 Mich. App. 472; 220 N.W.2d 178; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1159


March 6, 1974, Submitted Division One  
May 29, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Appeal granted by Cruz v. Chevrolet Grey Iron, 392 Mich. 808, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 1055 (1974)
Affirmed by Cruz v. Chevrolet Grey Iron, Div. of General Motors Corp., 398 Mich. 117, 247 N.W.2d 764, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 174 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former employee of defendant employer was granted leave to appeal from an order of the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Michigan), which find that if the age reduction section of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 418.357 was constitutional, it had been properly applied to the employee. The Board made no determination of constitutionality of § 418.357, which provided for a reduction in payments to employees over the age of 65.


OVERVIEW: The hearing referee found that the former employee had been totally disabled as a result of silico-tuberculosis caused by exposure to sand and dust during his 34 years of employment as a foundry worker, and that § 418.357 was applicable. The employee was 66 years old when he was injured. The referee awarded compensation. The employee appealed to the Board, claiming that § 418.357 was unconstitutional because it discriminated among employees on the basis of age. The Board denied the claim and the court affirmed. Viewed as compensation for wage loss, it was not unreasonable to assume that the legislature found that, upon attaining the age of 65, a worker's level of compensation often decreased as a result of retirement, reduction in work, or other reasons. That assumption had been reflected in § 418.357. The employee failed to carry the burden of showing that the law did not rest on any reasonable basis. Those injured before attaining the age of 65 would not be subjected to a benefit reduction at age 65 and those injured after attaining the age of 65 would be subject to benefit reduction. The court found no arbitrary, unreasonable, or capricious discrimination in § 418.357.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.
