DEPARTMENT OF NATURAL RESOURCES v. SEAMAN


Docket Nos. 16365, 16366, 16367


Court of Appeals of Michigan


53 Mich. App. 192; 218 N.W.2d 813; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1124


February 8, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
May 2, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Iosco, Allan C. Miller, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant commercial fishermen appealed from the decisions of the Iosco County Circuit Court (Michigan), which entered three condemnation and confiscation orders pursuant to complaints brought on behalf of plaintiff Department of Natural Resources.


OVERVIEW: The fishermen had three complaints brought against them by the Department for violating the provisions of their commercial fishing license. The lower court ordered the condemnation and confiscation of certain nets, fish, buoys, a boat, and other fishing paraphernalia, and the court affirmed. The court found that the legislature did not unconstitutionally delegate its legislative authority to the Department because the rule-making power of the Department was limited to areas where it was necessary for the preservation and protection of fisheries. The court concluded that Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 308.1b did not operate as an unconstitutional transfer by the legislature of the legislative function. The zone management plan established by the Department did not exceed the rule-making authority granted by the legislature because it was merely a means by which the considerations were effectuated. All three instances involved the use of certain nets in a specific zone, which was not authorized by defendants' license, and therefore, the fishing operations by defendants were unlawful on that ground alone. The search and seizure of their boat was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the condemnation and confiscation orders.

 

2128 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


KENT CTY. PROSECUTOR v. ROBERT EMMETT GOODRICH CORP.


Docket No. 18420


Court of Appeals of Michigan


53 Mich. App. 267; 218 N.W.2d 771; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1137


December 7, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
May 2, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Kent, John H. Vander Wal, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, corporation and movie theater owner-operator, challenged a judgment of the Kent County Circuit Court (Michigan) which permanently enjoined them from showing an allegedly obscene film in an action filed by plaintiffs, county prosecutor and city attorney, pursuant to Michigan's civil obscenity statute, Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.2938 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 27A.2938). The trial court granted a stay of the injunction pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: The parties stipulated to the challenged film's obscene content and to its lack of serious literary, artistic, political, or scientific value. The court reversed the trial court and vacated the injunction. The court noted that recent United States Supreme Court caselaw limited the permissible scope of obscene material regulated by state statutes to works depicting or describing sexual conduct and required that conduct be specifically defined by the state law as written or authoritatively construed. Section 600.2938 did not specifically define the depictions of sexual conduct it attempted to prohibit. The court determined that the trial court was without power to grant the injunction because it was not of statewide jurisdiction, nor was it the court of last resort in the state. Therefore, it could not qualify to "authoritatively construe" state issues. An appellate court of statewide jurisdiction was the proper body to "authoritatively construe" state obscenity statutes. The injunction was improperly granted because no Michigan state law, either statutory or judicial, specifically defined the depictions of sexual conduct which the state could regulate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and vacated the permanent injunction which had forbidden defendants from showing the disputed film in an action by the county prosecutor and city attorney under the Michigan civil obscenity statute.

Shavers v. State Highway Comm'r


Docket No. 17868


Court of Appeals of Michigan


53 Mich. App. 253; 218 N.W.2d 764; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1134


March 15, 1974, Submitted Division One  
May 2, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 392 Mich   .
Leave to appeal denied by Shavers v. State Highway Comm'n, 392 Mich. 778, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 433 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, Charles S. Farmer, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State Highway Commissioner and others, appealed from a judgment of the trial court, Wayne (Michigan) in favor of plaintiffs in their class action seeking a declaratory judgment on the constitutionality of 1972 Mich. Pub. Acts 326, codified at Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 207.102; and 1972 Mich. Pub. Acts 327, codified at Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 247.659a et seq.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs argued that Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 247.660e(1)(c)(vi) unconstitutionally denied equal protection of the law; was ambiguous, vague, and broad; and was discriminatory, constituting state action forbidden by the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution. The trial court declared § 247.660e(1)(c)(vi) unconstitutional but upheld the balance of the act and awarded pro bono publico attorney fees to plaintiffs. The trial court declared that the purpose of the subdivision was to penalize agencies, firms, corporations, or companies engaged in transporting school children under existing laws, along with perpetuating segregation in some school systems. The court disagreed and reversed. Read out of context, subsection (vi) might have supported the trial court's finding. However, read in context with 1972 Mich. Pub. Acts 327, and especially in context with the priorities-in-use section under which the subsection appeared, the purpose of the subsection was to insure the statutorily prescribed use of general transportation funds. So read, it did not offend the Constitution. The court's result obviated discussion of the propriety of the attorney fee award to plaintiffs.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment holding the statute unconstitutional.

Bundo v. Walled Lake


Docket No. 18860


Court of Appeals of Michigan


53 Mich. App. 317; 218 N.W.2d 869; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1143


April 10, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
May 2, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 392 Mich 755.
Appeal granted by Bundo v. City of Walled Lake, 392 Mich. 755, 219 N.W.2d 613, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 708 (1974)
Reversed by Bundo v. Walled Lake, 395 Mich. 679, 238 N.W.2d 154, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 287 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Oakland, Farrell E. Roberts, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff liquor licensee appealed from a judgment of the trial court, Oakland (Michigan), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant City of Walled Lake in the licensee's action claiming that the City unconstitutionally withheld renewal of his "consumption on the premises" liquor license.


OVERVIEW: The licensee allegedly agreed to refrain from presenting topless dancing and using topless waitresses. Apparently for breach of that agreement, the City declined to renew the license. At issue was the constitutionality of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 436.17, which empowered the City to nonrenew a "consumption on the premises" liquor license without a stated reason. Section 436.17 had been construed by the Michigan Supreme Court to vest full discretion in the local legislative body with respect to such licenses, even if exercised in an arbitrary and capricious manner. The court thus rejected the argument that the statute was unconstitutional for failing to provide for judicial review. The licensee also argued that denying his license without a right of review offended constitutional protection against impairment of contracts. However, under Michigan Supreme Court precedent, such a license was not a contract for purposes of the Contract Clause. The last argument was that nonrenewing the license without reason or right of appeal was a deprivation of property without due process. However, the Michigan Supreme Court had held that such a license was not property under the Due Process Clause.


OUTCOME: Following binding precedent, the court affirmed the summary judgment granted in favor of the City.

Mich. Fruit Canners v. Dep't of Treasury


Docket No. 16198


Court of Appeals of Michigan


53 Mich. App. 1; 218 N.W.2d 385; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1096


February 13, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
April 30, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Corporation Tax Appeal Board.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation appealed the decision of the Corporation Tax Appeal Board (Michigan), which issued a determination that franchise taxes were owed by the corporation pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 450.304 and § 450.305 for several tax years.


OVERVIEW: The corporation had plants in multiple states. A director in defendant state treasury department issued a determination that franchise taxes were owed. The department and then the appeal board affirmed. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court interpreted the words "subject to" and "taxable" at issue in Mich. Comp. Laws § 450.305 to mean, as the corporation claimed, that if all of, or a portion of the corporation's out-of-state activities were within the jurisdiction of another state's power to tax, the activities were exempt from coverage by the Michigan franchise fee tax. The court held that the corporation had to show that the statutory formula of apportionment placed a burden upon interstate commerce in a constitutional sense. The court found that the corporation's statement of facts showed a risk of multiple taxation because of the tax assessments and tax investigations made by other states. The court held that since the board did not evaluate the tax liability of the corporation under Mich. Comp. Laws § 450.305 consistent with the risk rule of multiple taxation, the case had to be remanded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the determination that franchise taxes were owed by the corporation and remanded for reconsideration of the tax assessment made against the corporation.

People v. Bennett


Docket No. 16148


Court of Appeals of Michigan


52 Mich. App. 742; 218 N.W.2d 407; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1095


March 11, 1974, Submitted Division One  
April 30, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 392 Mich   .
Leave to appeal denied by People v. Bennett, 392 Mich. 787, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 401 (1974)
Writ of certiorari denied Bennett v. Michigan, 419 U.S. 1072, 95 S. Ct. 662, 42 L. Ed. 2d 669, 1974 U.S. LEXIS 3749 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, George E. Bowles, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Wayne County Court (Michigan), which convicted him of murder in the first degree. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in admitting certain exhibits and in denying his motion for a mistrial.


OVERVIEW: The sheriff's department was called to a residence where they observed a body, which had been stabbed repeatedly, lying on the garage floor. A neighbor reported that a young man, later identified as defendant, earlier asked to enter the neighbor's home to use the telephone but was denied entry when the neighbor became suspicious. A license plate number led to defendant's arrest. Defendant raised an insanity defense but was convicted of murder in the first degree. Defendant asserted that the trial court erred in admitting certain exhibits and in denying his motion for a mistrial. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that there was no error committed when the trial court admitted the exhibits in question because the chain of custody was clearly established, a proper foundation was laid for the admission of the exhibits, and defendant's objections were properly directed to the weight to be afforded the evidence rather than to is admissibility. The court concluded that defendant's motion for a mistrial was properly denied because he was not denied a fair and impartial trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction.

 

2134 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bland


Docket No. 15833


Court of Appeals of Michigan


52 Mich. App. 649; 218 N.W.2d 56; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1082


December 6, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
April 29, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Berrien, Karl Zick, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of a Michigan trial court convicting him of selling heroin without a license in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 335.152 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 18.1122), and sentenced him to 20 to 40 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged and convicted for illegally selling heroin to a police informer. On appeal, the court reversed. The trial court erred by allowing plaintiff to introduce into evidence, for impeachment purposes, letters defendant wrote to a jail officer requesting medical treatment. Because defendant had to go through the officer in order to obtain medical treatment for the symptoms of drug withdrawal, the court found that the officer was acting as defendant's agent, and therefore the letters were within the scope of the physician-patient privilege. The letters were highly prejudicial as they implied that defendant was lying about his drug addiction and sale to the police informer. Defendant was denied a fair trial because plaintiff failed to disclose evidence that the police informer and another witness testified against defendant in exchange for a reduction of charges against them.


OUTCOME: Defendant's drug conviction was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial.

Bludders v. State Farm Mut. Ins. Co.


Docket No. 16048


Court of Appeals of Michigan


52 Mich. App. 714; 218 N.W.2d 107; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1090


November 8, 1973, Submitted Division One  
April 29, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, Charles S. Farmer, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a resident of Michigan who was injured in a collision with an uninsured motorist, sought review of the judgment of the Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan) which denied plaintiff's motion to compel payment of a default judgment obtained against the uninsured motorist by the State of Michigan Motor Vehicle Accident Claims Fund.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a resident of Michigan, was injured in a collision with an uninsured motorist. He sued his insurance company, with whom he had uninsured motorist coverage, and the uninsured motorist. He settled his suit against the insurance company and proceeded to default judgment against the uninsured motorist. Nineteen months after accrual of the claim and after entry of the default judgment, prompted by a failure to collect from the uninsured motorist, plaintiff sent a copy of the default judgment to the State of Michigan Motor Vehicle Accident Claims Fund. This was the first notice the fund received of plaintiff's suit. At this late date, plaintiff sent a copy of the summons and complaint in his original suit to the fund. A trial court's denial of plaintiff's motion to compel payment of the default judgment from the fund was affirmed on appeal because plaintiff had failed to comply with the Secretary of State notice requirements of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. §§ 257.1105 and 257.1118. In addition, the 19-month delay in affording any sort of notice to the Secretary of State was found to be sufficiently prejudicial as to bar plaintiff's claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying plaintiff's motion to compel payment was affirmed because plaintiff was found to have failed to comply with the statutorily mandated Secretary of State notice requirements. Plaintiff's 19-month delay in affording any sort of notice to the Secretary of State was found to be sufficiently prejudicial as to bar plaintiff's claim.

Hobolth v. Greenway


Docket No. 15967


Court of Appeals of Michigan


52 Mich. App. 682; 218 N.W.2d 98; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1087

April 29, 1974, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Livingston, Paul R. Mahinske, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father appealed the judgment of the trial court (Michigan), which held that Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 340.789 et seq. was constitutional. The father filed a complaint against defendants, a school system and a education board, on his own behalf and on behalf of approximately 1200 similarly situated parents seeking to have § 340.789 declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The father, whose child was enrolled as a student in the school system, filed a complaint alleging that § 340.789 constituted an unlawful delegation of legislative authority to school districts. The trial court held that § 340.789 was constitutional. However, the trial court modified the manner in which the school system was operating its program under the statute. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court recognized that the education board was authorized to establish the curriculum for the school system under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 340.114. The court noted that Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 340.789 did not compel instruction on sex education. The court further noted that neither the establishment of a course of instruction on sex education nor attendance at such a course, if established, was compulsory. The court also noted that parental authorization was one of the modifications imposed by the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that judgment of the trial court.

Frost--Pack Distributing Co. v. Grand Rapids


Docket No. 16044


Court of Appeals of Michigan


52 Mich. App. 694; 218 N.W.2d 75; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1089


October 4, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
April 29, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 392 Mich   .
Appeal granted by Frost-Pack Distrib. Co. v. City of Grand Rapids, 392 Mich. 785, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 376 (1974)
Reversed by Frost-Pack Distributing Co. v. Grand Rapids, 399 Mich. 664, 252 N.W.2d 747, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 177 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Kent, George V. Boucher, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed an order of summary judgment entered by the Kent County Circuit Court (Michigan), in favor of defendant city. The trial court's judgment had the effect of denying the taxpayer its claimed exemption under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 211.9(12) from the personal property tax levied by the city upon certain farm products stored in a warehouse.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer claimed an exemption pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 211.9(12) for farm goods stored in a warehouse owned by a subsidiary of the taxpayer. The tax authorities had denied the exemption because the exemption statute excluded farm products stored in a warehouse where the consignor was the owner of the warehouse. The court upheld the validity of this classification, holding that it was related to a rational purpose and was not a clear and hostile discrimination between particular persons and classes. The discrimination was based on the a rational basis by distinguishing "public" warehouses from others for exemption purposes. The court then held that the term "consignor" should be broadly construed and was not limited to those placing goods with another for shipment. The term included those who simply deposited products in a warehouse for storage. The broad construction of consignor was consistent with rules of statutory interpretation because it had the effect of narrowly construing the applicable tax exemption.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment in favor of the city.

Estate of Jones v. State


Docket Nos. 15778, 15779


Court of Appeals of Michigan


52 Mich. App. 628; 218 N.W.2d 89; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1079


March 11, 1974, Submitted Division Two  
April 29, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 392 Mich 770.
Leave to appeal denied by Jones v. State (In re Jones Estate), 392 Mich. 770, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 753 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Court of Claims, Leo B. Bebeau, J., and from Saginaw, Joseph R. McDonald, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administrator sought review of the decision of the Court of Claims (Michigan), which granted appellees, the State, the Department of Mental Health, a state hospital, and individuals, accelerated judgment in a negligence action.


OVERVIEW: The husband, an alcoholic patient committed to the state hospital escaped and shot and killed his wife, then shot himself. The administrator brought actions challenging the doctrine of sovereign and/or governmental immunity on constitutional grounds. The court affirmed, holding that (1) if a plaintiff could not bring an action under one of the statutory exceptions to governmental immunity, then the action was barred; (2) because this case did not properly fit within the exceptions found in Mich. Comp. Laws § 691.1401 et seq., (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 3.996(101) et seq.,), the action could not go forward; (3) the statute was founded on a reasonable basis and was not an arbitrary and unreasonable variance in the treatment of classes; and (4) while the custodian of an insane person could be liable when he failed to exercise reasonable care, he was ordinarily not liable for tortious acts of such persons which he could not reasonably anticipate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in the negligence action brought by the administrator against the State, the Department of Mental Health, the state hospital, and individuals.

 

2139 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Bell v. Secretary of State


Docket No. 15153


Court of Appeals of Michigan


52 Mich. App. 577; 218 N.W.2d 118; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1071


January 16, 1974, Submitted Division One  
April 26, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, Michael L. Stacey, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed a judgment from the Wayne County Circuit Court that denied his petition to restore his operator's license. Plaintiff alleged that he was denied due process under the statute administering the Motor Vehicle Accident Claims Fund, Mich. Comp. Laws § 1106.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed a judgment and held that plaintiff was entitled to the restoration of his operator's license, as he had been denied due process under provisions administering the Motor Vehicle Accident Claims Fund (the Fund), Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. §257.1106. Plaintiff was an uninsured motorist involved in a minor car accident. The other motorist filed a claim with the Fund for $ 6,500. Plaintiff was informed that a claim had been made, but not of the amount of the claim. Plaintiff wrote a letter admitting that he had hit claimant's vehicle but stated that damage to claimant's vehicle should not be more than $ 50. The Fund settled with claimant for the larger amount and suspended plaintiff's license. Under the statute, if an uninsured motorist denied liability, the Fund had to obtain a court judgment in order to suspend his license. The court held that given the limited information provided to plaintiff and the fact that he was not an attorney, plaintiff's letter should have been read as a denial of liability in excess of $ 50. The court found that plaintiff had been denied his rights under the statute and was entitled to return of his license.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and held that plaintiff's letter, which admitted hitting the other car but estimated damages at $ 50, should have been treated as a denial of any liability in excess of $ 50, and should have triggered plaintiff's rights under the statute.

 

2140 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Kunde v. Teesdale Lumber Co.


Docket Nos. 16178, 16179


Court of Appeals of Michigan


55 Mich. App. 546; 223 N.W.2d 67; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 853


January 2, 1974, Submitted Division Three  
March 28, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Amended Opinion Filed September 24, 1974. Leave to appeal denied, 391 Mich 841 (1974).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board.
Kunde v. Teesdale Lumber Co., 52 Mich. App. 360, 217 N.W.2d 429, 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1037 (1974)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed a decision of defendant, the Michigan Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (WCAB), which reversed a referee's finding that the employee had lost the sight of his right eye within the meaning of the compensation act.


OVERVIEW: The employee lost approximately 85 percent of the visual capacity of his right eye in an industrial accident. After he was fitted with a contact lens, the loss of vision was only 35 percent. In ruling that the employee did not lose the sight of his right eye within the meaning of Mich. Comp. Laws § 418.361, the WCAB based its decision on the employee's vision as corrected with the contact lens, not his vision in its natural state. The WCAB contended that the employee could compute his loss of vision upon the basis of his eyes in their natural state only if the lens in the injured eye had been surgically removed. In reversing the decision, the court held that the WCAB's decision was erroneous because nothing in § 418.361, which required an 80 percent loss of vision for a finding of the specific loss of an eye, said that the vision loss was measured under corrected, rather than natural, conditions. The court found that the WCAB had interpreted existing case law too narrowly in reaching its decision.


OUTCOME: A WCAB decision that held that an employee did not lose the sight of his right eye in an industrial accident was reversed. The case was remanded to make an appropriate compensation award consistent with the court's opinion.

Kunde v. Teesdale Lumber Co.


Docket Nos. 16178, 16179


Court of Appeals of Michigan


52 Mich. App. 360; 217 N.W.2d 429; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1037


January 2, 1974, Submitted Division Three  
March 28, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 391 Mich 841.
Appeal after remand at Kunde v. Teesdale Lumber Co., 55 Mich. App. 546, 223 N.W.2d 67, 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 853 (1974)
Leave to appeal denied by Kunde v. Teesdale Lumber Co., 391 Mich. 841, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 818 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Michigan) affirmed the referee's finding with regard to the average weekly wage and plaintiff employee's status as a non-part-time employee. However, the board reversed the referee's finding that the employee had lost the use of his right eye within the meaning of the compensation act. Both the employee and defendant workmen's compensation insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: In 1969, the employee was struck in the right eye by an object while he was cutting lumber in his employer's sawmill. In 1926, the employee lost all the vision of his left eye as a result of an automobile accident. Owing to the work-related injury in 1969, the employee lost almost 85 percent of the visual capacity of his right eye. Although the visual capacity was corrected somewhat by wearing a contact lens in the right eye, the employee was only able to wear the lens for two hours per day. The court reversed the board's determination that the employee had not lost the use of his right eye but affirmed the judgment in all other respects. The court held the board incorrectly determined that the employee had not sustained a specific loss of his right on the basis of his corrected vision rather than natural vision because such determination should have been based on natural vision. However, the board did correctly construe Michigan Comp. Laws Ann. § 418.371 pertaining to part-time employment in its determination of the average weekly wage because the employee was employed on a work-available basis. Also, Michigan Comp. Laws Ann. § 412.9 (amended 1968) was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the board's reversal of the referee's that the employee had lost the use of his right eye within the meaning of the compensation act. The board was instructed to reinstate the referee's finding that the plaintiff has suffered the specific loss of his right eye and to make an appropriate compensation award consistent with the opinion. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

Graber v. Kniola

Court of Appeals of Michigan


52 Mich. App. 269; 216 N.W.2d 925; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1024


February 7, 1974, Submitted Division Three  
March 27, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Berrien, William S. White, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff students sought review of a decision from a Michigan trial court, which held that the hair code provision of defendant school authorities was valid.


OVERVIEW: The school authorities had a dress code policy that specified that male student's hair could not exceed a specific length. The students brought an action to have that policy declared invalid. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the school authorities and held that the provision was valid. On appeal, the court reversed. People v. Collins


Docket No. 16059


Court of Appeals of Michigan


52 Mich. App. 332; 217 N.W.2d 119; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1033


December 6, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
March 27, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Clinton, Leo W. Corkin, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was arrested without a warrant for the murder of a grocery-store owner. The following morning, pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 764.13, a police trooper signed a complaint charging defendant with felony murder. Later, an information was filed in the Clinton County Circuit Court (Michigan). The trial court overruled defendant's motion to quash the information and defendant was convicted of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issue was whether a conviction based upon an information and belief complaint, written as an eyewitness complaint, is fatally defective when the complaint failed to allege the grounds upon which the complainant's information and belief were based. Defendant contended that the warrant was unconstitutionally issued since it was based on a complaint which was conclusory and which failed to identify sources of information. The court found that the complaint was made upon the knowledge of the trooper and defendant was precluded from impeaching the complaint by showing that the trooper was without personal knowledge of the commission of the crime or defendant's identity. The court found that once the trial court obtained jurisdiction over defendant, proof of an invalid arrest warrant did not divest the trial court of jurisdiction. The court noted that defendant's rights were fully protected and defendant was not bound over for trial without a probable cause determination. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment because the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to quash the information.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Jack Dykstra Ford, Inc.


Docket No. 15893


Court of Appeals of Michigan


52 Mich. App. 337; 217 N.W.2d 99; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1034


December 5, 1973, Submitted Division Two  
March 27, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Ingham, Jack W. Warren, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the circuit court, Ingham (Michigan), which affirmed a district court conviction of defendant of altering the mileage registered on the odometer of a motor vehicle pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.421d, 750.421e.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of altering the mileage registered on the odometer of a vehicle pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.421d in the district court. The circuit court affirmed. Defendant appealed, contending that the statute was unconstitutional because there was a lack of scienter as a required element of the offense and because it violated the Equal Protection Clauses of the United States Constitution and Michigan Constitution. On appeal, the court held that defendant was absolved of any violation of § 750.421d by the general absolution provision of Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.421e. Defendant was in possession of an affidavit, at the time of issuance of the criminal complaint against him, that fulfilled substantially the statutory requirement of § 750.421e. The declarer-signer testified that he inserted the mileage in his own handwriting, that the signature was his, that he knew he was signing an affidavit, and that he was in fact swearing to the verity of its contents.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment, which had affirmed defendant's conviction for altering the mileage registered on the odometer of a vehicle, and set aside defendant's conviction.

People v. Hendrick

Court of Appeals of Michigan


52 Mich. App. 201; 217 N.W.2d 112; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 1016

March 26, 1974, Decided

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the St. Joseph Court (Michigan), which convicted him with breaking and entering with intent to commit larceny, Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.110, and assault with intent to do great bodily harm less than murder, Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.84. He was convicted as a habitual criminal under Mich. Comp. Laws § 769.12 and sentenced to life imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to both charges. He had prior convictions in various states for second-degree burglary, robbery in the first degree, escape from prison, breaking and entering with intent to commit larceny, and assault with intent to do great bodily harm less than murder. After sentencing, the State filed a supplemental information that charged defendant with being a habitual criminal pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 769.12. It was permissible for the State to file the habitual criminal information after conviction.

People v. McLendon


Docket No. 14564


Court of Appeals of Michigan


51 Mich. App. 543; 215 N.W.2d 742; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 943


November 14, 1973, Submitted Division One  
March 1, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Recorder's Court of Detroit, Gordon W. Britten, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Recorder's Court of Detroit (Michigan), which entered his conviction for embezzlement by an agent of an amount exceeding $ 100 contrary to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.174.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of embezzlement. On appeal, he argued that he was deprived of due process of law when he was required to defend against alleged acts of embezzlement that occurred approximately one month subsequent to the date of the offense specified in the information. Further, defendant argued that evidence of an act of embezzlement occurring prior to the date of the offense specified in the information was impermissibly introduced at trial. Finally, defendant argued that he was denied a fair trial because certain statements made by the prosecution during its closing argument were not supported by the evidence. The court affirmed, holding first that Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 767.60 specifically allowed the prosecution to prove the charge of embezzlement with evidence of embezzlements that occurred within six months after the date of the offense alleged in the information. Here, the act complained of occurred only one month after the information; therefore, neither it, nor the evidence of other acts of embezzlement within that time frame, were precluded from consideration. Further, the court held that the remarks made by the prosecution did not constitute reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the recorder's court, which entered defendant's conviction for embezzlement.

Board of Education v. Michigan Bell Tel. Co.


Docket No. 14220


Court of Appeals of Michigan


51 Mich. App. 488; 215 N.W.2d 704; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 936


October 2, 1973, Submitted Division One  
March 1, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 392 Mich   .

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school board sought review, pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws § 340.192 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 15.3192), of a decision of the Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan), which awarded final judgments in favor of defendant utilities reimbursing them for the costs of relocating utility equipment, in response to the utilities' objections to the school board's petition for the vacation of realty to accommodate the expansion of one of its buildings.


OVERVIEW: The school board argued on appeal that it had the general police power right to compel a public utility to relocate its equipment from a right-of-way without compensation. The utilities argued that a taking had occurred. The court noted that school districts had long been classified as municipal corporations in Michigan. The court pointed out that municipal corporations, in the absence of a constitutional grant, had only such police powers as were granted them by the legislature, but stated that a municipal corporation could assume the posture of that power necessarily and fairly implied in or incident to those powers expressly stated. The court determined that the legitimate public interest in enlarging educational facilities was paramount to the continued right of usage by the utilities of the public streets. The court determined that provisional reservation of easements or reimbursement rights in the vacated property had been granted and an interest in property destroyed, and that whether this was tantamount to a taking or was the proper exercise of police power did not alter the fact that the utilities were entitled to be compensated for a loss of a vested property right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the utilities.

United Pentecostal Church v. Steendam


Docket No. 16509


Court of Appeals of Michigan


51 Mich. App. 323; 214 N.W.2d 866; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 911


October 4, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
January 17, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 391 Mich 821.
Leave to appeal denied by United Pentecostal Church v. 59th District Judge, 391 Mich. 821, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 308 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Muskegon, Charles A. Larnard, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff religious organization filed a claim against defendant city. The Muskegon County Circuit Court (Michigan) denied the religious organization's requested relief and granted summary judgment in favor of the city. The religious organization appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city had an anti-noise ordinance that provided that it was unlawful for any person to make, continue or cause to be made or continued any loud, unnecessary or unusual noise or any noise which either annoyed, disturbed, injured or endangered the comfort, repose, health, peace or safety of others, within the limits of the city. Area residents complained that they were disturbed by loud music and prayers that emanated from the church during its evening services, especially as those noises appeared to come from sound amplification equipment. The court reversed the lower court and held that the statute unconstitutionally vague. The court held that the statute had to proscribe an ascertainable standard of guilt for due process requirements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order that found residents in violation of an anti-noise ordinance, and found the ordinance unconstitutionally vague.

 

2151 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Briscoe


Docket No. 14351


Court of Appeals of Michigan


51 Mich. App. 153; 214 N.W.2d 877; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 889


November 6, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
January 15, 1974, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Leave to appeal denied by People v. Briscoe # 1, 403 Mich. 806, 1978 Mich. LEXIS 1156 (1978)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Saginaw, Joseph R. McDonald, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of a trial court, Saginaw County (Michigan), which convicted him of armed robbery, a violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.529.


OVERVIEW: A man wearing a black hat robbed a store at gunpoint. After the man left, a store employee saw him drive off in a car. The employees reported the robbery to the police. Another robbery was reported, and a police broadcast stated the license number of the getaway car. Police officers went to defendant's residence and saw a car fitting the description of the getaway car parked in the driveway. Defendant's landlady had recently seen defendant and gave the officers permission to enter his room. The officers entered and saw a black hat on a dresser. The officers returned to execute search warrants, and they seized the hat pursuant to two warrants. At trial, the prosecutor stipulated to not using evidence obtained under one warrant, but used the hat as evidence because it had been obtained under both warrants. Defendant objected to the admission of the hat. The court found that the officers had reasonable cause to believe that defendant had committed a felony. The officers were legitimately admitted to defendant's home, and the hat came within the "plain view doctrine."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

2152 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Moore


Docket No. 12438


Court of Appeals of Michigan


51 Mich. App. 48; 214 N.W.2d 548; 1974 Mich. App. LEXIS 876


December 7, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
January 14, 1974, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Muskegon, Charles A. Larnard, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order of a Muskegon trial court (Michigan), which convicted him of murder under the felony-murder rule, Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.316.


OVERVIEW: The victim's body was found behind the counter of his liquor store. Robbery was the apparent motive. Defendant was read his Miranda rights. He stated he was framed but refused to talk further without counsel. Questioning ceased. Defendant then requested a conference with the police captain. He then stated he was a lookout in an unarmed robbery. When asked if he contacted an attorney about the frame-up, defendant responded no. Defendant then said that he would talk, anyway, and stated that an accomplice killed the victim. A jury convicted defendant. On appeal, he argued that the admission of his three statements was in error on the basis that Miranda was violated. The court disagreed. In so ruling, the court stated that defendant's statements were voluntary. Further, the admission of a letter defendant wrote to another prison inmate proposing shady trial assistance and reciprocation was proper. The letter, which was intercepted by the prosecution, was relevant on the issue of defendant's credibility. A showing that some jurors may have hard or read the case through the news media was insufficient to show that defendant was denied an unfair trial due to prejudicial outside publicity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

2153 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Campbell v. Detroit


Docket No. 15984


Court of Appeals of Michigan


51 Mich. App. 34; 214 N.W.2d 337; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 685


November 9, 1973, Submitted Division One  
December 28, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, Joseph A. Moynihan, Jr., J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff alleged that in November 1969, she was injured in a fall on a defective sidewalk south of a public street. She filed suit against defendant City of Detroit in July 1972. The City asked for accelerated judgment, and the trial court (Michigan) granted the City's motion. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The City's motion was founded upon the defective highway statute, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1402, and its attendant two-year statute of limitations, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1411. At the time of plaintiff's injury, the street apparently had been closed for some time and was being removed to make way for an urban renewal project. The court overturned the trial court's judgment. First, the court held that even if the street could have been considered a public highway, road, or street, it was not "open for public travel" as required by the definition of highway found in Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1401. Since the street was not a highway, the sidewalk in question was not "on any highway" and was not, therefore, within the terms of the above statutes and their special two-year statute of limitations. Further, the court held that the date of plaintiff's injury should have controlled application of the amended immunity statute. The court held that a statutory right of action for damage to person or property, which had accrued, was a vested right.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

2154 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. White


Docket No. 14750


Court of Appeals of Michigan


51 Mich. App. 1; 214 N.W.2d 326; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 681


May 15, 1973, Submitted Division Two  
December 6, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 391 Mich 819.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Oakland, Farrell E. Roberts, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed from a judgment of the trial court (Michigan), which after a jury conviction, sentenced defendant to eight to 20 years imprisonment for armed robbery in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.529.


OVERVIEW: At the time of his arrest, defendant was a juvenile charged with five other felonies. A hearing was held and the probate judge waived jurisdiction to the circuit court. On appeal from his conviction, defendant argued that Mich. Comp. Laws § 712A.4 was unconstitutional in that it failed to provide standards for such waiver and that the trial court had no basis for determining whether the interests of defendant and the public would be served by such waiver. The court affirmed. Waiver of jurisdiction occurred over two years following adoption of Mich. Juv. Ct. R. 11.1 (1969), which supplied the due process protection that Mich. Comp. Laws § 712A.4 had lacked. The probate judge had sufficient evidence from which he could conclude that the best interests of the child and the public would best be served by granting a waiver of jurisdiction. Defendant had a long prior record with the juvenile court. The seriousness and repetitive pattern of the various offenses provided compelling evidence that the several rehabilitative efforts conducted under juvenile procedure had been unsuccessful. The trial court took judicial notice of available rehabilitative facilities.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Pichette v. Manistique Public Schools


Docket No. 16384


Court of Appeals of Michigan


50 Mich. App. 770; 213 N.W.2d 784; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 984


October 5, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
December 6, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Appeal granted by Pichette v. Manistique Pub. Schs, 399 Mich. 840, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 210 (1977)
Reversed by Pichette v. Manistique Pub. Sch., 403 Mich. 268, 269 N.W.2d 143, 1978 Mich. LEXIS 340 (1978)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Schoolcraft, William F. Hood, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff child sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Schoolcraft County (Michigan), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant school district and dismissed the child's case for damages on the basis of governmental immunity.


OVERVIEW: The child argued that the school district waived the defense of governmental immunity by purchasing general liability insurance. Alternatively, the child argued that the playground slide was a building that was within the statutory exemptions to governmental immunity. The child also argued that the school district's operation of the playground was a nonessential governmental function that denied the school district the shield of governmental immunity. The child also argued that the school district was not exercising a governmental function because the school was closed for the summer. The court rejected the child's arguments and affirmed the trial court's decision to grant summary judgment. The court noted that the school district's maintenance of the playground was a governmental function and there was no evidence to suggest that the school district had engaged in a proprietary function. The court concluded that the legislature that the school district was immune from tort liability unless it had done something for its own corporate benefit or for its pecuniary profit, which was not the case here.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision to grant the school district summary judgment and dismiss the child's case on the basis of governmental immunity.

 

2156 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Lanphear v. Antwerp


Docket No. 15682


Court of Appeals of Michigan


50 Mich. App. 641; 214 N.W.2d 66; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 962


October 4, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
November 29, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Van Buren, Robert E. A. Boyle, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, neighboring residents of the subject property, sought review of a decision of the trial court which denied an injunction against the township to prevent it from rezoning the property for use as a mobile home park and denied an injunction to prevent the property holders or their grantees from placing mobile homes on the property.


OVERVIEW: The neighboring residents of the property filed an action for an injunction against the township to prevent it from rezoning the property so that it could be used as a mobile home park, and filed an injunction to prevent the property holders or their grantees from placing mobile homes on the property. The trial court denied the injunctions, holding that the township was allowed to zone for mobile homes. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the resident electors of unincorporated portions of the township were secured a powerful voice in the zoning of the areas they lived in and was unwilling to second guess the township board's legislative determination that allowing a new mobile home park in the unincorporated portion of the township would serve the general welfare of the community, at least not without countervailing evidence of arbitrary action by any of the township legislative bodies. While publication might under some circumstances not be sufficient for due process purposes, the court found no constitutional inadequacy in the notice given.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court which denied an injunction against the township to prevent it from rezoning the property so that it could be used as a mobile home park, and denied an injunction to prevent the property holders or their grantees from placing mobile homes on the property..

 

2157 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Tomlinson


Docket No. 15944


Court of Appeals of Michigan


50 Mich. App. 655; 213 N.W.2d 803; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 963


August 31, 1973, Submitted Division Two  
November 29, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 391 Mich   .
Leave to appeal denied by People v. Tomlinson, 391 Mich. 824, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 356 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Monroe, William J. Weipert, Jr., J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment by the circuit court in Monroe (Michigan), which affirmed defendant's conviction for malicious prosecution of property under $ 100. The issue on appeal was whether the requirement that the trial court inform defendant of his constitutional rights applied to nolo contendere pleas to simple misdemeanors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled nolo contendere to the malicious destruction of property under $ 100. On appeal, the sole issue was whether the rule that a defendant must be informed by the trial judge on the record of certain constitutional rights applied to nolo contendere pleas to simple misdemeanors. The court held that the rule applied to pleas of nolo contendere because a nolo plea had the same consequences as a guilty plea. The court held, however, that the rule did not apply to simple misdemeanors. The court found that the consequences were less drastic in simple misdemeanors and thus less solicitude was required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

2158 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Johnkoski v. Johnkoski


Docket No. 13947


Court of Appeals of Michigan


50 Mich. App. 542; 213 N.W.2d 856; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 948


October 2, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
November 28, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 391 Mich 777.
Leave to appeal denied by Johnkoski v. Johnkoski, 391 Mich. 777, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 855 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Calhoun, Creighton R. Coleman, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant husband challenged the decision of the Calhoun County Court (Michigan), which granted plaintiff wife's request for a divorce and denied the husband's request for a continuance in order to obtain another lawyer.


OVERVIEW: The wife filed an action for divorce against the husband. The trial was delayed for almost two years while the husband tried to gain his release from commitment at a hospital and while he tried to retain an attorney. On the day that the trial was to begin, defendant asked for a continuance in order to obtain counsel. The trial court gave defendant a three-month continuance. Defendant obtained counsel and the case was reset again for another date, at which time the husband was displeased with his attorney and requested a continuance. The trial court denied the request and entered a judgment for divorce. On review, the court found that the divorce action was two years old and that the husband's neglect could have caused the trial to be delayed even longer. Furthermore, the husband had appeared at the first hearing with counsel and was able to participate. Finally, the court found that the husband's request for a continuance was due to his unwillingness to work with a particular lawyer and that the husband had previous problems with his lawyers. Therefore, the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it denied the husband's request for a continuance.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision that granted the wife's request for a divorce and denied the husband's request for a continuance was affirmed.

Washtenaw Community College Education Asso. v. Board of Trustees


Docket No. 15662


Court of Appeals of Michigan


50 Mich. App. 467; 213 N.W.2d 567; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 935


June 18, 1973, Submitted Division Two  
November 2, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Washtenaw, John W. Conlin, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an association of education professionals at a community college and a named instructor, appealed a decision from the Washtenaw County Circuit Court (Michigan), which ruled in favor of defendant board of trustees and dismissed the complaint challenging the constitutionality of 1970 Mich. Pub. Acts. ch. 83, § 2(c), which restricted the employer's contributions to more than one retirement fund.


OVERVIEW: The association was the exclusive bargaining representative for the professional personnel. Under the collective bargaining agreement, an employee had the right to make deposits in two different retirement fund programs and the board was required to deposit a matching amount, up to a fixed percent. The association argued that the statute impaired the contract and was thus, unconstitutional under both the United States and state constitutions. The court found no controversy that the statute impaired the collective bargaining agreement. However, not every modification of a contract was per se unconstitutional. The court found that the statute was subject to attack under the Contract Clause because it did not merely restrict the employees to those benefits reasonably to be expected from the contract. There was nothing to indicate that the prohibition on contributions to other retirement funds did anything to protect the vital interests of the general welfare of the people. The interests of the state did not justify the abrogation of the retirement provisions in the collective bargaining contract. Thus, the statute was found to be unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision and found that the statute was unconstitutional.

Kelley v. East Lansing


Docket No. 16136


Court of Appeals of Michigan


50 Mich. App. 511; 213 N.W.2d 557; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 942


October 4, 1973, Submitted Division Two  
November 2, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Jackson, Gordon W. Britten, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county sought review of the decision of the Jackson Circuit Court (Michigan), which denied the county's motion for summary judgment in plaintiff citizen's action for false arrest and imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: The citizen was arrested and held in jail overnight. The next day the citizen was released because the arrest warrant had been issued incorrectly. The citizen filed a complaint against the county for false arrest and imprisonment. The county filed a motion for summary judgment based on the governmental immunity statute, Mich. Comp. Laws § 691.1407, but the trial court denied the county's motion. On appeal, the court vacated the trial court's decision and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the court's decision. The court recognized that an exception existed from the governmental immunity protection for a nuisance that violated the constitutional protection against the taking of property without just compensation. The court concluded that there was no authority for the citizen to recover from the county, and the court was not authorized to establish such a remedy.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision of the trial court, which denied the county's motion for summary judgment in the citizen's action for false arrest and imprisonment. The court remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

2161 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Surowitz v. White Lake


Docket No. 14984


Court of Appeals of Michigan


50 Mich. App. 408; 213 N.W.2d 273; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 925


October 3, 1973, Submitted Division Two  
November 1, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Oakland, Clark J. Adams, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners brought an action challenging the validity of defendant township's zoning ordinance, which restricted the owners' land to agricultural use. The trial court (Michigan), sitting as trier of fact, held the ordinance unconstitutional and permanently restrained the township from enforcing the zoning ordinance to exclude the development of a trailer park on the owners' property. The township appealed that decision.


OVERVIEW: The owners had 113 acres of land in the township, most of which was unimproved property. An ordinance provided that the property could only be zoned for agricultural use. The owners applied to the township to re-zone their land so that they could use it to develop the property as a mobile home park. The township denied the request. The owners filed the instant lawsuit. At trial, the owners produced experts who testified that mobile homes were an essential part of the change in the character of the community. On review, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that the township only had six mobile home parks. The zoning ordinance that excluded the development of the trailer park on the owners' property gave the township's board unfettered control over the development of the property. Therefore, the owners had been left to the whim and caprice of the township board who could exercise their discretion by ordinance amendment but without prescribed standards. The court concluded that the zoning ordinance had resulted in the township taking property from the owners without due process of law in violation of their constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

People v. Tyler


Docket Nos. 15011, 15012


Court of Appeals of Michigan


50 Mich. App. 414; 213 N.W.2d 221; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 926


April 3, 1973, Submitted Division Two  
November 1, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 391 Mich 762.

Reversed by People v. Tyler, 399 Mich. 564, 250 N.W.2d 467, 1977 Mich. LEXIS 167 (1977)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeals from Oakland, Frederick C. Ziem, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a Michigan trial court decision that convicted both defendants of conspiring to burn real property, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.157a, and one defendant of the additional charges of burning real property, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.73, and burning insured property with intent to defraud, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.75.


OVERVIEW: Defendants contended that certain evidence was improperly admitted at trial because the evidence was obtained by an illegal search and seizure. The evidence was seized by fire and police officers investigating a fire. In affirming, the court held that the evidence was properly admitted because it was not the product of an unlawful search and seizure. The court noted that Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 29.6 authorized the investigation of the cause and origin of fires and provided for entry onto the premises without restraint. The court also determined that defendants' privacy and security were not disturbed by the investigations, and the investigations were not arbitrary invasions. Finally, the court found that based on the discovery of two containers on the burned premises, one of which was partially filled with a liquid that smelled like gasoline, the search was reasonable and mandated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

Genesee Land Corp. v. Leon Allen & Assocs.


Docket No. 14048


Court of Appeals of Michigan


50 Mich. App. 296; 213 N.W.2d 283; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 911


October 3, 1973, Submitted Division Two  
October 31, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Genesee, Anthony J. Mansour, J.
Genesee Land Corp. v. Leon Allen & Assocs., 383 Mich. 803, 1970 Mich. LEXIS 493 (1970)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of the grant of summary judgment by the trial court (Michigan) in favor of defendant in plaintiff's action to restrain defendants from constructing a mobile home park on defendants' property.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff contended the construction of a mobile home park violated the local Flint Township Zoning Ordinance. The record established defendants' predecessor in title requested a rezoning of the property that resulted in Flint Township, Mich., Zoning Ordinance No. 42, § 4, which rezoned the property in question from residential suburban agricultural district to light manufacturing district, restricted, however, to construction of and use as a warehouse for wholesale grocery purposes. The trial court held the restrictive portion of Ordinance No. 42 was invalid, but that the remainder of the ordinance rezoning to light manufacturing was valid. Thus, because the Flint Township Zoning Ordinance was a pyramid type, permitting any use in a "lower" zoned district that was permitted in a "higher" zoned district the mobile home park was not in violation of the zoning ordinance. On appeal, the court affirmed holding the inclusion of invalid surplus restrictive language in the zoning amendment ordinance did not invalidate the entire amendatory ordinance and that under Flint Township, Mich., Zoning Ordinance No. 132, § 7, mobile home parks were not prohibited in light manufacturing district.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of defendants in plaintiff's action to restrain defendants from constructing a mobile home park on property defendants' owned.

 

2164 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Tamulion v. State Waterways Comm'n


Docket No. 10372


Court of Appeals of Michigan


50 Mich. App. 60; 212 N.W.2d 828; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 885


February 9, 1972, Submitted Division Two  
September 27, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Court of Claims, William F. Ager, Jr., J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners challenged a judgment of the Court of Claims (Michigan) that dismissed their action against defendant Michigan State Waterways Commission for damages caused to their lakefront property by erosion-control measures taken on the property by the commission after the United States Army Corps of Engineers (corps) constructed a small-craft refuge harbor adjoining the landowners' property.


OVERVIEW: The commission wrote to the landowners, who lived in another city, to request permission to enter their vacation property to take remedial measures against erosion caused by the harbor construction. The landowners granted permission, but when the work was completed they discovered that boulders had been placed on their beach that prevented access to the water and destroyed the property's utility as a vacation residence. Both the corps and the commission disclaimed liability. The court reversed the judgment for the commission and remanded the action for the determination of damages. The permission given by the landowners to the commission did not preclude recovery because the commission's request did not fairly describe the work that was actually done. The work constituted an inverse condemnation because it was a taking of the landowners' property for public use without compensation. The navigational servitude did not excuse payment of compensation to the landowners whose land had been employed as a wall of the harbor with the result of loss of its beneficial use. The commission's involvement in the harbor construction was sufficient to hold it liable to the landowners.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment that dismissed the landowners' action against the commission and remanded the action to the trial court for determination of the amount of damage caused to the landowners' property by erosion-control measures taken by the commission.

 

2165 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


IT&T v. MICHIGAN


Docket No. 15817


Court of Appeals of Michigan


50 Mich. App. 5; 213 N.W.2d 226; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 878


June 6, 1973, Submitted Division Two  
September 27, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 391 Mich 774.
Leave to appeal denied by IT&T v. Mich., 391 Mich. 774, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 528 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Court of Claims, Leo W. Corkin, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed the judgment of the Court of Claims (Michigan), which upheld defendant State of Michigan's determination and redetermination of the taxpayer's franchise fee using the apportionment formula set forth in Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 450.305 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 21.208).


OVERVIEW: The state assessed a franchise fee against the taxpayer in accordance with the apportionment formula in Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 450.305 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 21.208). The taxpayer paid the fee, then commenced an action against the state. The taxpayer claimed that the application of the apportionment formula for computing franchise fees in Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 450.305 did not fairly represent the extent of its business within the state and that adjustments should be made. The taxpayer also sought a judgment against the state in an amount equal to the excess franchise fees which it paid in protest. The trial court upheld the state's determination of the fee amount. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's ruling because the formula for determining a franchise tax was up to the state, provided that the formula resulted in a fair franchise tax. Moreover, any party challenging a formula had a heavy burden to bear. In the instant case, not only did the trial court correctly analyze the fairness of the franchise fee imposed, but the taxpayer failed to establish that the apportionment formula did not fairly represent the extent of its business within the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment upholding the state's determination of the taxpayer's franchise fee in the taxpayer's action challenging the apportionment formula.

 

2166 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Bachor v. Detroit


Docket No. 12548


Court of Appeals of Michigan


49 Mich. App. 507; 212 N.W.2d 302; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 849


June 5, 1973, Submitted Division One  
September 25, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, Neal Fitzgerald, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of the decision of the trial court (Michigan), which granted defendants' motion for a directed verdict. Plaintiffs claimed that they were deprived of their right to a jury trial because they were indigent and failed to pay the required jury fee.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs proceeded pro per in their action against defendants. Although they requested a jury trial, they failed to make the required jury fee payment and a bench trial was had without objection by plaintiffs. The trial court granted defendants' motion for a directed verdict. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment finding that plaintiffs had only satisfied one-half of the requirements for a jury trial. Their failure to pay the jury fee by the close of the pretrial conference constituted a waiver of the right to a jury trial under Mich. Comp. Laws § 600.2537, Mich. Stat. Ann. § 27A.2537. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by holding a bench trial in plaintiffs' case. Although the trial court overlooked their demand for a jury trial, the oversight would not have occurred but for their failure to pay the jury fee, to plead their inability to pay, or to request an exercise of the court's discretion when it became apparent that the trial was going to be held without a jury. The court found that plaintiffs' appearance in pro per did not excuse all application of court rules.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment finding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in holding a bench trial.

 

2167 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Downes


Docket No. 12935


Court of Appeals of Michigan


49 Mich. App. 532; 212 N.W.2d 314; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 851


January 3, 1973, Submitted Division One  
September 25, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Appeal granted by People v. Downes, 391 Mich. 786, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 945 (1974)
Reversed by People v. Downes, 394 Mich. 17, 228 N.W.2d 212, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 201 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Recorder's Court of Detroit, Geraldine Bledsoe Ford, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a physician, appealed the judgment of the Recorder's Court of Detroit (Michigan), which convicted him of violating the provisions of Mich. Comp. Laws § 335.57(1) that prohibited prescribing narcotic drugs other than in good faith in the course of his professional practice.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of prescribing methadone, cocaine, dilaudid, and morphine sulphate and numorphan to addicts under an indictment alleging that the actions were not taken in good faith in the course of his professional practice as a physician. He argued that the term "good faith" was unconstitutionally vague and that the statute impermissibly compelled him to prove that he acted in good faith. In affirming the physician's conviction, the court held that the words "good faith" had a generally accepted meaning and were not so vague and indefinite as to violate due process. Lack of good faith was a substantive element of an offense charged under Mich. Comp. Laws § 335.57(1) that the prosecution was required to prove.Mich. Comp. Laws § 335.68, which cast the burden of proof on defendant with respect to any exception, excuse, proviso, or exemption contained in the uniform narcotic act, only applied to matters of defense. The act's references to federal law were merely the incorporation of federal law by reference rather than an improper delegation of state legislative power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Craig v. Detroit Police Dep't


Docket No. 16007


Court of Appeals of Michigan


49 Mich. App. 599; 212 N.W.2d 235; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 859


June 22, 1973, Submitted Division One  
September 25, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Craig v. City of Detroit Police Dep't, 391 Mich. 785, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 919 (1974)
Reversed by Craig v. Detroit Police Dep't, 397 Mich. 185, 243 N.W.2d 236, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 300 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, Charles S. Farmer, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Michigan Department of Treasury, appealed the decision of the Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan), which entered an order denying the Department's motion for accelerated judgment, rejecting a challenge to the trial court's jurisdiction, and directing the return of certain funds to plaintiff taxpayers. The funds had been received by the Department as a result of certain tax warrants and levies against the taxpayers.


OVERVIEW: The Department issued jeopardy tax assessments and tax warrants against the taxpayers for use and income taxes. The Department received certain funds as a result of the warrants and levies. The taxpayers filed an action before the trial court requesting that the Department be ordered to show cause why the funds should not be returned. The trial court entered judgment for the taxpayers. On appeal, the Department contended that the trial court lacked jurisdiction over the matter. The court held that under Mich. Comp. Laws § 205.7, the procedure for protesting an allegedly illegal jeopardy tax assessment included appealing to the State Board of Tax Appeals or, in the alternative, filing a suit before the state Court of Claims, filing an action in mandamus, or filing an action in the circuit court challenging the constitutionality of the tax statute. The court held that without a constitutional question, the taxpayers failed to exhaust their available statutory administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court.

 

2169 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Frum


Docket No. 14254


Court of Appeals of Michigan


49 Mich. App. 329; 212 N.W.2d 59; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 827


June 19, 1973, Submitted Division Two  
August 30, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Washtenaw, John W. Conlin, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of a circuit court (Michigan), which convicted him of escaping from prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been a juvenile when he was charged with breaking and entering. The probate court waived its juvenile jurisdiction over defendant, and defendant was tried as an adult. He was sentenced to a term of imprisonment at a facility from which he later escaped. After a jury trial, defendant was found guilty of escape. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment, finding that the prosecution for escape was proper because defendant was incarcerated under color of law. The court noted that the probate court waived its jurisdiction over defendant under a statute that had not yet been declared unconstitutional at the time of his initial trial. The case holding the statute unconstitutional was pending rehearing. The court found that defendant had not raised any other allegations of error pertaining to the trial in the circuit court. The court noted that defendant was not justified in escaping from prison because he was confined under color of law and that escape was not the proper means for challenging a conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

2170 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Sponick v. Detroit Police Dep't


Docket Nos. 15396, 15397, 15398


Court of Appeals of Michigan


49 Mich. App. 162; 211 N.W.2d 674; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 813


April 12, 1973, Submitted Division One  
August 29, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from Wayne, James Montante, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed as to plaintiff Daugherty.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officers sought review of an order of the Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan), which affirmed rulings of departmental trial boards which disciplined them for various violations of the rules and regulations of the Detroit Police Department.


OVERVIEW: The police officers, observed associating with a known felon, were charged with misconduct under provisions of the Detroit Police Manual. Three departmental trial boards disciplined the officers, and the officers sought review. The circuit court affirmed. Upon appeal, the court affirmed the circuit court's affirmation of the decisions of the trial boards. The court noted that one regulation unnecessarily restricted police officers' fundamental right to associate freely, and found the regulation constitutionally infirm. However, the court noted that the confidence of the public in the integrity of its police officers was of paramount concern in the regulations. Thus, other regulations such as the regulation that required the officers to notify their superiors of any contacts with criminals, were tailored to serve the interests of justice and gave fair warning of the type of activity that was required or prescribed. There was no evidence that the regulations had been arbitrarily or discriminatorily enforced. Thus, there was no constitutional issue as to enforcement. The departmental trial boards had jurisdiction to impose penalties, including the discharge of officers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court, which affirmed the decisions of the trial boards.
