Edel v. Filer Township


Docket No. 15438


Court of Appeals of Michigan


49 Mich. App. 210; 211 N.W.2d 547; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 814


May 10, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
August 29, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 391 Mich   .
Leave to appeal denied by Edel v. Filer Twp., 391 Mich. 753, 1973 Mich. LEXIS 580 (1973)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Manistee, Charles A. Wickens, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant township sought review of the grant of summary judgment in favor of plaintiff property owners and of the declaration that the township's 1954 zoning ordinance was invalid from the Circuit Court of Manistee (Michigan).


OVERVIEW: The property owners' property had been zoned as agricultural and they attempted to obtain a rezoning of their property to a light industrial classification. The township refused to rezone the property and the property owners brought suit. The trial court stated that the township failed to maintain a book of ordinances as required by Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 41.192 (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 5.6(2)). The court stated that while there was a failure to maintain a bound book of ordinances prior to 1961, the township did maintain a file of ordinances in which all of the township's zoning ordinances were set forth. The court held that the failure of the township clerk to keep a book of ordinances in strict compliance with § 41.192; § 5.6(2) was not an adequate ground to invalidate the ordinance. The court also held that because the ordinance had been in effect for 18 years and had been relied upon by numerous other parties, the grant of summary judgment due to a technical violation in the adoption of the ordinance was in error. The court reversed the grant of summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment in favor of the property owners was reversed.

People v. Holland


Docket No. 14600


Court of Appeals of Michigan


49 Mich. App. 76; 211 N.W.2d 224; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 800


April 4, 1973, Submitted Division One  
August 28, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, Joseph G. Rashid, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and defendant discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan), which entered a jury verdict convicting defendant of committing an act of gross indecency with a female person in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.338b. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statute and also alleged that the private act with which defendant was charged did not, as a matter of law, constitute an act of "gross indecency."


OVERVIEW: Defendant was observed by police while engaging in a sexual act with a female person. Defendant's female companion had her hand on defendant's penis while the two were seated in a car parked in a store parking lot. Defendant was charged and convicted of gross indecency with a female person. On appeal, defendant contended that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. Defendant alleged that the statute lacked sufficient specificity to inform those charged under the statute of the nature of the accusation. Defendant also claimed that the private act which defendant was charged with committing did not, as a matter of law, constitute an act of gross indecency. The court noted initially that § 750.338b would appear to apply to acts between a married couple and could constitute an invasion of the right of privacy in marriage. However, the court held that it did not need to reach the issue of the constitutionality of the statute because given that the act of intercourse was not "gross indecency," the court found it could not see how the action with which defendant was charged could possibly constitute a violation of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and discharged defendant.

RAY v. MASON CTY. DRAIN COMMR.


Docket No. 15090


Court of Appeals of Michigan


48 Mich. App. 559; 210 N.W.2d 810; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 759


May 8, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
July 25, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 391 Mich   .
Appeal granted by Ray v. Mason County Drain Comm'r, 391 Mich. 753, 1973 Mich. LEXIS 611 (1973)
Vacated by Ray v. Mason County Drain Comm'r, 393 Mich. 294, 224 N.W.2d 883, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 187 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Mason, Charles A. Wickens, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff watershed residents appealed a decision of the Mason Circuit Court (Michigan) rendered in favor of defendant county drain commissioner in the residents' action seeking to enjoin the commissioner from proceeding with a plan for drains in the watershed allegedly in violation of the Drain Code of 1956, Mich. Comp. Laws § 280.1 et seq. (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 11.1001 et seq.), and from assessing the residents any of the project cost.


OVERVIEW: The residents alleged that the commissioner, in adopting an extensive construction plan for drains in the watershed, failed to comply with the Drain Code, that the Drain Code was unconstitutional as it applied to them, that the commissioner and others were guilty of fraud and misrepresentation, and that they were specially assessed for a portion of the project costs when they would not benefit from it. The trial court ruled in favor of the commissioner. On appeal, the court held that the cost of the drain project was not a necessary factor in the initial determination of necessity under Mich. Comp. Laws §§ 280.2, 280.72 (Mich. Stat. Ann. §§ 11.1002, 11.1072). The court found that statements made by the commissioner and others regarding the residents' opportunity to vote on the project if the cost proved to be excessive were made in good faith with no intent to deceive and that the lack of knowledge that the statements were false vitiated against any finding of fraud. The court concluded that the Drain Code was not unconstitutional based upon the trial court's finding, after hearing substantial testimony, that the residents' land would benefit from the expanded drainage system.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered in favor of the commissioner in the residents' action seeking to enjoin the commissioner from proceeding with the plan for drains in the watershed.

Lambert v. Calhoun


Docket No. 14640


Court of Appeals of Michigan


48 Mich. App. 506; 210 N.W.2d 796; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 751


May 10, 1973, Submitted Division One  
July 25, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Appeal granted by Lambert v. Calhoun, 391 Mich. 777, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 857 (1974)
Reversed by Lambert v. Calhoun, 394 Mich. 179, 229 N.W.2d 332, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 216 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, Victor J. Baum, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In her action against defendant uninsured motorist, plaintiff minor passenger appealed a judgment of the Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan), which granted the accelerated judgment motion of intervenor Secretary of State (Michigan). The action concerned a two-car accident and alleged negligence. The parties disagreed over whether the minor passenger's claim against the Motor Vehicle Accident Claims Fund was time-barred.


OVERVIEW: The driver's insurer paid a claim of the minor passenger. The insurer, in turn, filed a subrogation action against the uninsured motorist. The minor passenger then filed the instant action under the Motor Vehicle Accident Claims Act more than three years after the accident. The Secretary intervened and filed the motion for accelerated judgment. The Secretary contended that the minor passenger's claim against the Fund was time-barred by the three-year limitations period in Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. §§ 257.1118, 257.1128. The minor passenger contended that because she was a minor, the general statute of limitations, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 600.5851(1), applied to save her claim against the Fund. The lower court granted the Secretary's motion. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment. The remedies and rights under the Act were subject to the Act's limitations. The driver's insurer filing of an action against the uninsured motorist did not toll the limitation period. That action could not result in recovery from the Fund. The limitation period did not bar the minor passenger's claim against the uninsured motorist.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

In re LaFlure


Docket No. 13484


Court of Appeals of Michigan


48 Mich. App. 377; 210 N.W.2d 482; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 735


March 7, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
July 23, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 390 Mich   .
Leave to appeal denied by In re Laflure, 390 Mich. 814, 1973 Mich. LEXIS 692 (1973)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Midland, James R. Rood, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a decision of the Midland County Circuit Court (Michigan), which affirmed a lower court's decision terminating the mother's parental rights.


OVERVIEW: Police officers removed a boy from a home that was in filthy condition when the mother refused police requests to return home from work. The boy was placed in foster care and a petition alleging neglect was filed. The trial court ultimately terminated the mother's parental rights. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the statute that placed the burden of proof on parents in proceedings to terminate parental rights, Mich. Comp. Laws § 712A.19a(f) (Mich. Stat. Ann. § 27.3178(598.19a)(f)), was unconstitutional. The court held that it was impermissible to shift the burden of proof onto the mother in the quasi-criminal proceeding because it resulted in a violation of the mother's due process rights. The court ruled that the state had the burden of proof in such proceedings and that the state had not provided clear and convincing evidence to support the termination of the mother's parental rights. The court also found that evidence of how and why the boy originally entered foster care related to the mother's unfitness and was improperly excluded from the proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decisions of the lower courts terminating the mother's parental rights and remanded the case for a new trial.

People v. Andrea


Docket No. 12285


Court of Appeals of Michigan

July 23, 1973, Decided

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan), which convicted defendant of unarmed robbery upon her guilty plea and sentenced her to prison for a term of 3 to 15 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised several issues on appeal, including that the federal and state constitutions plus state case law established that legislation, which irrationally discriminated against women, was violative of equal protection guarantees. Based upon that contention, defendant argued that the statutes establishing the Detroit House of Correction discriminated against women prisoners because the provisions governing good-time credit, parole, and superintendent qualifications at the women's prison differed substantially from the statutory provisions on the same points for male prisoners in other state penal institutions. On appeal, the court conceded that legislation that established an unreasonable and arbitrary classification on the basis of sex violated the equal protection guarantee of the federal constitution and that male and female convicts in state prisons must be treated equally with respect to good-time credits for early release. However, the court found that the defendant failed to show that equal protection laws were violated and it affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Nickola v. Grand Blanc


Docket No. 12959


Court of Appeals of Michigan


47 Mich. App. 684; 209 N.W.2d 803; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1349


May 9, 1973, Submitted Division Two  
June 25, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 390 Mich   .
Appeal granted by Nickola v. Grand Blanc Twp., 390 Mich. 806, 1973 Mich. LEXIS 670 (1973)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Nickola v. Grand Blanc, 394 Mich. 589, 232 N.W.2d 604, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 261 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Genesee, Donald R. Freeman, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed, and ordinance held unconstitutional as to plaintiffs' property.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sought review of a ruling of a trial court of Genesee (Michigan) upholding the decision of defendants, a township and its board of officers, that denied the property owners' petition to rezone a tract of land for a mobile home park.


OVERVIEW: The property owners purchased land with the admitted purpose of building and maintaining a mobile home park. At the time of purchase the property was zoned single family residences other than mobile homes. The property owners filed a petition for rezoning accompanied by consent thereto by 11 adjacent property owners. No action was taken thereon for two years. The court stated that the real question presented by the appeal was whether zoning in Michigan was a popularity contest to be won by the most organized and vocal party, or whether it was a set of legal principles embodied in some recognizable and dependable case precedent. In reversing and holding the zoning ordinance unconstitutional as applied to the property owners' land, the court stated that according full acceptance to the trial judge's findings it could not possibly see how a mobile home park could possibly have affected the township's morals, health, or safety. Standards of sanitation, fire protection, and other general health and safety requirements were imposed upon mobile home parks by statute, and nothing suggested that trailer parks created any greater "moral" problem than any other type structure.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, holding the township zoning ordinance constitutionally infirm as applied to the property owners' land.

 

2178 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Edwards


Docket No. 13732


Court of Appeals of Michigan


47 Mich. App. 307; 209 N.W.2d 527; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1294


March 9, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
May 23, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 390 Mich 787.
Appeal granted by, Remanded by People v. Edwards, 390 Mich. 787, 1973 Mich. LEXIS 208 (1973)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Saginaw, Fred J. Borchard, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction in a trial court (Michigan) for second-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with having murdered the victim while attempting to rob him. The jury was instructed as to four possible verdicts: guilty of first-degree murder, of second-degree murder, or of manslaughter; and not guilty. Defendant appealed from his conviction for second-degree murder, arguing that the trial court erred when it instructed the jury to disregard testimony by a witness who claimed that another man confessed to the murder before he died. The court affirmed the conviction, but remanded for resentencing. The presentence report submitted to the trial court prior to defendant's sentencing detailed defendant's juvenile record. The likelihood that defendant's sentence was influenced by the trial court's knowledge of his juvenile record was so strong that the court remanded for resentencing. The court held that any admission of guilt by the decedent did not come within the traditional exception to the hearsay rule for declarations against proprietary or pecuniary interest. Defendant presented no extrinsic evidence to corroborate the alleged confession, which was not made under oath or in writing, indicia of trustworthiness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and remanded for resentencing. The court ordered that a new presentence report be prepared, omitting any reference to defendant's juvenile record, and ordered that the court administrator assign a judge from other than the trial court's circuit to resentence defendant.

People v. Gebarowski


Docket No. 14009


Court of Appeals of Michigan


47 Mich. App. 379; 209 N.W.2d 543; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1300


January 10, 1973, Submitted Division Two  
May 23, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 390 Mich 785.
Leave to appeal denied by People v. Gebarowski, 390 Mich. 785, 1973 Mich. LEXIS 200 (1973)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Lenawee, Rex B. Martin, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of a district court (Michigan) convicting her of driving under the influence of alcohol.


OVERVIEW: A police officer warned defendant that, under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 257.625a(4), her refusal to take a breathalyzer test would automatically result in a suspension of her license. Defendant took the test but filed a motion to suppress the results. She argued that a suspension was not automatic, as the officer said, and thus the warning unconstitutionally coerced her into waiving her rights under the Fifth Amendment. The district court granted the motion to suppress but adjourned to permit the prosecutor to appeal the ruling. The circuit court reversed the ruling and remanded. Defendant was convicted. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the circuit court had jurisdiction to review the district court's suppression order. The prosecutor had the right to seek review of questions of law by an order of superintending control, pursuant to Mich. Gen. Ct. R. 711 (1963). The court held that the results of the test were admissible. Defendant could be coerced into submitting to a breathalyzer test without violating her Fifth Amendment right against self incrimination. Consequently, any error in the statutory warning was a mere technicality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for driving under the influence of alcohol.

McCann v. State


Docket No. 13913


Court of Appeals of Michigan


47 Mich. App. 326; 209 N.W.2d 456; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1296

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Court of Claims, James E. Hoff, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff newspaper owner sought review of a decision of the Court of Claims (Michigan), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant Department of Mental Health and dismissed the owner's negligence complaint for failing to state a claim upon which relief could have been granted pursuant to Mich. Ct. R. 117.2(1) (1963).


OVERVIEW: The owner's newspaper contained several stories raising the issue of whether a state mental hospital patient died of natural causes, or due to some negligence of hospital employees. As a result of the articles, the owner claimed that several employees successfully persuaded most of the newspaper's advertisers to discontinue advertising in the paper. The owner challenged the trial court's dismissal of his complaint on the basis of governmental immunity. The court found that by its terms, 1970 Mich. Pub. 2182 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Smyers


Docket Nos. 14007, 9710


Court of Appeals of Michigan


47 Mich. App. 61; 209 N.W.2d 281; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1268


February 6, 1973, Submitted Division Two  
May 22, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal as to Smyers applied for.
Appeal granted by People v. Smyers, 391 Mich. 766, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 471 (1974)
Affirmed by People v. Smyers, 398 Mich. 635, 248 N.W.2d 156, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 204 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Genesee, Philip C. Elliott, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated action, defendants appealed a decision of the trial court (Michigan) that, after a jury trial, convicted them of conspiring to break and enter occupied dwellings and conspiring to receive and conceal stolen property. One defendant argued that the State's closing remarks were improper.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of conspiring to break and enter occupied dwellings and conspiring to receive and conceal stolen property. On appeal, it was alleged that the prosecutor for the State improperly remarked to the jury regarding his own personal belief that the defendant at issue was guilty. In affirming, the court noted that the remark, although improper, was in response to a similar comment made by defense counsel; furthermore, the prosecutor indicated immediately after this comment that he wanted the jury to decide the case on the evidence, which he proceeded to discuss. Also, the record was devoid of any showing of objection by defendant's own trial counsel regarding the remark, nor did defense counsel request a curative instruction. Finally, the trial court properly instructed the jury as to the function of counsel and specifically charged the trier of fact to disregard any expression by counsel with respect to their personal belief of defendant's guilt or innocence. Accordingly, the error, if any, was harmless.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed.

Regents of University of Mich. v. State


Docket No. 13422


Court of Appeals of Michigan


47 Mich. App. 23; 208 N.W.2d 871; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1266


November 8, 1972, Submitted Division Two  
May 16, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 390 Mich 768.
Appeal granted by Regents of the Univ. of Mich. v. State of Mich., 390 Mich. 768, 1973 Mich. LEXIS 489 (1973)
Affirmed by, in part Regents of University of Mich. v. State, 395 Mich. 52, 235 N.W.2d 1, 1975 Mich. LEXIS 154 (1975)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Ingham, Marvin J. Salmon, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant state and intervening defendant state board of education (board) sought review of the judgment of the Ingham trial court (Michigan), which held certain sections of 1971 Mich. Pub. Acts 122 unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff state universities.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held §§ 13, 16, 18, 19, 20 and 26 of 1971 Mich. Pub. Acts 122 unconstitutional. These sections put limitations on how the universities could appropriate the funds granted by the state legislature. The trial court also held that the board possessed no power to require its prior approval of certain education programs proposed by the universities before the universities could validly implement said programs. The state and the board sought review of the trial court's judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that §§ 13, 16, 18, 19 and 20 of 1971 Mich. Pub. Acts 122 were invalid because through those sections, the legislature was attempting to control the internal operations of the universities by dictating how the appropriated funds could be spent by the universities' governing boards. The court held that such control was beyond the power of the legislature. Mich. Const. art. 8, § 5 clearly vested the power to control and direct university funds to the universities' governing boards. The board did not have the right to limit or interfere with the power of the universities' boards in governing their institutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which held certain laws that attempted to control how a university appropriated its funds to be unconstitutional as applied to the state universities.

 

2184 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


McNees v. Scholley


Docket No. 14613


Court of Appeals of Michigan


46 Mich. App. 702; 208 N.W.2d 643; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1251


April 3, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
April 26, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Van Buren, David Anderson, Jr., J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a student and others, appealed a judgment from a Van Buren trial court (Michigan) that granted defendant school district summary judgment in plaintiffs' negligence action, under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1405, in which they sought to recover damages for personal injuries sustained by the student while he was waiting for a school bus.


OVERVIEW: A passing car struck the student as he was waiting for his school bus; the student was waiting across the street from a designated road-side bus stop. The accident occurred as the driver's car and another car, which was traveling in the opposite direction of the driver's car, passed each other in front of the student. In their suit, plaintiffs' alleged that the negligent designation of the bus stop constituted negligent operation of a motor vehicle under § 691.1405. On appeal, the court ruled that the district was properly granted summary judgment on that claim because the district's school bus was not in a state of being at work at the time and place the injury was inflicted, and thus plaintiffs did not have a cause of action under § 691.1405. The court further ruled that, even though the governmental immunity statute, 1964 Mich. Pub. Acts 170, § 7, Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1407, had been declared invalid, the district enjoyed immunity from plaintiffs' suit. The district's acts of laying out school bus routes and designating bus stops were essential exercises of the governmental function of education. The court declined to hold that governmental immunity was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

In re Jackson


Docket Nos. 11298, 11837


Court of Appeals of Michigan


46 Mich. App. 764; 208 N.W.2d 526; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1263


October 3, 1972, Submitted Division One  
April 26, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, Horace W. Gilmore, J.

Appeal from Recorder's Court of Detroit, John R. Murphy, J.



DISPOSITION: PEOPLE v. JACKSON; Issue not considered, being moot. (Docket No. 11298.)

JACKSON v. PEOPLE; Affirmed. (Docket No. 11837.)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, sought review of a judgment of the trial court (Michigan), which convicted him of unarmed robbery under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.530.


OVERVIEW: A series of robberies and assaults were perpetrated against elderly women in a neighborhood. After police investigation, defendant was arrested and convicted of unarmed robbery. The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that the waiver of jurisdiction of the juvenile court was proper pursuant to Mich. Juv. Ct. R. 11 (1969). The court found that the presence of court-appointed counsel satisfied the due process requirements for the showup identification, which was done before defendant's mother had retained counsel for defendant. The court concluded that there was probable cause for defendant's arrest and that the identification testimony was not the product of an illegal arrest. The court noted that defendant closely resembled a composite drawing of the attacker, he wore clothing similar to that worn by the assailant, and he lived within walking distance of all the victims. The court found that the identification made by the complainant was the product of her extensive opportunity to observe defendant at the time of the offense and had an independent basis. The court held that evidence of other crimes was properly admitted because of their striking similarity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment against defendant.

People v. Potts


Docket No. 13717


Court of Appeals of Michigan


46 Mich. App. 538; 208 N.W.2d 583; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1232


February 7, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
April 25, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal applied for.
Leave to appeal denied by People v. Potts, 391 Mich. 833, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 817 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Kent, John H. Vander Wal, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed with sentence modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Kent County Circuit Court (Michigan), which convicted defendant of forgery and uttering and publishing. The trial court imposed a sentence to serve of 7-1/2 to 14 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant cashed a check at a supermarket, which was made out to the name of another person, and he endorsed the check in the presence of the cashier. He presented a social security card and a health insurance card as identification that was in the name of the other person. He wore a shirt when he cashed the check, which he and another party had previously purchased with the other person's name placed on it. The check was among blank checks from a closed bank account that was taken from a company's office the previous year. The court held that: (1) defendant failed to show where he was prejudiced by a 16-month delay between his arrest and trial because a preliminary examination transcript was lost and the withdrawal of defendant's attorney; (2) there was no error that required resentencing because the trial judge was aware of other charges against defendant because the case was the first of two cases that was routinely assigned to the same judge under a local practice; and (3) defendant was entitled to a credit against his sentences for forgery and uttering and publishing for the 307 days he was not free on bond prior to sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court modified defendant's sentences so he was granted credit for 307 days he spent in jail and in prison on other offenses. As modified, the court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

People v. Osteen


Docket No. 13145


Court of Appeals of Michigan

April 24, 1973, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Ingham, Jack W. Warren, J.
People v. Osteen, 388 Mich. 783, 1972 Mich. LEXIS 726 (1972)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of an Ingham trial court (Michigan), which convicted defendant of the sale of heroin and imposed a prison term of 20 to 25 years. The court granted leave to defendant for a delayed appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for the sale of heroin to a police informant in the bedroom of an apartment. Defendant asserted an alibi defense and offered eight relatives as witnesses that he was attending a family picnic. The prosecution offered the testimony of a witness who visited the apartment as a rebuttal to defendant testimony that he was not present. Defendant alleged that a state supreme court order was the basis of an alleged error in sentencing. The court held that: (1) a disparity between a mandatory sentence of 20 years under an old statute and a maximum sentence of four years under the Michigan Controlled Substances Act made the 20-year sentence for a marijuana conviction cruel and unusual but did not apply to a heroin conviction because a distinction between heroin and marijuana was justified; (2) an appellate court order that reversed a trial court judgment governed only that case presented because the order responded only the particular need; and (3) the admission of defendant's 15 prior misdemeanor convictions was an abuse of discretion and was not consistent with guidelines that required consideration of factors for the exercise of the trial court's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and sentence. The court remanded the case to the trial court for a new trial.

People v. Ferguson


Docket Nos. 12762, 12763


Court of Appeals of Michigan


46 Mich. App. 331; 208 N.W.2d 647; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1207; 73 A.L.R.3d 716


December 14, 1972, Submitted Division Two  
April 23, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Livingston, Paul R. Mahinske, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of a judgment of a Livingston trial court (Michigan), which convicted them of breaking and entering, safe robbery, and possession of burglary tools.


OVERVIEW: The state police arrested defendants inside a supermarket. The officers found several holes drilled into a safe. Two sticks of dynamite, a length of fuse, and blasting caps were in a shopping basket next to the safe. On the first day of trial, the trial court denied a request from defendants' appointed counsel for a continuance so defendants could confer with and help recently retained counsel for preparation of a defense. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the words "bank, safe and vault robbery" were not the title of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.531 but were part of the catch line of § 750.531 and catch lines were not deemed part of the section pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 8.4b; (2) defendants were not improperly charged under of the "bank, safe and vault robbery" statute even though they could have been charged under the "burglary with explosives" statute once they broke and entered carrying dynamite; and (3) the trial court abused its discretion where it refused a continuance to defendants' substitute counsel because there was no evidence defendants attempted to delay the proceedings and the trial date had been advanced by 20 days without adequate notice to defendants.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendants' convictions and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings not inconsistent with the court's opinion.

Tilmon v. Kaye


Docket No. 14162


Court of Appeals of Michigan


46 Mich. App. 63; 207 N.W.2d 467; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1171


January 9, 1973, Submitted Division One  
March 29, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, Nathan J. Kaufman, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff cabdriver brought an action against defendant, a decedent's representative, in a Wayne trial court (Michigan) to recover damages for injuries sustained in an accident involving a vehicle operated by the decedent. The Motor Vehicle Accident Claims Fund undertook to defend the action pursuant to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 257.1108 and appealed the decision not to reduce the cabdriver's award by the amount of his compensation benefits.


OVERVIEW: As a result of his injuries in the accident, the cabdriver received workmen's compensation benefits pursuant to his employment. The Fund accepted a mediation award for the cabdriver, but contended unsuccessfully in the trial court that the award should have been reduced by the amount of the benefits the cabdriver received. The issue before the court was whether the language of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 257.1122 required such a reduction. In reversing the decision, the court held that § 257.1122 applied to injured parties who received workmen's compensation benefits and that the Fund was entitled to a reduction of the judgment equal to the amount of the benefit. The section of the Motor Vehicle Accident Claims Act that denied access to the Fund to persons covered by the Workmen's Compensation Act previously had been held to be unconstitutional. The court found, however, that it was impermissible under § 257.1122 to raise injured employees covered by workmen's compensation to a status above those otherwise insured. The court declined to hold the Fund responsible for the full amount of the award.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision and remanded for action not inconsistent with the opinion.

Dow v. State


Docket No. 14690


Court of Appeals of Michigan


46 Mich. App. 101; 207 N.W.2d 441; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1178


February 7, 1973, Submitted Division Three  
March 29, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 389 Mich 817.
Appeal granted by Dow v. State, 389 Mich. 817, 1973 Mich. LEXIS 766 (1973)
Reversed by Dow v. State, 396 Mich. 192, 240 N.W.2d 450, 1976 Mich. LEXIS 250 (1976)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Kent, John T. Letts, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a former titleholder and the former equitable owners of a lot, sought review of a decision of the trial court (Michigan), which granted summary judgment to defendant State of Michigan in plaintiffs' action to set aside the sale of their real property for delinquent taxes.


OVERVIEW: The titleholder owned a lot that the equitable owners were purchasing under an existing land contract. The premises were rented to and occupied by others. The annual city property taxes for the lot were not paid, and a couple of years later the State acquired title to the land. One of the equitable owners received notice of the redemption period, but no offer to redeem was made until after the redemption period had expired. The State rejected offers that were made after that period. Plaintiffs brought an action against the State to set aside the tax sale, and the trial court granted summary judgment to the State. The court affirmed that decision. The court found that the government complied with the mandatory provision of the statutes dealing with tax foreclosure. The court noted that the small newspaper in which notice was published met the requirements of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 600.1461. The court held that notice of the tax proceedings by publication alone did not constitute a violation of due process requirements. The court concluded that any failure to give notice of redemptive rights did not invalidate the foreclosure and sale proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment against plaintiffs.

Goachee v. Garden City


Docket No. 13679


Court of Appeals of Michigan


45 Mich. App. 716; 206 N.W.2d 801; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1157


March 3, 1973, Submitted Division One  
March 28, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, Charles Kaufman, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, who were owners and occupiers of residential premises located in an urban renewal project area, appealed the judgment of the Wayne County Circuit Court (Michigan), which granted defendant city's motion for a dismissal of plaintiffs' action. Plaintiffs had sought to have Garden City, Michigan, Ordinance No. 71-008 declared unconstitutional and void for failure to comply with the enabling statute.


OVERVIEW: In addition to a declaration that Garden City, Michigan, Ordinance No. 71-008 was void and unconstitutional, plaintiffs sought an injunction enjoining the city from implementing a proposed urban renewal project. Plaintiffs contended that the composition of the citizens' council, which was to be comprised of the residents of the development area, was not representative of those people residing in the proposed site of the urban renewal project as was required by statute. The court held that the trial court erred in granting the city's motion to dismiss plaintiffs' action. In so holding, the court found that: (1) the city's failure to ensure that residents of the proposed urban renewal project received representation to the maximum extent possible clearly violated the statutory provisions of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 125.74; (2) not one resident of the project area was selected to be a member of the citizens' district council; and (3) the absence of any residents of the area ran counter to the statutory language and violated the tenets of fair representation to people most affected by the urban renewal project.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

2192 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Wolverine Steel Co. v. Detroit


Docket No. 13407


Court of Appeals of Michigan


45 Mich. App. 671; 207 N.W.2d 194; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1150


January 11, 1973, Submitted Division One  
March 27, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 390 Mich 771.
Leave to appeal denied by Wolverine Steel Co. v. City of Detroit, 390 Mich. 771, 1973 Mich. LEXIS 358 (1973)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, Bernard H. Davidson, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of an order of a trial court (Michigan), which dismissed the taxpayer's action for the return of certain personal property taxes for no cause of action. The taxpayer claimed the taxes were assessed by appellee city in violation of U. S. Const. art 1, § 10.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, a corporation, paid personal property taxes on imported goods owned by it. It did so, relying on information provided to its controller by an auditor from the personal property division of the board of assessors of the city. The payment was made without protest. The taxpayer initiated the action claiming that under the holding of a subsequent case, its goods were unconstitutionally assessed. It further claimed that under Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 211.53a it could recover the money paid because the incorrect payment had been made as the result of a mutual mistake of fact made by the assessing officer and the taxpayer. The trial court dismissed the action and the court affirmed. An error made in determining the application of the United States Constitution to the tax laws of Michigan was not the type of mistake of fact required by the statute. Section 211.53a applied to excess taxes paid because of a clerical error or mutual mistake of fact made by the assessing officer and the taxpayer. The court held that § 211.53a alluded to questions of whether or not the taxpayer had listed all of its property, or listed property that it had already sold, or not yet received.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

2193 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mash


Docket No. 12023


Court of Appeals of Michigan


45 Mich. App. 459; 206 N.W.2d 767; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1122


February 7, 1973, Submitted Division Two  
March 26, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied 390 Mich 778.
Leave to appeal denied by People v. Mash, 390 Mich. 778, 1973 Mich. LEXIS 384 (1973)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Washtenaw, Ross W. Campbell, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed on leave granted from a judgment of the Washtenaw County Circuit Court (Michigan), which affirmed defendant's district court conviction for making a disturbance in a public building, contrary to Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 750.170.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of making a disturbance in a public building for his participation in a sit-in at a university. On appeal, he alleged that § 750.170 was vague and overbroad; that the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction; that the testimony of the university president as to the statements he made to participants at the sit-in was hearsay and prejudicial; and that the charge to the jury was inaccurate and confusing. The court reviewed the definition of "disturbance" and found that § 750.170 was not vague or overbroad. The jury was properly instructed to use the definition of "disturbance" and not "contention" in reaching its verdict. There was sufficient evidence produced at trial for the jury to convict defendant beyond a reasonable doubt of creating a disturbance. The university president's testimony concerning statements he made to the protesters was not hearsay because its value did not depend on the credibility of an out-of-court declarant. The jury charges was not confusing and erroneous as defendant contended. The trial court properly limited the jury's consideration to "disturbance," as defendant requested and as the prosecution had submitted the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Roberts v. State


Docket No. 13640


Court of Appeals of Michigan


45 Mich. App. 252; 206 N.W.2d 466; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1084; 5 ERC (BNA) 1111; 3 ELR 20207


December 7, 1972, Submitted Division Two  
February 23, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Ingham, Jack W. Warren, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action by plaintiff citizen against defendants, the Michigan Secretary of State and the Director of the State Department of Highways, an appeal was taken from a judgment of the Ingham County Circuit Court (Michigan), which dismissed the action insofar as it sought to require defendants to adopt rules to control pollution from motor vehicles, but which held that the Environmental Protection Act of 1970 (Act) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The citizen filed an action for injunctive relief and damages, asking that defendants be restrained from issuing motor-vehicle licenses, constructing highways, or operating state-owned vehicles until rules, regulations, standards, and safeguards were adopted that would control air pollution caused by automobiles. Defendants claimed that they lacked authority to adopt standards, rules, regulations, and safeguards in relation to pollution arising from the operation of motor vehicles. The trial court agreed and dismissed that portion of the action, but it held that the Act was unconstitutional because it was an unlawful delegation of legislative authority to the courts. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal of the action but reversed the trial court's determination of the Act's unconstitutionality. The Act's constitutionality should not have been passed upon because the action should have been dismissed on other grounds. The Michigan Court of Claims had exclusive jurisdiction of actions for damages against state officials, and neither defendant had the authority or the responsibility to promulgate rules and regulations to control air pollution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that portion of the judgment that determined that the Act was unconstitutional, but it affirmed the dismissal of the action.

People v. Urban


Docket No. 13653


Court of Appeals of Michigan


45 Mich. App. 255; 206 N.W.2d 511; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1085


January 5, 1973, Submitted Division Two  
February 23, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Macomb, Howard R. Carroll, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the trial court (Michigan) convicting him of unlawfully possessing d-lysergic acid diethylamide (LSD) in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws § 335.106; Mich. Stat. Ann. § 18.1106 (repealed).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant challenged his conviction of unlawfully possessing LSD in violation of Mich. Comp. Laws § 335.106; Mich. Stat. Ann. § 18.1106 (repealed). The court sua sponte considered an error concerning the correct interpretation and application to defendant of Mich. Comp. Laws § 335.106; Mich. Stat. Ann. § 18.1106 (repealed). The court reversed defendant's conviction of unlawfully possessing LSD and remanded for a new trial. By incorporating the version of the Federal Food, Drug, and Cosmetic Act, 21 U.S.C.S. § 301 et seq., in effect at the time of its enactment, Mich. Comp. Laws § 335.106; Mich. Stat. Ann. § 18.1106 (repealed) provided for a statutory exception for personal or household use of LSD. In this case, the prosecutor failed to meet its burden of proving that defendant's possession of LSD was not for his personal or household use.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of unlawfully possessing LSD and remanded for a new trial.

People v. Bennett


Docket No. 13199


Court of Appeals of Michigan


45 Mich. App. 127; 205 N.W.2d 831; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1065


December 5, 1972, Submitted Division Three  
February 22, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal denied, 389 Mich 816.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Barry, Richard E. Robinson, J.
People v. Bennett, 388 Mich. 754, 1972 Mich. LEXIS 307 (1972)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Barry County Circuit Court (Michigan), which convicted him of taking liberties with a 14-year-old boy, a violation of Mich. Comp. Laws § 750.336, and sentenced him to a prison term of two to 10 years.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of taking indecent liberties with a 14-year-old boy, and he was sentenced to a prison term. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of conviction. Alexander v. Detroit


Docket No. 12491


Court of Appeals of Michigan


45 Mich. App. 7; 205 N.W.2d 819; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1050


December 12, 1972, Submitted Division One  
February 21, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Leave to appeal granted, 389 Mich 816.
Appeal granted by Alexander v. City of Detroit, 389 Mich. 816, 1973 Mich. LEXIS 742 (1973)
Reversed by, Remanded by Alexander v. Detroit, 392 Mich. 30, 219 N.W.2d 41, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 167 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Wayne, George T. Martin, J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed, the class action dismissed, and the order segregating the fees vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of a judgment from a Wayne trial court (Michigan), which found in favor of plaintiff property owners in their class action against the city seeking to invalidate an ordinance regarding the pick up of commercial waste in the city.


OVERVIEW: A dispute arose between property owners and a city regarding the constitutionality of a city ordinance providing for the collection of commercial waste. The owners filed an action in the trial court, in the form of an asserted class action, and essentially sought money damages. The trial court set forth an order segregating all the monies collected pursuant to the ordinance and placed them in an escrow account. The trial court ruled that all of the monies collected from the members of the class which the owners claimed to represent were determined to be the property of the owners and the class. On appeal, the court reversed. The court stated that the owners had the options of private contract, private disposition, or the service offered by the city at the price established by the ordinance. Therefore, the owners were not the victims of alleged discrimination in classification or discriminatory enforcement unless they opted for the offered municipal service. Next, the court held that there was nothing arbitrary, capricious, or fanciful in setting the ordinance and that the exclusion of condominiums and cooperatives by the city was not without a rational and reasonable basis.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated the judgment of the trial court.

 

2199 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Fisher v. Hatcher


Docket No. 10973


Court of Appeals of Michigan


44 Mich. App. 541; 205 N.W.2d 913; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 1028


April 5, 1972, Submitted Division One  
February 20, 1973, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Wayne, John D. O'Hair, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from an order of a trial court (Michigan), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff on a jury verdict in plaintiff's action for property damages. The first trial had resulted in a verdict of no cause of action. Plaintiff had filed a motion for a new trial on the ground that four jurors had failed to disclose that they had at one time been involved in a motor-vehicle collision that resulted in a claim for property damages.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff alleged that property damages were suffered as a result of an automobile accident. The first trial resulted in a verdict of no cause of action, but the jury returned a verdict in favor of plaintiff in the second trial. Defendants appealed, arguing that they were improperly denied the right to read to the jury certain portions of the hospital records that had been admitted into evidence on the authority of Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 600.2146. The court affirmed. No proof was presented that would indicate the truth or falsity of the statements and impressions that were set forth in the record. All of those were prepared while plaintiff was an outpatient and had nothing to do with acts, occurrences, transactions, or events incident to her treatment after the accident. Section 600.2146 provided that those entries that dealt with "transactions, occurrences, or events" could be admitted. Plaintiff was on the stand, but the attorney for defendants neglected to cross-examine her concerning those statements. Accordingly, the trial court properly denied admission of those portions of the hospital record relating to prior statements made by plaintiff to hospital personnel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

2200 of 2443 DOCUMENTS


Busha v. State


Docket No. 15703


Court of Appeals of Michigan


51 Mich. App. 397; 215 N.W.2d 567; 1973 Mich. App. LEXIS 688


November 9, 1973, Submitted Division Two  
January 21, 1973, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by Busha v. State Highway Dep't, 391 Mich. 816, 1974 Mich. LEXIS 330 (1974)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Court of Claims, Charles A. Wickens, J.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injury victims appealed the judgment of the Court of Claims (Michigan), which granted a motion for an accelerated judgment filed by defendant, the Michigan Department of State Highways, in the victims' action alleging that their motor vehicle accident was caused by an unsafe highway.


OVERVIEW: The victims were involved in a motor vehicle accident on a state highway. The victims filed a notice of intent to file a claim against the Department. However, they did not file a claim against the Department for more than two years after the accident. The victims alleged that the highway was unsafe. The Department filed a motion for an accelerated judgment because the victims failed to file their claim within the two-year statute of limitations in Mich. Comp. Laws Ann. § 691.1411. The trial court granted the motion. The victims appealed. The court affirmed, holding that the language of § 691.1411 plainly required that the victims file their claim within two years. The court also concluded that the victims did not sustain the heavy burden to show that the two-year limitation period denied them equal protection of law. The court explained that § 691.1411 applied to each and every person who might have been injured by a defective public highway. Thus, the provision did not discriminate against any group or classification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.
